DIGITAL SAT READING & WRITING - QUESTION BANK BLUEPRINT (VERSION 3)
======================================================================

1. Information and Ideas
   
   • Central Ideas and Details
     -----------------------------------------------------------------
     [DIFFICULTY LEVEL: LOW - QUESTIONS 1-10]
     
     QUESTION 1
     Passage:
     Sunflowers are known for their bright yellow petals, but their behavior is even more remarkable. Young sunflowers exhibit heliotropism, meaning they track the movement of the sun from east to west during the day. At night, they turn back to the east to prepare for the next morning. Once the sunflowers mature, however, they stop tracking the sun and remain permanently facing east, which helps attract pollinators like bees by warming up the flowers more quickly.
     
     Prompt:
     Which choice best states the main idea of the text?
     
     Options:
     A) Sunflowers face east permanently because they no longer need nutrients from the sun.
     B) The movement of sunflowers changes as they grow, ultimately serving to attract pollinators.
     C) Bees prefer yellow flowers over any other color because they are warmer.
     D) Young sunflowers move randomly throughout the night to prepare for the morning.
     
     Correct Answer: B
     
     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice A is incorrect because the text states that sunflowers face east to warm up and attract pollinators, not because they no longer need nutrients from the sun.
     * Choice C is incorrect because the text only mentions that facing east warms the flowers to attract bees; it does not claim that bees prefer yellow over all other colors.
     * Choice D is incorrect because the text directly contradicts this, stating that young sunflowers turn specifically back to the east at night, not randomly.

     -----------------------------------------------------------------
     
     QUESTION 2
     Passage:
     Louisa May Alcott is best remembered for her novel Little Women, a story closely based on her own childhood experiences growing up with three sisters. While the book brought her immense financial success and lasting fame, Alcott initially did not want to write it. She preferred writing thriller stories under a secret pen name. She only agreed to write Little Women because her publisher promised to publish a book by her father if she complied.
     
     Prompt:
     According to the text, why did Louisa May Alcott write Little Women?
     
     Options:
     A) She wanted to share her childhood memories with a large audience.
     B) She hoped it would bring her the financial success she needed to write thrillers.
     C) She did it to secure a publishing deal for her father's work.
     D) Her father forced her to abandon her secret pen name.
     
     Correct Answer: C
     
     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice A is incorrect because the text explicitly states that Alcott initially did not want to write the book, meaning sharing her memories was not her primary motivation.
     * Choice B is incorrect because while the book did bring financial success, the text does not say she wrote it with the hope of funding her thriller writing.
     * Choice D is incorrect because the text notes she wrote it due to a promise made by her publisher regarding her father's book, not because her father forced her to give up her pen name.

     -----------------------------------------------------------------
     
     QUESTION 3
     Passage:
     Mars has long fascinated scientists because it possesses features similar to Earth, such as polar ice caps and ancient river valleys. However, Mars's atmosphere is incredibly thin, composed of over 95% carbon dioxide. This thin atmosphere cannot trap heat effectively, resulting in an average surface temperature of minus 80 degrees Fahrenheit. Consequently, despite having water ice, Mars remains an incredibly harsh environment for any potential life.
     
     Prompt:
     Which choice best states the main idea of the text?
     
     Options:
     A) Mars's thin atmosphere and cold temperatures make it a difficult place for life to exist.
     B) Scientists have proven that life once existed in Mars's ancient river valleys.
     C) Mars is exactly like Earth except for its higher percentage of carbon dioxide.
     D) The polar ice caps on Mars are rapidly melting due to the planet's thin atmosphere.
     
     Correct Answer: A
     
     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice B is incorrect because the text mentions ancient river valleys as a feature, but it never states or proves that life once existed there.
     * Choice C is incorrect because the text states Mars is only "similar" in some features, while highlighting massive differences like extreme cold and a thin atmosphere, meaning it is not "exactly like Earth."
     * Choice D is incorrect because the text mentions that Mars has polar ice caps, but it provides no data or claims suggesting that they are rapidly melting.

     -----------------------------------------------------------------
     
     QUESTION 4
     Passage:
     For centuries, the purpose of Stonehenge, a prehistoric monument in England, remained a total mystery. Recently, archaeologists discovered evidence suggesting the site functioned as an ancient solar calendar. The alignment of the massive stones perfectly tracks the winter and summer solstices. This setup allowed the people who built it to keep track of the days, weeks, and months of the year, which helped them plan vital agricultural cycles.
     
     Prompt:
     According to the text, what did archaeologists recently discover about Stonehenge?
     
     Options:
     A) It was built by farmers who migrated to England from other parts of Europe.
     B) It served as a tool for tracking time and planning farming activities.
     C) The stones have shifted position over the centuries due to weather.
     D) It was designed to block out the sun during the winter solstice.
     
     Correct Answer: B
     
     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice A is incorrect because the text does not mention where the builders migrated from; it only states that the monument helped them track agricultural cycles.
     * Choice C is incorrect because the text focuses on the alignment of the stones tracking solstices, and it never mentions the stones shifting due to weather.
     * Choice D is incorrect because the text states that the stones "perfectly track" the solstices, not that they were meant to block out the sun.

     -----------------------------------------------------------------
     
     QUESTION 5
     Passage:
     Sea otters play a crucial role in maintaining the health of coastal marine ecosystems. They feed heavily on sea urchins, which are small creatures that consume kelp. If sea otter populations decline, sea urchin populations explode and quickly destroy entire kelp forests. Because kelp forests provide food and shelter for hundreds of other marine species, the presence of sea otters is vital for protecting ocean biodiversity.
     
     Prompt:
     Which choice best states the main idea of the text?
     
     Options:
     A) Sea urchins are the most dangerous predators living in coastal kelp forests.
     B) Kelp forests are declining worldwide because of a lack of nutrients in the ocean.
     C) Protecting ocean biodiversity requires humans to feed coastal sea otters.
     D) Sea otters are essential for preserving kelp forests and the marine life that depends on them.
     
     Correct Answer: D
     
     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice A is incorrect because sea urchins are described as creatures that consume kelp, not as dangerous predators.
     * Choice B is incorrect because the text attributes kelp forest destruction to overpopulations of sea urchins when sea otters decline, not to a worldwide lack of nutrients.
     * Choice C is incorrect because the text focuses on the natural predator-prey relationship between sea otters and urchins, making no mention of human intervention.

     -----------------------------------------------------------------
     
     QUESTION 6
     Passage:
     In the early 20th century, the Harlem Renaissance marked a major turning point for African American culture. Centered in New York City, this vibrant movement saw an explosion of literature, music, and visual art created by Black artists. Figures like Langston Hughes and Duke Ellington gained widespread recognition, challenging racial stereotypes and deeply shaping mainstream American culture for decades to come.
     
     Prompt:
     Which choice best summarizes the main idea of the text?
     
     Options:
     A) The Harlem Renaissance was a cultural movement that showcased Black artistry and influenced broader American culture.
     B) Langston Hughes and Duke Ellington were the only successful artists of the Harlem Renaissance.
     C) The movement was unsuccessful because it remained confined entirely within New York City.
     D) Visual art was more influential than music during the early 20th century.
     
     Correct Answer: A
     
     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice B is incorrect because the text introduces Hughes and Ellington as examples ("Figures like..."), implying there were many other artists.
     * Choice C is incorrect because the text says it "deeply shaped mainstream American culture for decades," directly contradicting the idea that it was unsuccessful.
     * Choice D is incorrect because the text lists literature, music, and visual art together without ranking one as more influential than the other.

     -----------------------------------------------------------------
     
     QUESTION 7
     Passage:
     Modern smartphones rely on lithium-ion batteries because they are lightweight and can hold a charge for a long time. However, these batteries degrade over time as they go through repeated charging cycles. Exposure to extreme heat can accelerate this damage, causing the battery to lose its capacity even faster. To extend a phone's battery lifespan, experts recommend keeping the device out of hot environments and avoiding letting the charge drop to zero percent.
     
     Prompt:
     Based on the text, what is one factor that can cause a smartphone battery to degrade more quickly?
     
     Options:
     A) Using the phone while it is plugged into a charger.
     B) Exposing the smartphone to very high temperatures.
     C) Keeping the phone's battery charged at exactly fifty percent.
     D) Manufacturing the battery with lightweight lithium materials.
     
     Correct Answer: B
     
     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice A is incorrect because the text does not mention using the phone while it is charging as a factor in battery degradation.
     * Choice C is incorrect because the text mentions avoiding letting the charge drop to zero percent, but it never mentions keeping it at exactly fifty percent.
     * Choice D is incorrect because the text states that lightweight lithium materials are a benefit that makes smartphones rely on them, not a cause of rapid degradation.

     -----------------------------------------------------------------
     
     QUESTION 8
     Passage:
     Deep-sea hydrothermal vents are fissures on the ocean floor that release superheated water rich in minerals. Although these vents exist in complete darkness under immense pressure, they support thriving ecosystems. Instead of using sunlight for energy like plants do, the bacteria living near these vents use a process called chemosynthesis, converting the vents' chemical minerals into food. This allows an entire food web of crabs, clams, and tubeworms to survive without any sunlight.
     
     Prompt:
     According to the text, how do bacteria near hydrothermal vents produce food?
     
     Options:
     A) By converting sunlight into chemical energy through photosynthesis.
     B) By feeding on small crabs and clams that live on the ocean floor.
     C) By using minerals from superheated water in a process called chemosynthesis.
     D) By absorbing nutrients from decaying plants falling from the ocean surface.
     
     Correct Answer: C
     
     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice A is incorrect because the text explicitly states the vents exist in complete darkness and that bacteria produce food "instead of using sunlight."
     * Choice B is incorrect because bacteria form the base of the food web by converting minerals; the crabs and clams depend on the bacteria.
     * Choice D is incorrect because the text states that bacteria use the chemical minerals directly from the vents, making no mention of falling plants.

     -----------------------------------------------------------------
     
     QUESTION 9
     Passage:
     Before the invention of the printing press by Johannes Gutenberg in the 1440s, books had to be copied entirely by hand. This tedious process meant that books were rare, expensive, and accessible only to the wealthy and educated elite. Gutenberg's press allowed for the mass production of texts for the first time. As a result, books became significantly cheaper, literacy rates soared across Europe, and information spread faster than ever before.
     
     Prompt:
     Which choice best states the main idea of the text?
     
     Options:
     A) Gutenberg invented the printing press to help wealthy elites control information.
     B) The printing press made books affordable and widely available, which transformed European society.
     C) Literacy rates in Europe were high even before the invention of the printing press.
     D) Hand-copying books was a preferred method because it produced higher quality texts.
     
     Correct Answer: B
     
     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice A is incorrect because the printing press expanded information access to the wider public, undermining exclusive elite control.
     * Choice C is incorrect because the text points out that books were initially accessible only to elites and that literacy rates "soared" only after the press was invented.
     * Choice D is incorrect because the text describes hand-copying as a "tedious process," never stating it was preferred or superior in quality.

     -----------------------------------------------------------------
     
     QUESTION 10
     Passage:
     Honeybees use an extraordinary form of communication known as the "waggle dance." When a forager bee discovers a rich source of nectar, it returns to the hive and performs a series of movements in a figure-eight pattern. The angle and duration of the dance tell the other bees exactly which direction to fly and how far to travel to find the food. This cooperative behavior allows the hive to collect resources efficiently.
     
     Prompt:
     According to the text, what is the primary purpose of the honeybee's "waggle dance"?
     
     Options:
     A) To defend the hive against predators and rival insect colonies.
     B) To signal to other bees that a new queen bee has been born.
     C) To communicate the specific location of a food source to other hive members.
     D) To warm up the hive during cold winter months through movement.
     
     Correct Answer: C
     
     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice A is incorrect because the text links the dance entirely to resource collection, not hive defense.
     * Choice B is incorrect because the text mentions the dance is performed when a bee discovers nectar, making no mention of queen bee births.
     * Choice D is incorrect because the purpose is explicitly to show direction and distance to food, not to generate structural heat.

     -----------------------------------------------------------------
     [DIFFICULTY LEVEL: MEDIUM-LOW - QUESTIONS 11-20]
     
     QUESTION 11
     Passage:
     Beneath the forest floor, a complex network of fungal filaments known as mycorrhizae connects the roots of different trees. This symbiotic system allows trees to share vital resources, such as carbon, water, and nutrients. Healthy, mature trees can channel excess sugars to younger saplings that are struggling to survive in the shade of the canopy. Additionally, if a tree is attacked by pests, it can transmit warning chemicals through the network, prompting neighboring trees to elevate their defenses.
     
     Prompt:
     Which choice best states the main idea of the text?
     
     Options:
     A) Mycorrhizal fungal networks act as an active underground pathway through which trees cooperate and share critical information.
     B) Mature trees dominate mycorrhizal networks to prevent younger saplings from accessing resources.
     C) Pests are highly destructive to forests because they break down the fungal filaments that connect trees.
     D) Fungal networks are unique because they can survive independently without relying on host trees.
     
     Correct Answer: A
     
     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice B is incorrect because the text states that mature trees use the network to help younger saplings survive by sharing excess sugars, not to dominate or restrict them.
     * Choice C is incorrect because the text suggests that pests trigger warning signals through the network; it does not say that pests break down or destroy the fungal filaments.
     * Choice D is incorrect because the text emphasizes a symbiotic system where the networks connect the roots of living trees, never stating that fungi survive independently of them.

     -----------------------------------------------------------------
     
     QUESTION 12
     Passage:
     Author and anthropologist Zora Neale Hurston is celebrated today for her contributions to African American literature, particularly her 1937 novel Their Eyes Were Watching God. However, Hurston was also a dedicated folklorist who spent years collecting oral histories, songs, and traditions in the American South and the Caribbean. While her fictional work received widespread attention, her documentary ethnographic research provided an essential, authentic record of Black rural life that heavily informed her creative writing and enriched American anthropology.
     
     Prompt:
     According to the text, what is true about Zora Neale Hurston's ethnographic research?
     
     Options:
     A) It was highly controversial among other anthropologists during her lifetime.
     B) It was neglected by Hurston after the publication of her most famous novel.
     C) It provided a valuable documentation of Black rural culture that influenced her fiction.
     D) It focused primarily on collecting European folktales that had spread to the Caribbean.
     
     Correct Answer: C
     
     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice A is incorrect because the text does not mention whether her anthropological work was controversial among her peers.
     * Choice B is incorrect because the text notes that her ethnographic research heavily informed her creative writing, not that she neglected it after publishing her novel.
     * Choice D is incorrect because the text explicitly states that her research provided an authentic record of "Black rural life" and traditions in the American South and Caribbean, not European folktales.

     -----------------------------------------------------------------
     
     QUESTION 13
     Passage:
     During the Song Dynasty in 11th-century China, the booming iron and silk industries created a massive demand for currency. Carrying thousands of heavy iron and copper coins along trade routes proved highly impractical and dangerous for merchants. To solve this dilemma, private shops began issuing paper receipts as promises of payment. Recognizing the immense efficiency of this system, the Song government soon took exclusive control of the practice, issuing the world's first official government-backed paper banknotes, known as Jiaozi.
     
     Prompt:
     Which choice best states the main idea of the text?
     
     Options:
     A) The Song government banned iron and copper coins to prevent merchants from becoming too wealthy.
     B) Paper money was invented by the Song government to replace an entirely failed trade network.
     C) In response to the impracticality of heavy metal coins, paper currency emerged and was eventually adopted by the state.
     D) Private shops in China became more powerful than the Song government by controlling paper receipts.
     
     Correct Answer: C
     
     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice A is incorrect because the text states metal coins were impractical and dangerous to carry due to weight, not that they were banned to suppress merchants' wealth.
     * Choice B is incorrect because paper money initially began as private receipts from shops, not as an invention by the government to rescue a failed trade network.
     * Choice D is incorrect because the text shows that the government "took exclusive control of the practice," demonstrating that the state retained ultimate authority over the currency.

     -----------------------------------------------------------------
     
     QUESTION 14
     Passage:
     Astronomers search for exoplanets—planets outside our solar system—primarily by using the transit method. When an exoplanet passes directly between its host star and Earth, it temporarily blocks a tiny fraction of the star's light. By monitoring these predictable, periodic dips in starlight, scientists can not only confirm the existence of a planet but also estimate its orbital period and physical size. Although this technique requires highly sensitive telescopes, it has led to the discovery of thousands of alien worlds.
     
     Prompt:
     Which choice best summarizes the primary function of the transit method as described in the text?
     
     Options:
     A) It allows astronomers to measure the temperature and chemical composition of an exoplanet's atmosphere.
     B) It detects exoplanets by tracking regular drops in a star's brightness caused by a passing planet.
     C) It helps scientists observe exoplanets directly without the use of specialized telescopes.
     D) It calculates when an exoplanet will collide with its host star.
     
     Correct Answer: B
     
     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice A is incorrect because the text states the method helps estimate orbital periods and physical sizes, making no mention of atmospheric temperature or chemical composition.
     * Choice C is incorrect because the text states that this technique explicitly "requires highly sensitive telescopes," contradicting the idea that it can be done without them.
     * Choice D is incorrect because the method monitors planets passing in front of a star, not impending orbital collisions.

     -----------------------------------------------------------------
     
     QUESTION 15
     Passage:
     Founded in Germany in 1919 by architect Walter Gropius, the Bauhaus school revolutionized modern design. Gropius believed that fine art, craft, and technology should be integrated rather than treated as separate fields. The Bauhaus philosophy emphasized functionalism: the idea that the design of an object or building should be stripped of unnecessary ornamentation and dictated entirely by its practical use. This approach created a sleek, minimalist aesthetic that fundamentally altered corporate and residential architecture throughout the twentieth century.
     
     Prompt:
     Which choice best states the main idea of the text?
     
     Options:
     A) Walter Gropius established the Bauhaus school to prove that technology was superior to traditional fine art.
     B) The Bauhaus school introduced a functional, minimalist philosophy that unified multiple disciplines and shaped modern architecture.
     C) Twentieth-century residential buildings were highly ornate until the Bauhaus school banned handcrafts.
     D) The Bauhaus aesthetic was widely rejected because it ignored the practical functions of everyday objects.
     
     Correct Answer: B
     
     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice A is incorrect because Gropius believed these disciplines should be integrated and unified, not that technology was superior to fine art.
     * Choice C is incorrect because the text states that Bauhaus integrated craft rather than banning it, and it does not state that all prior housing was highly ornate.
     * Choice D is incorrect because the text explicitly states the aesthetic fundamentally altered architecture and emphasized practical use, meaning it was influential and prioritized functionality.

     -----------------------------------------------------------------
     
     QUESTION 16
     Passage:
     Cephalopods, such as octopuses and cuttlefish, possess an unmatched ability to alter their appearance instantly. Their skin contains specialized cells called chromatophores, which are surrounded by tiny muscles. By contracting or relaxing these muscles, cephalopods can expand or shrink individual color sacs, changing their skin patterns to match their surroundings perfectly. This dynamic camouflage serves two essential purposes: it allows these soft-bodied creatures to hide from sharp-eyed predators and enables them to ambush unsuspecting prey.
     
     Prompt:
     According to the text, how do chromatophores enable cephalopods to change color?
     
     Options:
     A) They absorb chemical signals from predators and automatically shift colors.
     B) They rely on surrounding muscles to change the size of color-containing sacs in the skin.
     C) They shed the outer layer of their skin to reveal brighter, more colorful layers beneath.
     D) They capture ambient light from the environment and reflect it back like a mirror.
     
     Correct Answer: B
     
     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice A is incorrect because muscle contractions and relaxations drive the movement, not automatic chemical absorption from predators.
     * Choice C is incorrect because the text states color changes happen instantly via chromatophores and muscles, not through shedding skin.
     * Choice D is incorrect because the mechanism involves manipulating color sacs within specialized cells, not mirroring or reflecting ambient light.

     -----------------------------------------------------------------
     
     QUESTION 17
     Passage:
     Completed in 1825, the Erie Canal connected the Hudson River in New York to Lake Erie, creating an unprecedented water highway between the Atlantic Ocean and the Great Lakes. Before its construction, transporting agricultural goods from the Midwest to eastern ports was incredibly expensive and took weeks. The canal reduced shipping costs by nearly ninety percent and cut travel time dramatically. This infrastructure breakthrough turned New York City into a dominant global commercial hub and accelerated westward expansion.
     
     Prompt:
     Which choice best states the main idea of the text?
     
     Options:
     A) The Erie Canal failed to benefit Midwestern farmers because shipping routes remained too slow.
     B) Transporting goods by water was dangerous before the Erie Canal provided a safe alternative.
     C) The Erie Canal dramatically lowered shipping costs and times, transforming trade and American economic geography.
     D) New York City was already a dominant commercial hub before the construction of the Erie Canal.
     
     Correct Answer: C
     
     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice A is incorrect because the text directly states that the canal cut travel times dramatically and assisted in transporting goods from the Midwest.
     * Choice B is incorrect because the passage focuses on the expense and time of shipping, never mentioning safety or danger.
     * Choice D is incorrect because the text explicitly states that the canal "turned New York City into a dominant global commercial hub," meaning it caused or accelerated this status.

     -----------------------------------------------------------------
     
     QUESTION 18
     Passage:
     In her short stories, author Jhumpa Lahiri frequently explores the nuanced experiences of Indian immigrants adapting to life in the United States. Lahiri rarely relies on dramatic plot twists; instead, she focuses on quiet, domestic details—such as the preparation of traditional meals or subtle shifts in family dialogue. By highlighting these mundane moments, Lahiri effectively captures the internal friction between holding onto one's cultural heritage and trying to assimilate into a new society.
     
     Prompt:
     Which choice best summarizes the main idea of the text?
     
     Options:
     A) Lahiri's stories use dramatic plot developments to criticize immigrants who abandon their native traditions.
     B) Lahiri emphasizes everyday domestic details to depict the internal cultural conflicts faced by Indian immigrants.
     C) Traditional cooking techniques are the primary subject matter of Lahiri's anthropological essays.
     D) Lahiri argues that it is impossible for immigrants to balance their heritage with American societal norms.
     
     Correct Answer: B
     
     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice A is incorrect because the text states that Lahiri "rarely relies on dramatic plot twists" and focuses on quiet details instead.
     * Choice C is incorrect because the text refers to her fictional "short stories," not anthropological essays, and cooking is just one example of the details she uses.
     * Choice D is incorrect because the text states she captures the "internal friction" of balancing these elements, not that doing so is entirely impossible.

     -----------------------------------------------------------------
     
     QUESTION 19
     Passage:
     Graphene, a material composed of a single layer of carbon atoms arranged in a two-dimensional honeycomb lattice, has captured the attention of materials scientists worldwide. Despite being only one atom thick, graphene is roughly two hundred times stronger than steel. Furthermore, its unique molecular structure allows electrons to move through it with minimal resistance, making it an exceptionally efficient conductor of electricity and heat. These extraordinary properties suggest that graphene could revolutionize fields from flexible electronics to advanced medical devices.
     
     Prompt:
     Based on the text, what makes graphene an exceptional conductor of electricity?
     
     Options:
     A) Its ability to transform carbon atoms into metallic steel under extreme pressure.
     B) Its high flexibility, which allows it to stretch into three-dimensional shapes.
     C) Its distinct molecular structure that allows electrons to travel with very little resistance.
     D) Its density, which prevents heat from escaping during electrical transmission.
     
     Correct Answer: C
     
     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice A is incorrect because the text states graphene is stronger than steel, not that it transforms carbon into steel under pressure.
     * Choice B is incorrect because while flexible electronics are mentioned as a potential application, flexibility is not cited as the reason for its electrical conductivity.
     * Choice D is incorrect because the text notes that electrons encounter "minimal resistance," not that its density captures heat.

     -----------------------------------------------------------------
     
     QUESTION 20
     Passage:
     In behavioral economics, "loss aversion" describes the tendency for people to strongly prefer avoiding losses over acquiring equivalent gains. Pioneered by psychologists Daniel Kahneman and Amos Tversky, studies reveal that the psychological pain of losing one hundred dollars is roughly twice as intense as the pleasure of gaining that same amount. This cognitive bias heavily influences financial decision-making, often leading individuals to make overly conservative investments or avoid rational risks out of an unbalanced fear of negative outcomes.
     
     Prompt:
     Which choice best states the main idea of the text?
     
     Options:
     A) Loss aversion is a psychological phenomenon where the desire to avoid losses outweighs the appeal of gains, altering rational economic choices.
     B) Daniel Kahneman and Amos Tversky proved that losing money causes physical pain in investors.
     C) Conservative investments are always safer and more profitable due to human cognitive biases.
     D) People can eliminate loss aversion by calculating the exact mathematical probability of financial risks.
     
     Correct Answer: A
     
     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice B is incorrect because the text refers to "psychological pain," not physical pain.
     * Choice C is incorrect because the text states loss aversion leads people to make "overly conservative" choices out of fear, implying it might be irrational or counterproductive rather than always profitable.
     * Choice D is incorrect because the text never discusses ways to eliminate loss aversion or mentions probability calculations.

     [DIFFICULTY LEVEL: MEDIUM-HIGH - QUESTIONS 21-30]
     
     QUESTION 21
     Passage:
     In 1874, a group of avant-garde artists in Paris bypassed the official, state-sanctioned Salon exhibition to host an independent showcase, introducing what would become known as Impressionism. Painters like Claude Monet and Camille Pissarro abandoned the smooth brushwork and historical grandiosity demanded by the French Academy of Fine Arts. Instead, they favored visible, rapid strokes and transient effects of light, often painting outdoors ("en plein air") to capture immediate sensory impressions. While contemporary critics initially dismissed their work as sloppy and unfinished, this deliberate departure from academic orthodoxy re-oriented the trajectory of Western art, prioritizing subjective perception over photographic accuracy.
     
     Prompt:
     Which choice best states the main idea of the text?
     
     Options:
     A) Impressionism was initially developed as a way to help academic painters achieve more photographic accuracy when working outdoors.
     B) By rejecting strict academic standards and prioritizing immediate sensory experiences, the Impressionists fundamentally transformed Western art.
     C) The French Academy of Fine Arts eventually shut down independent exhibitions because critics found the brushwork unfinished.
     D) Monet and Pissarro focused exclusively on painting outdoor light because they lacked training in traditional historical grandiosity.
     
     Correct Answer: B
     
     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice A is incorrect because the text explicitly states Impressionism departed from academic orthodoxy and prioritized subjective perception *over* photographic accuracy.
     * Choice C is incorrect because the text mentions that critics dismissed the work, but it never claims the French Academy shut down the independent exhibitions.
     * Choice D is incorrect because the text attributes their style to a "deliberate departure" and artistic choice, not a lack of training or technical capability.

     -----------------------------------------------------------------
     
     QUESTION 22
     Passage:
     In evolutionary biology, the concept of a "spandrel"—borrowed from architecture—refers to a biological trait that arises as an incidental byproduct of other adaptations rather than as a direct result of natural selection for a specific function. Biologists Stephen Jay Gould and Richard Lewontin argued that researchers frequently err by fabricating adaptive narratives for every physiological feature. For instance, the human chin is likely not an engineered adaptation for chewing or speech, but rather a structural byproduct resulting from the evolutionary recession of the surrounding facial bones. Understanding spandrels cautions scientists against assuming that every complex biological trait must possess its own unique evolutionary utility.
     
     Prompt:
     Which choice best states the main idea of the text?
     
     Options:
     A) Biological traits known as spandrels demonstrate that natural selection is an ineffective mechanism for evolutionary change.
     B) Researchers should analyze every physical feature as a direct adaptation designed to solve an environmental problem.
     C) The human chin evolved specifically to enhance speech capabilities as facial bones receded over generations.
     D) Certain biological traits exist merely as structural byproducts of other evolutionary changes rather than as distinct, functional adaptations.
     
     Correct Answer: D
     
     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice A is incorrect because the text doesn't argue that natural selection is ineffective; rather, it argues that some traits are byproducts of adaptations that *were* selected.
     * Choice B is incorrect because the text directly opposes this idea, stating that researchers "frequently err" by fabricating adaptive narratives for every single feature.
     * Choice C is incorrect because the text uses the human chin as an example of a structural byproduct, explicitly stating it is "likely not" an adaptation for speech.

     -----------------------------------------------------------------
     
     QUESTION 23
     Passage:
     Historians examining the French Revolution have traditionally concentrated on male-dominated political clubs, yet recent scholarship has illuminated the vital role played by women within the printing trade. Operating behind the scenes as printshop managers, compositors, and underground distributors, women were crucial in disseminating radical pamphlets and political treatises. Because female printers often inherited operations upon a husband’s or father’s death, they exploited their legal standing to sustain press operations when male counterparts were imprisoned by state censors. Thus, the ideological mechanics of the Revolution relied heavily on a female network that sustained the print apparatus under intense political pressure.
     
     Prompt:
     Which choice best states the main idea of the text?
     
     Options:
     A) Women printers during the French Revolution used their positions to advocate exclusively for female inheritance laws.
     B) Radical political pamphlets were written almost entirely by women who managed underground printshops.
     C) The preservation and dissemination of revolutionary ideology depended significantly on the operations of women in the printing industry.
     D) Male political clubs intentionally suppressed the contributions of female printshop managers to maintain control over the press.
     
     Correct Answer: C
     
     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice A is incorrect because the text states women used their legal standing to "sustain press operations," not to advocate exclusively for inheritance laws.
     * Choice B is incorrect because the passage focuses on women *disseminating* and *sustaining the apparatus* of print, not necessarily being the primary authors of the political pamphlets.
     * Choice C is the best answer because it captures the main thesis: the ideological mechanics relied heavily on this female printing network.
     * Choice D is incorrect because the text doesn't claim that male political clubs intentionally suppressed or attacked women printers; it only states that historians have traditionally focused on those male clubs.

     QUESTION 24
     Passage:
     The classic mantle plume hypothesis posits that localized hotspots of volcanic activity, such as those forming the Hawaiian Islands, are fed by narrow streams of abnormally hot rock rising from deep within Earth's mantle. However, this model has faced scrutiny from geophysicists who point out anomalies that the classic theory fails to explain. For example, some hotspot tracks exhibit irregular volcanic progressions or lack the expected thermal signatures at their base. In response, alternative paradigms suggest that upper-mantle processes, such as tectonic plate stretching and shallow cracks, can create volcanism without requiring deep-seated thermal plumes, revealing that intraplate volcanism may be driven by multiple, distinct geodynamic mechanisms.
     
     Prompt:
     Which choice best states the main idea of the text?
     
     Options:
     A) The classic mantle plume hypothesis has been entirely disproven by modern thermal signatures under the Hawaiian Islands.
     B) Deficiencies in the classic mantle plume model have led scientists to consider alternative upper-mantle mechanisms for intraplate volcanism.
     C) Volcanic activity at tectonic plate boundaries is much easier to predict than localized hotspot volcanism.
     D) Shallow mantle cracks are the sole cause of irregular volcanic progressions across the globe.
     
     Correct Answer: B
     
     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice A is incorrect because the text states the model has faced "scrutiny" due to anomalies, not that it has been entirely disproven or abandoned.
     * Choice C is incorrect because the text compares different theories explaining intraplate volcanism; it does not discuss the predictability of volcanism at plate boundaries.
     * Choice D is incorrect because the text offers shallow cracks as part of "alternative paradigms" that suggest volcanism can be driven by "multiple, distinct" mechanisms, not a single sole cause.

     QUESTION 25
     Passage:
     In her seminal 1924 essay "Mr. Bennett and Mrs. Brown," Virginia Woolf launched a critique against Edwardian realists like Arnold Bennett, arguing that their obsessive focus on external, material details—such as property, income, and social status—failed to capture the essence of human character. Woolf asserted that true reality resides within the fluid, internal consciousness of an individual. She advocated for a modernist narrative technique that abandoned rigid chronological plots in favor of capturing the fragmented, subjective impressions of the mind. For Woolf, a novel’s success depended not on recording societal architecture, but on rendering the elusive, interior life of its subjects.
     
     Prompt:
     Which choice best summarizes Virginia Woolf's perspective on the novel as discussed in the text?
     
     Options:
     A) A novel should prioritize the exploration of internal consciousness and subjective impressions over the meticulous depiction of external social facts.
     B) Realist novels are superior because they provide an accurate historical record of Edwardian societal architecture.
     C) Modernist literature should use rigid chronological structures to clarify the confusing nature of human thoughts.
     D) Literature can only be successful if it completely avoids addressing the concepts of property and social status.
     
     Correct Answer: A
     
     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice B is incorrect because Woolf critiques realist novels, arguing they fail to capture the actual essence of human character.
     * Choice C is incorrect because Woolf explicitly advocated for abandoning rigid chronological plots in favor of fragmented, subjective impressions.
     * Choice D is incorrect because while Woolf argued that an *obsessive focus* on material details was a flaw, the text does not say she believed novels must completely avoid these concepts entirely.

     QUESTION 26
     Passage:
     Metacognition—frequently defined as "thinking about thinking"—refers to an individual's awareness and management of their own cognitive processes. In educational psychology, studies demonstrate that students with highly developed metacognitive skills outperform their peers regardless of baseline intellectual measures. These students do not simply memorize information; instead, they continually monitor their understanding, evaluate the efficacy of their study strategies, and deliberately adjust their methods when encountering difficulties. Consequently, fostering metacognitive awareness may be a more critical intervention for academic success than merely expanding a student's factual knowledge base.

     A) Metacognition is an automatic cognitive trait that cannot be changed or developed through educational interventions.
     B) Students who possess vast factual knowledge automatically develop superior metacognitive monitoring strategies.
     C) Actively monitoring and managing one's learning processes through metacognition is a powerful driver of academic achievement.

     * Choice B is incorrect because the text contrasts metacognition with factual knowledge and baseline intellect, stating metacognitive skills boost performance *regardless* of those factors.
     * Choice D is incorrect because the final sentence explicitly suggests that fostering metacognition may be *more* critical than merely expanding a factual knowledge base.

     QUESTION 27
     Passage:
     For decades, the prevailing scientific consensus maintained that the adult human brain was structurally static, incapable of generating new neurons. However, the discovery of adult neurogenesis—specifically within the dentate gyrus of the hippocampus—shattered this dogma. Research reveals that environmental enrichment, physical exercise, and cognitive challenges stimulate the production and integration of these mature new cells. Conversely, chronic stress and sleep deprivation significantly suppress neurogenesis, potentially accelerating cognitive decline. This dynamic plasticity indicates that the structural integrity of the adult brain is continuously modulated by lifestyle factors and environmental interactions.
     
     Prompt:
     Which choice best states the main idea of the text?
     
     Options:
     A) The discovery of adult neurogenesis proved that the brain's structure is fixed from birth and unaffected by chronic stress.
     B) Physical exercise is the only lifestyle factor capable of preventing the degeneration of the dentate gyrus.
     C) Modern neuroscience has confirmed that the adult human brain undergoes continuous structural modification influenced by external and lifestyle inputs.
     D) Chronic stress completely eliminates the human brain's capacity to process cognitive challenges by destroying the hippocampus.
     
     Correct Answer: C
     
     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice A is incorrect because adult neurogenesis directly shatters the dogma that the brain's structure is fixed, and the text shows stress *does* affect it.
     * Choice B is incorrect because the text lists environmental enrichment and cognitive challenges alongside physical exercise, meaning exercise is not the *only* factor.
     * Choice D is incorrect because while chronic stress *suppresses* neurogenesis, the text does not make the extreme claim that it "completely eliminates" processing capacity or "destroys" the entire hippocampus.

     QUESTION 28
     Passage:
     In his 1689 treatise An Essay Concerning Human Understanding, philosopher John Locke attacked the doctrine of innate ideas—the notion that human beings are born with pre-existing knowledge and concepts. Locke famously posited that the human mind at birth is a *tabula rasa*, or blank slate. According to his empiricist framework, all knowledge is subsequently derived from experience, entering the mind via sensory perception and internal reflection on those sensations. Locke contended that complex ideas do not emerge from an internal genetic blueprint but are constructed through the mind’s active combining of simple sensory inputs received from the external world.
     
     Prompt:
     Which choice best summarizes John Locke's argument as presented in the text?
     
     Options:
     A) Human minds are born with pre-existing complex ideas that are gradually unlocked by physical experiences.
     B) The human mind begins as a blank slate, and all knowledge is constructed out of subsequent sensory and reflective experiences.
     C) Sensory perception is unreliable because the external world is constantly shifting its structural inputs.
     D) Genetic blueprints determine how the mind combines pre-existing innate concepts into complex ideas.
     
     Correct Answer: B
     
     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice A is incorrect because Locke explicitly attacked the doctrine of pre-existing innate ideas, arguing against them.
     * Choice C is incorrect because the text does not mention Locke viewing sensory perception as unreliable or stating that the external world is problematically unstable.
     * Choice D is incorrect because Locke rejected the idea of genetic or internal blueprints for concepts, stating knowledge is derived from experience instead.

     QUESTION 29
     Passage:
     As global temperatures rise, Arctic permafrost—permanently frozen soil that blankets polar regions—is thawing at an unprecedented rate. This thaw creates a perilous positive feedback loop: permafrost contains vast reservoirs of organic matter, consisting of ancient dead plants and animals. When the soil warms, microbes decompose this organic material, releasing enormous volumes of methane and carbon dioxide into the atmosphere. These greenhouse gases trap additional solar radiation, further accelerating global warming and inducing even more permafrost to melt. This self-reinforcing cycle amplifies the localized impacts of Arctic warming into a global climatic threat.
     
     Prompt:
     Which choice best explains the "positive feedback loop" described in the text?
     
     Options:
     A) Rising temperatures melt permafrost, which releases gases that trap more heat and cause further melting.
     B) Decomposing microbes consume greenhouse gases, which cools the Arctic and slows permafrost decay.
     C) The growth of polar plants absorbs methane, neutralizing the negative effects of permafrost thaw.
     D) Solar radiation directly destroys organic matter in the permafrost, preventing gases from escaping into the atmosphere.
     
     Correct Answer: A
     
     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice B is incorrect because the text states that microbes *release* greenhouse gases rather than consuming them, and this warms rather than cools the region.
     * Choice C is incorrect because the text describes a self-reinforcing warming threat; it does not mention plants absorbing methane or neutralizing the thaw.
     * Choice D is incorrect because the text states that *microbes* decompose the material when soil warms, not that solar radiation directly destroys it to prevent gas escape.

     QUESTION 30
     Passage:
     Classical scholarship often characterized the ancient Roman economy as a localized, agrarian system focused primarily on Mediterranean trade. However, recent archaeological excavations at ports along the Red Sea coast have revealed a sophisticated, long-distance maritime network connecting Rome with the Indian subcontinent. Artifacts such as Roman pottery, coins, and glass beads found in India—matched by Indian pepper, silk, and teakwood discovered in Egyptian Roman ports—demonstrate a robust commercial exchange. This evidence forces historians to revise previous assumptions, showing that the Roman economic apparatus was deeply integrated into a globalizing network of Eurasian commerce.
     
     Prompt:
     Which choice best states the main idea of the text?
     
     Options:
     A) New archaeological discoveries prove that the ancient Roman economy was entirely dependent on Indian silk and teakwood.
     B) Traditional historical scholarship was correct in characterizing the Roman economy as purely agrarian and localized.
     C) Trade along the Red Sea coast was limited exclusively to the exchange of pottery and glass beads.
     D) Recent evidence reveals that the Roman economy engaged in extensive long-distance maritime commerce with India, altering historical consensus.
     
     Correct Answer: D
     
     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice A is incorrect because the text states the economy was "deeply integrated," which is a nuanced claim, not that it was "entirely dependent" on these specific items.
     * Choice B is incorrect because the text directly states that the discoveries force historians to *revise* traditional assumptions, meaning the previous localized characterization was incomplete or flawed.
     * Choice C is incorrect because the text lists many other items (pepper, silk, teakwood) and describes it as a "sophisticated, long-distance maritime network," not a limited exchange.

     QUESTION 31
     Passage:
     The following text is adapted from George Eliot’s 1871 novel Middlemarch.
     Dorothea Brooke’s mind was vibrant, but her energy was trapped within the narrow avenues of her social environment. She yearned for a grand life purpose, envisioning herself assisting a great intellect in sorting through the historical wreckage of human belief. Yet, her marriage to the aging scholar Edward Casaubon quickly transformed this romantic idealism into a claustrophobic reality. Casaubon’s much-vaunted intellectual project, a comprehensive mythological synthesis, was not a soaring cathedral of thought but a sprawling labyrinth of trivialities. Dorothea discovered, to her profound dismay, that his mind was a dark room filled with old files, incapable of illuminated thought, leaving her to mourn not the failure of her devotion, but the tragic insignificance of the idol she had chosen to serve.
     
     Prompt:
     Which choice best states the central idea of the text?
     
     Options:
     A) Dorothea’s disillusionment stems from realizing that her husband’s intellectual pursuit is a trivial, unilluminated endeavor rather than a grand, transformative work.
     B) Dorothea regrets her marriage because Casaubon explicitly prevents her from publishing her own historical and mythological research.
     C) Casaubon’s failure to complete his comprehensive architectural synthesis is the primary source of conflict between him and Dorothea.
     D) Dorothea’s vibrant energy allows her to transcend the dark, claustrophobic reality of her domestic life and find a new purpose.
     
     Correct Answer: A
     
     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice B is incorrect because the passage never states that Casaubon prevented Dorothea from publishing her own research; her distress comes from his lack of true intellectual depth.
     * Choice C is incorrect because the conflict arises from the *nature* of his mind and project (a "labyrinth of trivialities"), not because he simply failed to complete it chronologically.
     * Choice D is incorrect because the text emphasizes that she is left in a state of profound dismay and mourning over his insignificance, meaning she does not transcend this reality within the text.

     QUESTION 32
     Passage:
     Quantum computing promises to solve computational problems that are entirely intractable for classical silicon architectures by exploiting the principles of superposition and entanglement. However, the engineering reality is constrained by quantum decoherence—the process by which quantum bits, or qubits, lose their delicate quantum states due to environmental interactions like thermal fluctuations or electromagnetic interference. Researchers are developing quantum error correction (QEC) protocols to counter this vulnerability, which use networks of entangled physical qubits to safeguard a single unit of logical information. Nonetheless, the massive physical overhead required—frequently thousands of physical qubits just to sustain one error-free logical qubit—means that scaling these systems poses a profound physical and architectural challenge that tempers immediate commercial timelines.
     
     Prompt:
     Which choice best states the main idea of the text?
     
     Options:
     A) Quantum error correction protocols have eliminated the physical overhead that previously prevented quantum computers from outperforming classical silicon systems.
     B) While quantum computing offers unmatched theoretical processing capabilities, the extreme vulnerability of qubits to environmental interference creates scaling challenges that complicate its near-term realization.
     C) Environmental interactions such as electromagnetic interference can be completely blocked by shielding individual physical qubits within classical silicon architectures.
     D) The commercial timeline for quantum computing is delayed because researchers are unable to establish entanglement across multiple logical qubits.
     
     Correct Answer: B
     
     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice A is incorrect because QEC protocols have *not* eliminated overhead; rather, they require a "massive physical overhead" that complicates scaling.
     * Choice C is incorrect because the text suggests using error correction protocols to *safeguard* information, not that interference can be "completely blocked" via classical silicon shielding.
     * Choice D is incorrect because the text notes that establishing entanglement *is* part of the QEC strategy, but the problem is the *overhead and scaling constraints* of physical qubits, not an inability to entangle them.

     QUESTION 33
     Passage:
     The following text is adapted from James Madison’s 1787 essay Federalist No. 10.
     The latent causes of faction are thus sown in the nature of man; and we see them everywhere brought into different degrees of activity, according to the different circumstances of civil society. A zeal for different opinions concerning religion, concerning government, and many other points... have, in turn, divided mankind into parties, inflamed them with mutual animosity, and rendered them much more disposed to vex and oppress each other than to co-operate for their common good. So strong is this propensity of mankind to fall into mutual animosities, that where no substantial occasion presents itself, the most frivolous and fanciful distinctions have been sufficient to kindle their unfriendly passions and excite their most violent conflicts. But the most common and durable source of factions has been the various and unequal distribution of property.
     
     Prompt:
     Which choice best states the main idea of the text?
     
     Options:
     A) Factions emerge primarily because citizens lack a common religious and political framework, which can be remedied through civil education.
     B) Human nature is inherently inclined toward division and conflict over various distinctions, with economic disparities serving as the most persistent catalyst for these factions.
     C) Frivolous and fanciful distinctions are the most durable and violent sources of societal conflict across civil societies.
     D) Civil society can completely eliminate the violent propensity for factions by distributing property equally among all citizens.
     
     Correct Answer: B
     
     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice A is incorrect because the text characterizes factions as "sown in the nature of man," and it never suggests that civil education can remedy or erase this inherent trait.
     * Choice C is incorrect because while the text notes that frivolous distinctions are *sufficient* to ignite conflict when no other cause exists, it explicitly states that the "most common and durable source" is the unequal distribution of property.
     * Choice D is incorrect because Madison identifies unequal property as the most common source, but he treats the tendency to form factions as an unalterable facet of human nature, never claiming civil society can completely eliminate it through redistribution.

     QUESTION 34
     Passage:
     Proponents of transgenerational epigenetic inheritance argue that environmental stressors, such as famine or psychological trauma, can induce chemical modifications to DNA—like methylation—that alter gene expression across multiple subsequent generations without changing the underlying genetic sequence. This provocative hypothesis challenges classical neo-Darwinian paradigms by reintroducing a pseudo-Lamarckian mechanism of acquired characteristics. However, skeptical evolutionary biologists point out a critical mechanistic barrier: during early embryonic development in mammals, primordial germ cells undergo extensive, global epigenetic reprogramming. This "wiping of the slate" strips away the vast majority of acquired methylation marks. Consequently, while transient epigenetic transmission has been observed in brief laboratory models, confirming robust, multi-generational inheritance in wild mammalian populations remains highly contentious due to this cellular erasure mechanism.
     
     Prompt:
     Which choice best states the main idea of the text?
     
     Options:
     A) Mammalian embryonic development completely validates transgenerational epigenetics by protecting methylation marks from cellular erasure.
     B) Classical neo-Darwinian paradigms have been entirely overturned by definitive evidence of Lamarckian inheritance in wild mammalian populations.
     C) The hypothesis that environmental trauma can structurally alter gene expression across generations faces significant skepticism due to a biological mechanism that erases most epigenetic marks during development.
     D) Laboratory models are fundamentally flawed because they artificially induce DNA methylation marks that do not appear in nature.
     
     Correct Answer: C
     
     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice A is incorrect because mammalian development presents a "critical mechanistic barrier" that *erases* rather than protects or validates these marks.
     * Choice B is incorrect because the text notes that the hypothesis remains "highly contentious" and has *not* entirely overturned the classical paradigm.
     * Choice D is incorrect because the text acknowledges that transient transmission has been *observed* in laboratory settings; it doesn't label the models as fundamentally flawed, but rather questions if those findings scale to long-term multi-generational inheritance in the wild.

     QUESTION 35
     Passage:
     The Sapir-Whorf hypothesis, or linguistic relativity, historically posited that the structural grammar and lexicon of a language act as an absolute prison, dictating and circumscribing the cognitive boundaries of its speakers. Early critics dismissed this radical determinism, noting that translation across disparate languages is readily achievable, which suggests a universal human cognitive baseline. Modern cognitive linguistics has revised this paradigm, shifting away from strict determinism toward a softer formulation. Current empirical frameworks suggest that while language does not *imprison* thought or prevent alternative conceptualizations, it acts as a subtle lens that alters cognitive processing efficiency. By rendering certain conceptual relationships more syntactically salient, a language shifts the cognitive path of least resistance, influencing how its speakers categorize experiences without rigidly preventing them from understanding other perspectives.
     
     Prompt:
     Which choice best states the main idea of the text?
     
     Options:
     A) Recent empirical research has completely vindicated the historical Sapir-Whorf hypothesis, proving that cross-linguistic translation is fundamentally impossible.
     B) Language has no discernible impact on human cognition, as all human minds operate along identical, universal paths of processing efficiency.
     C) Modern cognitive linguistics views language as a rigid structural barrier that prevents individuals from understanding alternative cultural frameworks.
     D) The understanding of linguistic relativity has evolved from a view of absolute cognitive determinism to one where language subtly biases, rather than limits, mental processing.
     
     Correct Answer: D
     
     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice A is incorrect because the text states early critics showed translation *is* achievable and that modern linguistics has abandoned this radical determinism.
     * Choice B is incorrect because the text directly states that language *does* have an impact, functioning as a "subtle lens that alters cognitive processing efficiency."
     * Choice C is incorrect because the modern view explicitly rejects the idea of language as a rigid barrier that prevents alternative conceptualizations.

     QUESTION 36
     Passage:
     The following text is adapted from a literary analysis of John Milton’s 1667 epic poem, Paradise Lost.
     Milton’s portrayal of Satan has long vexed literary critics who grapple with the character’s complex rhetorical architecture. In the opening books, Satan is cast in an undeniably heroic mold, delivering majestic speeches that resonate with classical themes of republican resistance against tyranny. Romantic poets like Percy Bysshe Shelley famously celebrated this rebellious grandeur, declaring Milton’s Satan to be morally superior to his tyrannical God. However, analyzing the epic's trajectory reveals a deliberate narrative deconstruction. As the poem progresses, Satan’s grand rhetoric degrades into petty self-delusion, and his physical form deteriorates from a radiant archangel into a base reptile. Milton intentionally seduces the reader with classical heroism only to systematically expose its moral vacuity, suggesting that true heroism lies not in assertive, self-aggrandizing rebellion, but in the quiet, submissive virtue exemplified later in the text.
     
     Prompt:
     Which choice best states the central idea of the text?
     
     Options:
     A) Shelley’s romantic interpretation of Satan as a morally superior hero completely aligns with the structural trajectory of Milton's entire epic poem.
     B) Milton utilizes a process of narrative and physical degeneration to dismantle Satan's initial heroic grandeur, ultimately redefining the true nature of virtue.
     C) Satan’s physical degradation into a reptile was a late editorial addition that contradicted Milton's original focus on classical republican resistance.
     D) The failure of Satan's rebellion proves that Milton believed political resistance against monarchy was inherently sinful and morally vacant.
     
     Correct Answer: B
     
     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice A is incorrect because Shelley's view only aligns with the *opening books*, whereas the text states the *entire trajectory* serves to deconstruct and expose that initial view.
     * Choice C is incorrect because the passage presents the degradation as a "deliberate narrative deconstruction" by Milton, not an arbitrary or contradictory late addition.
     * Choice D is incorrect because the text frames the moral critique around *spiritual* concepts of pride vs "quiet, submissive virtue," rather than making a sweeping historical claim about all political resistance against earthly monarchies.

     QUESTION 37
     Passage:
     Standard cosmological models predict that dwarf galaxies, because of their relatively low stellar masses, should exhibit steep, highly concentrated spikes of dark matter at their galactic centers—a phenomenon known as the "cusp" profile. However, high-resolution spectroscopic observations of nearby dwarf spheroidal galaxies consistently reveal a drastically different reality: the dark matter distribution is flat and uniformly distributed across a broad central core. This persistent mismatch, termed the "cusp-core problem," has ignited intense theoretical debates. Some astrophysicists argue that the predictive models are correct but fail to account for "baryonic feedback"—the energetic processes of supernova explosions that can physically push dark matter outward from the center. Others contend that the anomaly exposes a fundamental flaw in the cold dark matter model itself, suggesting that dark matter particles may interact via self-repulsive forces that naturally smooth out galactic centers.
     
     Prompt:
     Which choice best states the main idea of the text?
     
     Options:
     A) High-resolution observations have disproven the existence of dark matter in dwarf spheroidal galaxies, forcing a complete abandonment of cosmological models.
     B) The cusp-core problem describes a contradiction between predicted and observed dark matter concentrations in dwarf galaxies, inspiring competing astrophysical explanations.
     C) Supernova explosions are the universally accepted explanation for the flat dark matter cores observed at the center of dwarf galaxies.
     D) Cold dark matter models are completely flawless when applied to large spiral galaxies, but become inaccurate due to the absence of baryonic matter in dwarf systems.
     
     Correct Answer: B
     
     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice A is incorrect because the observations show a different *distribution* (core instead of cusp) of dark matter, not that dark matter does not exist or has been completely abandoned.
     * Choice C is incorrect because supernova explosions (baryonic feedback) represent only *one* side of an intense theoretical debate, not a "universally accepted" explanation.
     * Choice D is incorrect because the text does not discuss large spiral galaxies or claim that dwarf systems entirely lack baryonic matter.

     QUESTION 38
     Passage:
     Sociological analyses of workplace automation frequently diverge along ideological lines. Structural functionalists view automation as a stabilizing mechanism of optimization that shifts human labor toward high-skill, cognitive domains while purging hazardous or repetitive tasks. This perspective frames technological transition as an adaptive sorting process that ultimately enhances societal equilibrium. Conversely, conflict theorists interpret automation through the lens of power asymmetry, arguing that it functions primarily as a mechanism of capitalist deskilling. By embedding worker expertise into proprietary software and robotic algorithms, industrialists can depress wages, weaken collective bargaining power, and intensify worker alienation. Therefore, automation cannot be evaluated as an isolated technical upgrade; its societal meaning is fundamentally contingent upon whether it is analyzed as an instrument of system efficiency or as an apparatus of class exploitation.
     
     Prompt:
     Which choice best summarizes the main idea of the text?
     
     Options:
     A) Structural functionalism provides a more accurate empirical framework for studying the real-world economic impacts of labor automation than conflict theory.
     B) Automation inevitably leads to higher wages and stronger collective bargaining power by optimizing system efficiencies within modern factories.
     C) The sociological impact of automation is interpreted differently depending on whether it is viewed as an adaptive optimization process or an expression of power and exploitation.
     D) Industrialists intentionally adopt robotic algorithms to replace skilled cognitive labor while maintaining hazardous working conditions for unskilled laborers.
     
     Correct Answer: C
     
     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice A is incorrect because the passage presents both perspectives as divergent ideological frameworks without validating one as more "accurate" than the other.
     * Choice B is incorrect because it reflects a misinterpretation of conflict theory, which argues automation can *depress* wages and *weaken* bargaining power.
     * Choice D is incorrect because it twists the claims; structural functionalists note that automation *purges* hazardous tasks, and conflict theorists argue it causes deskilling, rather than industrialists intentionally maintaining hazardous conditions.

     QUESTION 39
     Passage:
     In his influential 1935 essay "The Work of Art in the Age of Its Technical Reproducibility," cultural philosopher Walter Benjamin introduced the concept of the "aura"—the unique, irreplaceable presence of an artwork tied to its specific location, history, and cultural tradition. Benjamin argued that mass reproduction techniques, such as photography and film, systematically dismantle this aura. By detachedly replicating an image millions of times, the reproduction strips the object of its singular authenticity and historical testimony. Yet, Benjamin’s critique is remarkably ambivalent: he notes that while the decay of the aura eliminates the traditional, quasi-religious ritual value of art, it simultaneously democratizes visual culture. By making art accessible to the masses outside of elite galleries, technical reproducibility transforms art from an object of passive, esoteric contemplation into an active instrument of political critique.
     
     Prompt:
     Which choice best states the main idea of the text?
     
     Options:
     A) Walter Benjamin argued that photography and film are inferior artistic mediums because they completely lack historical authenticity and political value.
     B) The technical reproducibility of art destroys its traditional unique aura, a process that Benjamin viewed with ambivalence because it simultaneously democratizes art for political engagement.
     C) Art galleries intentionally promoted mass reproduction techniques to protect the quasi-religious ritual value of traditional masterpieces.
     D) The unique aura of an artwork can be perfectly preserved and even enhanced when it is replicated millions of times via mass media.
     
     Correct Answer: B
     
     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice A is incorrect because Benjamin notes that reproducibility transforms art into an "active instrument of political critique," meaning he sees profound value in these mediums rather than viewing them as simply inferior.
     * Choice C is incorrect because the text states reproducibility strips art of its ritual value and places it *outside* elite galleries, contradicting the idea that galleries used it to protect ritual value.
     * Choice D is incorrect because the passage explicitly states that mass reproduction "systematically dismantle[s]" and causes the "decay" of the aura, making perfect preservation impossible under this framework.

     QUESTION 40
     Passage:
     Deep-sea ecosystems centered around chemosynthetic hydrothermal vents have long been considered insulated from anthropogenic disturbances affecting the upper ocean. However, marine ecologists have recently uncovered teleconnections indicating that localized ocean acidification can cascade down to these benthic depths. Acidification disrupts the metabolic efficiency of larval organisms in the epipelagic zone, leading to a drastic reduction in the volume of "marine snow"—the falling organic detritus that feeds intermediary trophic levels. As this biological pump weakens, the nutritional scarcity triggers a metabolic stress response in the predatory crab and gastropod populations that graze near the vents. Because these apex vent predators regulate the expansion of primary chemosynthetic bacterial mats, their decline allows unchecked bacterial overgrowth that rapidly chokes out critical tubeworm habitats, exposing a profound vulnerability at the core of the benthic food web.
     
     Prompt:
     Which choice best states the main idea of the text?
     
     Options:
     A) Chemosynthetic bacteria are capable of neutralizing ocean acidification, thereby protecting deep-sea tubeworm habitats from upper-ocean disturbances.
     B) Localized ocean acidification can trigger a downward ecological cascade that disrupts deep-sea vent ecosystems by weakening the biological pump and destabilizing predator-prey dynamics.
     C) Deep-sea tubeworms are highly resilient organisms that easily adapt to nutritional scarcity by feeding directly on marine snow.
     D) The biological pump is an isolated system that prevents epipelagic metabolic disruptions from reaching benthic depths.
     
     Correct Answer: B
     
     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice A is incorrect because the text states that unchecked bacterial overgrowth "rapidly chokes out" tubeworm habitats, meaning they do not neutralize or protect the ecosystem from the threat.
     * Choice C is incorrect because the text notes that the disruption "chokes out critical tubeworm habitats," showing they are vulnerable rather than easily adaptive, and they are dependent on the ecosystem's structural balance rather than directly eating marine snow to survive.
     * Choice D is incorrect because the entire passage demonstrates that the biological pump connects the zones, allowing upper ocean disruptions to cascade down to benthic depths, contradicting the idea that it is an isolated or protective shield.
