     QUESTION 41
     Passage:
     A student is researching plant biology and forms a hypothesis that playing classical music near tomato plants will cause them to grow taller. To test this hypothesis, the student sets up two separate greenhouses with identical soil, water, and sunlight conditions. In the first greenhouse, classical music is played continuously. In the second greenhouse, no music is played. After six weeks, the student measures the heights of all the plants.
     
     Prompt:
     Which choice, if true, would most directly support the student's hypothesis?
     
     Options:
     A) The plants in the first greenhouse grew significantly taller on average than the plants in the second greenhouse.
     B) The plants in both greenhouses grew to exactly the same average height at the end of the six weeks.
     C) The plants in the first greenhouse produced greener leaves, but their stems remained short.
     D) The plants in the second greenhouse grew taller when the student played rock music instead of classical music.
     
     Correct Answer: A
     
     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice B is incorrect because if the plants grew to the same height, it demonstrates that classical music had no effect, which directly weakens the hypothesis.
     * Choice C is incorrect because greener leaves do not support the specific hypothesis regarding plant *height*.
     * Choice D is incorrect because testing rock music in the second greenhouse introduces a new variable that does not prove classical music causes plants to grow taller.

     -----------------------------------------------------------------
     
     QUESTION 42
     Passage:
     An archaeologist claims that an ancient coastal city in Greece engaged in regular trade with a nearby island community during the Bronze Age. To support this claim, the archaeologist points out that the coastal city lacked its own natural sources of copper, an essential material for making tools, while the nearby island possessed a massive copper mine that was highly active during that exact historical period.
     
     Prompt:
     Which choice, if true, would most directly support the archaeologist's claim?
     
     Options:
     A) Excavations of the coastal city's marketplace revealed numerous bronze tools containing copper chemically identical to the copper from the island's mine.
     B) The coastal city had large stone walls that were built to protect its citizens from pirate attacks.
     C) Historians discovered that the island community also traded copper with cities located thousands of miles away in Egypt.
     D) The residents of the coastal city primarily used stone tools instead of metal tools for everyday farming.
     
     Correct Answer: A
     
     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice B is incorrect because stone walls for protection against pirates provide no evidence regarding trade relations with the island.
     * Choice C is incorrect because the island trading with Egypt does not prove that it traded specifically with the nearby Greek coastal city mentioned by the archaeologist.
     * Choice D is incorrect because if the city primarily used stone tools, it suggests they had little need for imported copper, which weakens the trade claim.

     -----------------------------------------------------------------
     
     QUESTION 43
     Passage:
     A zoologist hypothesizes that global temperature increases are causing a specific species of songbird to alter its yearly migration patterns. The zoologist believes that warmer spring temperatures prompt the birds to leave their wintering grounds in South America and arrive at their northern nesting grounds much earlier in the year than they did in the past.
     
     Prompt:
     Which choice, if true, would most directly support the zoologist's hypothesis?
     
     Options:
     A) In years with unusually warm spring temperatures, the songbirds arrived at their northern nesting grounds up to ten days earlier than normal.
     B) The songbirds chose to build larger nests in trees that provided more shade from the sun.
     C) Over the last decade, the songbird population has declined due to a shortage of insect food sources.
     D) Other bird species that do not migrate have shown no changes in their breeding behaviors during warm years.
     
     Correct Answer: A
     
     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice B is incorrect because nest size and shade preferences do not address the timing of migration arrival.
     * Choice C is incorrect because a population decline due to food shortages is irrelevant to the specific link between temperature and migration timing.
     * Choice D is incorrect because the behavior of non-migratory bird species does not provide data about the migration schedule of the songbird species in question.

     -----------------------------------------------------------------
     
     QUESTION 44
     Passage:
     A literary critic argues that in her poetry, Elena Vance uses dark, shadow-filled imagery not simply to describe nighttime settings, but specifically to symbolize the internal feelings of grief and sorrow experienced by her speakers. 
     
     Prompt:
     Which choice provides the most direct textual evidence to support the critic's argument?
     
     Options:
     A) In "Midnight Bell," Vance writes, "The moon shines bright upon the town / As children sleep in beds of down."
     B) In "October Fog," Vance writes, "A heavy mist rolls down the lane / To clear away the summer rain."
     C) In "The Empty Room," Vance writes, "An endless shadow wraps my heart / Since the sad day we had to part."
     D) In "Starlight Walk," Vance writes, "The stars align to guide my feet / Along the quiet, empty street."
     
     Correct Answer: C
     
     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice A is incorrect because bright moonlight and sleeping children convey peace or calm, not internal grief and sorrow.
     * Choice B is incorrect because mist clearing away rain describes a natural setting without linking dark imagery to personal grief.
     * Choice D is incorrect because stars guiding feet along a quiet street lacks any connection to themes of sorrow or mourning.

     QUESTION 45
     Passage:
     A team of nutritionists conducted a study to test the claim that consuming high daily doses of Vitamin C reduces the frequency of common colds. They tracked two groups of 500 participants over a winter season. Group 1 took a daily Vitamin C supplement, while Group 2 took an identical-looking sugar pill (placebo). All participants followed the same diet and exercise routines.
     
     Prompt:
     Which choice, if true, would most directly support the claim being tested?
     
     Options:
     A) Participants in Group 1 reported having significantly fewer colds during the winter than participants in Group 2.
     B) Many participants in Group 2 stated that they preferred the taste of the sugar pill over regular fruit juices.
     C) At the end of the study, both Group 1 and Group 2 had the exact same total number of recorded sick days.
     D) Group 1 participants felt more energetic during the day, but they still caught colds at a normal rate.
     
     Correct Answer: A
     
     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice B is incorrect because the taste preference for the placebo pill does not provide any evidence regarding the medical efficacy of Vitamin C against colds.
     * Choice C is incorrect because equal numbers of sick days between groups indicates that Vitamin C had no impact, directly undermining the claim.
     * Choice D is incorrect because increased daytime energy does not fulfill the specific claim that Vitamin C reduces the *frequency* of common colds.

     QUESTION 46
     Passage:
     Marine biologists investigating coral reef degradation hypothesized that coral reefs located in shallow waters recover from storm damage much faster than coral reefs located in deep waters. To evaluate this, they monitored a shallow reef and a deep reef in the same region for three years following a severe hurricane that damaged both environments equally.
     
     Prompt:
     Which choice, if true, would most directly support the biologists' hypothesis?
     
     Options:
     A) The shallow reef showed a 65% return of healthy coral colonies after three years, whereas the deep reef showed only a 15% return.
     B) The deep reef was home to a wider variety of colorful fish species than the shallow reef before the hurricane hit.
     C) Water temperatures near the shallow reef fluctuated wildly throughout the three-year monitoring period.
     D) Tourists preferred to visit the shallow reef for snorkeling because it offered better underwater visibility.
     
     Correct Answer: A
     
     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice B is incorrect because fish variety *before* the hurricane does not provide evidence about the post-storm *recovery rate* of the corals.
     * Choice C is incorrect because temperature fluctuations alone do not prove or show faster structural recovery.
     * Choice D is incorrect because tourist preferences and snorkeling visibility are commercial/recreational factors, not biological evidence of reef recovery.

     QUESTION 47
     Passage:
     A technology developer claims that using a newly designed smartphone application called BudgetBuddy helps individuals save more money each month compared to traditional pen-and-paper budgeting methods. The developer sets up an experiment with 200 participants: half are instructed to use BudgetBuddy, and the other half are told to use a paper notebook to track expenses.
     
     Prompt:
     Which choice, if true, would most directly support the developer's claim?
     
     Options:
     A) Participants using BudgetBuddy saved an average of $150 more per month than the participants using paper notebooks.
     B) The BudgetBuddy application was downloaded more than one million times during its first week on the app store.
     C) Participants using the paper notebooks reported that writing down expenses by hand was relaxing.
     D) Both groups of participants spent the same average amount of money on monthly grocery shopping.
     
     Correct Answer: A
     
     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice B is incorrect because high download numbers indicate popularity or successful marketing, but do not prove that users actually successfully saved more money.
     * Choice C is incorrect because the physical relaxation of writing by hand does not provide data supporting the claim that the app yields superior financial savings.
     * Choice D is incorrect because equal spending on groceries shows a lack of difference in one category, offering no proof of overall monthly savings success for the app group.

     QUESTION 48
     Passage:
     An educational psychologist asserts that reading a physical fiction book for fifteen minutes before bed improves overall sleep quality in teenagers. To investigate this, the psychologist tracks the bedtime routines and sleep patterns of 100 high school students over two weeks, comparing nights when students read a fiction book to nights when they watched television before sleeping.
     
     Prompt:
     Which choice, if true, would most directly support the psychologist's assertion?
     
     Options:
     A) On nights when students read physical fiction books, they fell asleep faster and experienced longer periods of deep sleep than on nights they watched television.
     B) High school students who read books reported that they preferred reading fantasy novels over realistic fiction.
     C) Students who watched television before bed reported that their favorite programs were comedies rather than dramas.
     D) Reading physical books during afternoon study halls made students feel tired and unfocused.
     
     Correct Answer: A
     
     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice B is incorrect because a preference for fantasy over realistic fiction does not provide empirical evidence regarding sleep quality metrics.
     * Choice C is incorrect because the genre of television watched does not support the claim that reading books improves sleep quality.
     * Choice D is incorrect because feeling tired during afternoon study halls contradicts the idea of healthy sleep improvement and addresses the wrong time of day.

     QUESTION 49
     Passage:
     An ecologist claims that planting white clover in agricultural fields improves the overall health of the soil. White clover is known to form partnerships with soil bacteria that pull nitrogen gas from the air and convert it into a nutrient form that stays in the earth, which should benefit neighboring plants.
     
     Prompt:
     Which choice, if true, would most directly support the ecologist's claim?
     
     Options:
     A) Fields planted with white clover showed a substantial increase in soil nitrogen levels and higher crop yields compared to fields left empty.
     B) White clover fields attracted a large population of honeybees and butterflies throughout the summer months.
     C) Farmers found that white clover seeds were more expensive to purchase than grass seeds.
     D) White clover grew rapidly even in areas experiencing mild drought conditions.
     
     Correct Answer: A
     
     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice B is incorrect because attracting pollinators like bees and butterflies is a benefit to local wildlife, but does not provide direct evidence of improved *soil health*.
     * Choice C is incorrect because the market price of the seeds is an economic detail completely irrelevant to the biological health of the soil.
     * Choice D is incorrect because a plant's ability to survive a drought proves its resilience, but does not demonstrate that it actively improves the nutrient quality of the surrounding soil.

     QUESTION 50
     Passage:
     An art historian claims that the 17th-century painter Mateo Silva used expensive blue paint made from crushed lapis lazuli stones exclusively to signify characters of royal or divine status in his portraits, reserving cheaper earth-toned pigments for depictions of common citizens.
     
     Prompt:
     Which choice, if true, would most directly support the art historian's claim?
     
     Options:
     A) Chemical testing of Silva's paintings revealed lapis lazuli pigments only in the robes of kings and angels, while merchants and servants were painted with basic brown and yellow clays.
     B) Documents show that Silva purchased large quantities of lapis lazuli from overseas traders at a very high financial cost.
     C) Silva's contemporaries often praised his portraits for their lifelike details and masterly use of shadow and light.
     D) Lapis lazuli was a highly prized stone across Europe and was frequently used to create jewelry for noble families.
     
     Correct Answer: A
     
     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice B is incorrect because purchasing expensive lapis lazuli proves he had access to it, but does not prove he used it *exclusively* for royal/divine subjects as claimed.
     * Choice C is incorrect because general praise for lifelike details and shadows does not address the specific symbolic use of blue pigment based on social status.
     * Choice D is incorrect because the general use of lapis lazuli for jewelry among nobles does not provide direct textual or physical evidence regarding Silva's painting choices.

     QUESTION 51
     Passage:
     An economist hypothesized that reducing public transit fares in a metropolitan city increases local business revenue by lowering the financial barrier for suburban residents to travel to urban shopping districts. To evaluate this hypothesis, the economist analyzed sales tax data from two comparable cities: City X, which reduced transit fares by 50% for six months, and City Y, which kept transit fares constant during the same period.
     
     Prompt:
     Which choice, if true, would most directly support the economist's hypothesis?
     
     Options:
     A) City X experienced a significant surge in retail sales revenues within its urban shopping districts during the fare reduction, while City Y's retail revenues remained flat.
     B) Public transit ridership in City X increased among students and elderly residents who rarely visited retail shopping districts.
     C) City Y launched a successful marketing campaign that encouraged residents to shop online rather than visit brick-and-mortar stores.
     D) Suburban residents in City X reported that they saved money on transit fares but preferred to spend those savings on home renovations.
     
     Correct Answer: A
     
     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice B is incorrect because if ridership increased only among demographics who rarely shop in the retail districts, it undermines the mechanism proposed by the economist.
     * Choice C is incorrect because online shopping habits in City Y do not provide evidence that lowering transit fares actively boosts business revenue in City X.
     * Choice D is incorrect because if savings were spent on home renovations rather than urban retail, it directly contradicts the idea that fare reductions boost shopping district revenue.

     QUESTION 52
     Passage:
     A paleontologist investigating the behavioral habits of a recently discovered dinosaur species, *Spinosuchus*, hypothesized that the creature was semi-aquatic rather than entirely terrestrial. To bolster this claim, the researcher analyzed the chemical composition of fossilized teeth from *Spinosuchus* alongside teeth from known terrestrial dinosaurs and ancient fully aquatic crocodiles found in the same geological strata.
     
     Prompt:
     Which choice, if true, would most directly support the paleontologist's hypothesis?
     
     Options:
     A) The oxygen isotope ratios in *Spinosuchus* teeth closely matched those of the ancient aquatic crocodiles, differing significantly from the ratios found in terrestrial dinosaurs.
     B) *Spinosuchus* fossilized skeletons possessed large, sharp claws that were physically identical to the claws of modern land-dwelling lizards.
     C) Strata analysis indicated that the geographic region inhabited by *Spinosuchus* shifted from a lush wetland to an arid desert over millions of years.
     D) The teeth of *Spinosuchus* were smaller on average than the teeth of fully aquatic crocodiles from the same period.
     
     Correct Answer: A
     
     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice B is incorrect because claws identical to land-dwelling lizards would suggest a terrestrial adaptation, which directly weakens the semi-aquatic hypothesis.
     * Choice C is incorrect because long-term regional climate shifts over millions of years do not provide evidence about the specific behavioral habits of this individual species.
     * Choice D is incorrect because the physical size comparison of the teeth does not provide evidence of a semi-aquatic lifestyle, whereas chemical isotope tracking does.

     QUESTION 53
     Passage:
     Astronomers seeking to explain atmospheric variations on the rocky exoplanet *Zephyr-7* hypothesized that active volcanic eruptions on the surface are responsible for sudden spikes in atmospheric sulfur dioxide. To test this, they utilized high-resolution space telescopes to continuously monitor both the planet's atmospheric chemical signatures and its localized surface thermal output over a one-year period.
     
     Prompt:
     Which choice, if true, would most directly support the astronomers' hypothesis?
     
     Options:
     A) Sharp increases in atmospheric sulfur dioxide concentrations were observed immediately after telescopes detected intense, localized spikes in surface heat signatures.
     B) *Zephyr-7* possesses an orbital path that brings it close to its host star, causing uniform surface temperatures across the entire planet.
     C) Atmospheric sulfur dioxide levels remained low and perfectly stable during months when the exoplanet was hidden behind its host star.
     D) Computer simulations indicated that if *Zephyr-7* had an iron core, volcanic activity would be impossible on its surface.
     
     Correct Answer: A
     
     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice B is incorrect because uniform surface temperatures caused by a star do not support the idea of localized volcanic eruptions causing chemical spikes.
     * Choice C is incorrect because stable levels when hidden do not establish a correlation between surface volcanic events (heat spikes) and atmospheric changes.
     * Choice D is incorrect because a simulation establishing a condition under which volcanism is *impossible* does not provide evidence that volcanism is occurring and driving sulfur spikes.

     -----------------------------------------------------------------
     
     QUESTION 54
     Passage:
     A sociology student conducted a study regarding online academic peer groups. The student claimed that participating in online study groups only yields measurable academic benefits for students if the group has a clearly designated leader to guide discussions. To test this, the student evaluated the exam performance of 300 undergraduates divided into leader-led groups, leaderless groups, and individual self-study blocks.
     
     Prompt:
     Which choice, if true, would most directly support the sociology student's claim?
     
     Options:
     A) Undergraduates in leader-led online study groups scored significantly higher on exams than those who studied individually or in leaderless groups, while leaderless groups showed no improvement over individual study.
     B) Students in leaderless groups reported having more enjoyable discussions and spending more total hours online than students in leader-led groups.
     C) Individual self-study blocks resulted in the highest overall exam scores when students had access to recorded video lectures.
     D) Leader-led groups performed exceptionally well only when the designated leader was a student majoring in the specific subject being tested.
     
     Correct Answer: A
     
     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice B is incorrect because enjoyable discussions and hours spent online do not equate to "measurable academic benefits" (exam performance), which is the focus of the claim.
     * Choice C is incorrect because if individual study yielded the highest scores, it completely refutes the idea that online peer groups provide unique academic benefits.
     * Choice D is incorrect because it narrows the conditions of success to the leader's major, rather than supporting the general thesis that a designated leader is the necessary threshold component for group efficacy.

     QUESTION 55
     Passage:
     A botanist hypothesized that elevated carbon dioxide levels in the atmosphere benefit invasive vine species to a much greater degree than they benefit native tree species. The botanist grew samples of the invasive vine *Kudzu* and the native *White Oak* tree in controlled environmental chambers, exposing half of the samples to current atmospheric CO2 levels and the other half to doubled CO2 levels.
     
     Prompt:
     Which choice, if true, would most directly support the botanist's hypothesis?
     
     Options:
     A) Under doubled CO2 levels, the invasive vine exhibited a 50% increase in total biomass, whereas the native tree exhibited only a 5% increase in total biomass.
     B) Both the invasive vine and the native tree showed an identical 25% increase in growth rates when exposed to doubled CO2 levels.
     C) Under current CO2 levels, the native tree naturally produced stronger root structures and grew taller than the invasive vine.
     D) The native tree exhibited signs of toxic leaf stress and stunted growth when exposed to doubled CO2 levels in the absence of water.
     
     Correct Answer: A
     
     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice B is incorrect because an identical increase in growth rates across both species indicates that elevated CO2 does not benefit the invasive vine to a *greater* degree.
     * Choice C is incorrect because baseline growth advantages under *current* CO2 levels do not provide information about how the species respond to *elevated* CO2.
     * Choice D is incorrect because introducing a confounding variable like the absence of water obscures the direct impact of elevated CO2 on relative growth.

     -----------------------------------------------------------------
     
     QUESTION 56
     Passage:
     A linguistics researcher asserted that young children acquire new vocabulary words significantly faster through active interactive play than through passive listening to educational audiobooks. To gather evidence, the researcher designed a study where two groups of toddlers were exposed to ten unfamiliar words: Group A interacted with puppets controlled by an instructor who spoke the words, while Group B listened to a recorded narrator read a story containing the same words.
     
     Prompt:
     Which choice, if true, would most directly support the researcher's assertion?
     
     Options:
     A) Toddlers in Group A correctly identified and used an average of eight new words during a post-study assessment, compared to an average of only two words for Group B.
     B) Parents of toddlers in Group B reported that their children listened to audiobooks at home for several hours each week prior to the study.
     C) A follow-up test revealed that toddlers in both groups forgot all ten unfamiliar words within two weeks if they did not practice them at home.
     D) Toddlers in Group A displayed higher physical energy levels during the sessions but threw more behavioral tantrums than those in Group B.
     
     Correct Answer: A
     
     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice B is incorrect because home listening habits prior to the study do not measure the relative word acquisition rates achieved during the experiment.
     * Choice C is incorrect because identical rates of forgetting across both groups indicates long-term parity, failing to show that active play speeds up initial acquisition.
     * Choice D is incorrect because physical energy levels and behavioral tantrums are behavioral traits that do not provide evidence of cognitive vocabulary acquisition.

     -----------------------------------------------------------------
     
     QUESTION 57
     Passage:
     An architectural engineer claimed that installing extensive green roofs (roofs covered with living vegetation) on urban buildings reduces internal cooling costs during summer months by providing natural insulation and reducing heat absorption. The engineer conducted a comparative analysis of two structurally identical concrete office buildings in Chicago during July: Building 1 featured a newly installed green roof, while Building 2 retained its traditional black tar roof.
     
     Prompt:
     Which choice, if true, would most directly support the engineer's claim?
     
     Options:
     A) Building 1 required 35% less electricity for its air conditioning systems and maintained lower internal temperatures than Building 2 throughout July.
     B) The installation cost of the green roof on Building 1 was significantly higher than the maintenance costs of Building 2's tar roof.
     C) Building 2 experienced minor roof leaks during a heavy thunderstorm, whereas Building 1's vegetation absorbed the rainwater perfectly.
     D) Employees working in Building 1 reported higher job satisfaction scores because they enjoyed looking at the green roof plants.
     
     Correct Answer: A
     
     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice B is incorrect because higher upfront installation costs represent an economic drawback, offering no support for the claim regarding internal cooling reduction.
     * Choice C is incorrect because preventing roof leaks demonstrates structural water management, which is independent of thermodynamic insulation and cooling costs.
     * Choice D is incorrect because psychological employee satisfaction does not provide empirical evidence of physical engineering performance or energy reduction.

     QUESTION 58
     Passage:
     A literary scholar claimed that the poet Arthur Vance's stylistic choices became drastically more avant-garde and experimental after his permanent relocation to Paris in 1922. To demonstrate this shift, the scholar compared Vance's early works published in London with his later collections produced during his Parisian period.
     
     Prompt:
     Which choice provides the most direct textual evidence to support the scholar's claim?
     
     Options:
     A) Vance's Parisian poems are characterized by fragmented syntax, stream-of-consciousness formatting, and irregular line breaks, elements completely absent from his highly structured London sonnets.
     B) In a 1923 letter from Paris, Vance wrote, "The city is beautiful, but I find myself writing about the exact same themes of nature and loss that I explored while living in London."
     C) Vance's London poetry collections sold significantly more physical copies and received warmer reviews from contemporary mainstream literary critics than his Parisian books.
     D) Vance continued to use traditional rhyme schemes and strict iambic pentameter across all poems written between 1915 and 1930.
     
     Correct Answer: A
     
     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice B is incorrect because Vance's letter states he is writing about the "exact same themes," which suggests continuity rather than a drastic stylistic evolution.
     * Choice C is incorrect because sales figures and critical reviews measure commercial reception and popularity, not internal stylistic features.
     * Choice D is incorrect because it directly refutes the claim by showing Vance maintained traditional, non-experimental forms uniformly before and after his move.

     QUESTION 59
     Passage:
     A zoologist hypothesized that gray squirrels emit a unique high-pitched alarm call exclusively to warn group members about aerial predators, such as hawks or owls, rather than terrestrial predators, such as foxes or coyotes. To observe this distinction, the zoologist exposed wild squirrel colonies to realistic mechanical models of various predators and recorded their vocal responses.
     
     Prompt:
     Which choice, if true, would most directly support the zoologist's hypothesis?
     
     Options:
     A) Squirrels emitted the unique high-pitched alarm call in 95% of trials involving the hawk and owl models, but remained silent or fled without calling in trials involving the fox and coyote models.
     B) The high-pitched alarm call was loud enough to be heard by other squirrels located up to half a mile away from the source of danger.
     C) When exposed to the mechanical fox model, squirrels emitted a low-frequency clicking sound that was also used during territorial disputes with rival squirrels.
     D) Younger squirrels frequently emitted the high-pitched alarm call by mistake when harmless falling leaves passed through their field of vision.
     
     Correct Answer: A
     
     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice B is incorrect because the physical volume and travel distance of the call do not prove that it is used *exclusively* for aerial vs terrestrial threats.
     * Choice C is incorrect because while it shows a different sound for foxes, it does not confirm that the specific high-pitched call is triggered reliably by aerial threats.
     * Choice D is incorrect because mistaken calls triggered by falling leaves suggest a lack of precision, weakening the idea that the call is a specific, evolved warning system.

     QUESTION 60
     Passage:
     Environmental scientists hypothesized that microplastic particles accumulate heavily within marine filter-feeding organisms (which strain food from water) compared to predatory marine organisms occupying higher positions in the food web. To test this, they collected wild specimens of filter-feeding blue mussels and predatory rock crabs from the same coastal bay and measured microplastic concentrations per gram of tissue.
     
     Prompt:
     Which choice, if true, would most directly support the scientists' hypothesis?
     
     Options:
     A) The blue mussels contained an average of 45 microplastic particles per gram of tissue, whereas the rock crabs contained an average of only 3 particles per gram.
     B) Rock crabs collected from areas further out in the open ocean displayed higher microplastic levels than crabs collected inside the coastal bay.
     C) Laboratory experiments showed that exposing blue mussels to high heat caused them to expel microplastics at a rapid rate.
     D) The total population of filter-feeding blue mussels in the coastal bay has declined steadily over the past decade due to water pollution.
     
     Correct Answer: A
     
     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice B is incorrect because comparing crabs from different locations does not test the relative accumulation between filter-feeders and predators in the same ecosystem.
     * Choice C is incorrect because a laboratory heat reaction does not provide data on the natural accumulation rates under baseline environmental conditions.
     * Choice D is incorrect because general population declines due to pollution do not prove that microplastics specifically accumulate more in one demographic than another.

     QUESTION 61
     Passage:
     Cognitive psychologists hypothesized that working memory training exercises improve mathematical reasoning skills only if the training program specifically incorporates tasks requiring spatial manipulation. To test this conditional hypothesis, researchers divided 150 students into three groups: Group 1 performed working memory exercises involving spatial rotating shapes; Group 2 performed working memory exercises involving verbal number sequences; and Group 3 did not participate in any training. All groups demonstrated identical baseline working memory capacities and mathematical reasoning scores prior to the study.
     
     Prompt:
     Which choice, if true, would most directly support the psychologists' hypothesis?
     
     Options:
     A) Group 1 showed substantial improvements in mathematical reasoning scores post-training, while Group 2 and Group 3 showed no statistical changes in mathematical reasoning, despite Group 2 showing significant increases in verbal memory capacity.
     B) Both Group 1 and Group 2 exhibited massive, identical improvements in mathematical reasoning scores and overall working memory capacities compared to Group 3.
     C) Group 2 outperformed Group 1 on subsequent standardized vocabulary tests, while Group 3 showed the highest performance on geometry assignments.
     D) Working memory exercises that did not include spatial manipulation were found to be completely ineffective at increasing any form of memory retention across all three groups.
     
     Correct Answer: A
     
     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice B is incorrect because if both groups improved identically, it contradicts the specific claim that spatial tasks are *contingently necessary* for math improvement.
     * Choice C is incorrect because vocabulary tests and geometry homework do not measure the precise relationship between working memory types and generalized mathematical reasoning scores.
     * Choice D is incorrect because if verbal exercises failed to increase *any* memory retention, it leaves open the possibility that memory improvement itself—not spatial design—drives math gains. Choice A isolates the variable perfectly by showing verbal memory increased but math did not.

     -----------------------------------------------------------------
     
     QUESTION 62
     Passage:
     An economic historian argues that the dramatic decline of the medieval Hanseatic trade network during the late 15th century was primarily driven by an escalation in maritime piracy along Northern European shipping lanes, rather than by the systemic silver currency inflation that occurred across the continent. To isolate the true causal mechanism, the historian compared trade volumes across various regions under Hanseatic control during this period.
     
     Prompt:
     Which choice, if true, would most directly support the historian's argument?
     
     Options:
     A) Hanseatic trade volumes plummeted by over 70% along maritime routes heavily targeted by pirates, while Hanseatic land-based trade routes remained completely stable and profitable, despite both sectors experiencing identical rates of silver currency inflation.
     B) Silver currency inflation caused the market price of essential maritime supplies, such as timber and canvas, to double across all Northern European ports during the 15th century.
     C) Historical court records indicate that several prominent Hanseatic merchants were caught secretly financing pirate fleets to disrupt the operations of their domestic commercial rivals.
     D) Maritime trade networks in the Mediterranean region flourished during the late 15th century because local governments successfully executed or imprisoned major pirate leaders.
     
     Correct Answer: A
     
     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice B is incorrect because highlighting the negative impacts of inflation weakens the claim that piracy—rather than inflation—was the primary driver of the network's decline.
     * Choice C is incorrect because merchants financing pirates to hurt rivals shows internal corruption, but does not isolate shipping line disruption as the macro-economic cause over currency trends.
     * Choice D is incorrect because economic data from a completely different geographic region (the Mediterranean) cannot validate the specific operational cause of decline for the northern Hanseatic network.

     -----------------------------------------------------------------
     
     QUESTION 63
     Passage:
     Marine ecotoxicologists hypothesized that ocean acidification harms sea urchin populations by disrupting their olfactory sensory navigation systems (which allow them to locate food), rather than by physically weakening the structural integrity of their protective calcium carbonate shells. Researchers exposed experimental groups of sea urchins to varying pH levels matching projected future ocean acidity profiles and assessed both their behavior in scent-guided mazes and the mechanical strength of their shells.
     
     Prompt:
     Which choice, if true, would most directly support the scientists' hypothesis?
     
     Options:
     A) Urchins exposed to highly acidic water consistently failed to navigate toward food cues in the mazes, yet their shells exhibited identical thickness and crushing resistance compared to urchins housed in normal water.
     B) Highly acidic water caused a 30% reduction in shell density over six months, but the urchins successfully adapted by increasing their moving speed toward food sources.
     C) Urchins in the control group with normal pH water displayed exceptional navigation skills and developed significantly thicker shells when fed a diet rich in calcium.
     D) When sensory navigation failed, the sea urchins suffered a high mortality rate because predatory fish could easily crush their weakened outer shells.
     
     Correct Answer: A
     
     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice B is incorrect because it explicitly shows shell degradation and successful navigation, which directly reverses the variables stated in the hypothesis.
     * Choice C is incorrect because the behavior of the control group under a special high-calcium diet does not isolate how acidification impacts sensory traits relative to shell structure.
     * Choice D is incorrect because it states that the outer shells were weakened, contradicting the premise that acidification does *not* physically degrade shell strength.

     QUESTION 64
     Passage:
     A literary historian hypothesized that the nineteenth-century novelist Claire Dupin authored an anonymous, controversial political pamphlet mocking a local politician in 1842, despite her public denials at the time. To evaluate authorship, stylistic analysts conducted a comprehensive computational stylometric profile, comparing the syntax, sentence length distributions, and rare vocabulary frequencies of the anonymous pamphlet with Dupin's known novels and private journals from that exact era.
     
     Prompt:
     Which choice provides the most direct textual evidence to support the stylometric analysts' hypothesis?
     
     Options:
     A) The anonymous pamphlet contains an idiosyncratic pattern of semicolons and a specific sequence of archaic adjectives that are perfectly mirrored in Dupin's private letters and novels written during the autumn of 1842.
     B) In an 1843 journal entry, Dupin wrote, "The anonymous pamphlet attacking the politician is brilliant, and whoever wrote it possesses an artistic mind far superior to my own."
     C) Historical publishing records from 1842 show that the anonymous pamphlet was printed using the exact same type of printing press that Dupin's publisher used for her novels.
     D) The local politician targeted by the pamphlet had previously published a harsh, highly public review criticizing the plot structure of Dupin's first major novel.
     
     Correct Answer: A
     
     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice B is incorrect because Dupin explicitly praises the author as someone "superior to my own," reinforcing her denial rather than supporting her authorship.
     * Choice C is incorrect because sharing a common commercial printing press proves proximity or standard industry usage, but does not provide individual textual evidence of authorship.
     * Choice D is incorrect because establishing a personal motive for revenge does not constitute stylistic or textual evidence that she wrote the specific piece.

     QUESTION 65
     Passage:
     In ecology, the "ecology of fear" hypothesis suggests that apex predators influence prey populations and lower trophic levels not primarily by killing and reducing the physical number of prey animals, but rather by altering the prey's foraging geography. According to this model, prey animals abandon high-risk open areas where predators hunt, allowing vegetation in those zones to recover. To evaluate this model, ecologists monitored elk foraging movements and willow tree growth before and after wolves were reintroduced to a national park.
     
     Prompt:
     Which choice, if true, would most directly support the ecology of fear hypothesis?
     
     Options:
     A) Following the wolf reintroduction, the total number of elk in the park remained statistically unchanged, but the elk completely stopped feeding in open river valleys, resulting in a dramatic increase in willow tree density within those valleys.
     B) The wolf population grew rapidly and killed over 40% of the park's elk herd within two years, leading to a uniform expansion of vegetation across all areas of the park.
     C) Elk that were tracked using GPS collars showed high physiological stress levels only when they were physically chased by a wolf pack near the park boundaries.
     D) Willow trees located on high, rocky cliffs grew taller than willow trees located in low valleys because cliff soil contained higher moisture levels.
     
     Correct Answer: A
     
     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice B is incorrect because it shows the predators functioning via direct mortality (killing 40% of the herd), which contradicts the hypothesis that they influence systems *independent* of changing headcount.
     * Choice C is incorrect because stress reactions during an active physical chase do not demonstrate a long-term geographic shift in foraging choices.
     * Choice D is incorrect because attributing tree growth variations to soil moisture levels overlooks and fails to measure the impact of predator-induced prey behavior.

     QUESTION 66
     Passage:
     Materials scientists claimed that incorporating silicon nanowires into thin-film solar cells increases their overall energy conversion efficiency by accelerating electron transport to the electrodes, rather than by expanding the cell's physical capacity to absorb incoming sunlight. To test this specific operational claim, the scientists manufactured standard solar cells and nanowire-infused solar cells, evaluating both their light absorption spectrum profiles and their internal electrical current transit times.
     
     Prompt:
     Which choice, if true, would most directly support the scientists' operational claim?
     
     Options:
     A) Solar cells with silicon nanowires demonstrated a light absorption spectrum identical to standard cells, but exhibited a 40% reduction in the time required for generated electrons to reach the electrodes.
     B) Nanowire-infused solar cells absorbed 50% more total incoming sunlight across the ultraviolet spectrum compared to standard thin-film solar cells.
     C) The energy conversion efficiency of standard solar cells decreased rapidly when exposed to high surface temperatures, while nanowire cells remained stable.
     D) Incorporating silicon nanowires increased manufacturing costs by 20% but doubled the total operational lifespan of the solar panels in field tests.
     
     Correct Answer: A
     
     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice B is incorrect because it shows the improvement stems from expanded light absorption, which directly contradicts the claim that the mechanism operates via accelerated transport *instead* of absorption.
     * Choice C is incorrect because thermal stability under high temperatures does not isolate electron transit speeds or clarify the precise mechanism of efficiency.
     * Choice D is incorrect because increased production costs and lifespan improvements address commercial durability rather than the physical mechanism of electron conversion kinetics.

     QUESTION 67
     Passage:
     An anthropologist specializing in early human history hypothesized that the transition from a mobile hunter-gatherer lifestyle to a sedentary agricultural lifestyle in Western Asia initially caused a severe decline in overall human health due to dietary monotony. According to the anthropologist, early farmers relied too heavily on a small selection of cereal crops, leading to chronic nutritional deficiencies that were rare among hunter-gatherers who consumed a diverse array of wild plants and animals.
     
     Prompt:
     Which choice, if true, would most directly support the anthropologist's hypothesis?
     
     Options:
     A) Skeletal remains from early agricultural strata in the region displayed a 60% increase in bone lesions associated with iron-deficiency anemia compared to older hunter-gatherer skeletons found in the same area.
     B) Archaeological excavations of early agricultural villages revealed large stone storage bins filled with remnants of domesticated wheat, barley, and lentils.
     C) Skeletons of hunter-gatherers often showed high frequencies of fractures and joint trauma resulting from the physical demands of tracking large game animals across rugged terrain.
     D) DNA analysis indicated that early farming populations expanded rapidly in size, outnumbering neighboring hunter-gatherer groups within a few generations.
     
     Correct Answer: A
     
     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice B is incorrect because discovering grain storage bins proves they cultivated crops, but does not provide pathological evidence that this diet caused a physiological decline in health.
     * Choice C is incorrect because hunting injuries reflect physical hazards of an active lifestyle, rather than chronic nutritional deficiencies stemming from dietary monotony.
     * Choice D is incorrect because rapid population expansion implies demographic success, which does not directly support the claim of severe systemic health and nutritional declines.

     QUESTION 68
     Passage:
     A zoologist hypothesized that male túngara frogs in urban environments produce louder, more complex mating calls than their rural counterparts to overcome ambient city traffic noise, despite this adaptation making them significantly more vulnerable to predatory fringe-lipped bats, which hunt frogs by tracking their vocalizations. The zoologist conducted speaker playback experiments in controlled environments to test bat attraction rates to urban and rural frog call recordings.
     
     Prompt:
     Which choice, if true, would most directly support the zoologist's hypothesis?
     
     Options:
     A) Urban male frogs produced calls that were 15 decibels louder than rural frogs, and predatory bats attacked speakers playing the urban call recordings three times more frequently than speakers playing rural recordings.
     B) Predatory bats completely ignored all frog call recordings when researchers played loud city traffic noise over the experimental chamber's sound system.
     C) Rural male frogs instantly silenced themselves when a mechanical bat model passed overhead, whereas urban frogs continued calling without interruption.
     D) Urban male frogs possessed smaller body sizes on average than rural frogs, allowing them to hide more effectively in shallow puddles.
     
     Correct Answer: A
     
     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice B is incorrect because if bats ignore calls during traffic noise, it undermines the idea that urban frog calls remain effectively vulnerable to bat hunting in actual city environments.
     * Choice C is incorrect because continuing to call around a physical predator suggests a lack of awareness or a behavioral difference, but does not measure acoustic complexity or quantify actual predatory attraction rates.
     * Choice D is incorrect because body size hiding strategies are independent of the vocalization volume and predatory trade-offs outlined in the hypothesis.

     QUESTION 69
     Passage:
     An public policy researcher evaluated the efficacy of an excise tax imposed on sugar-sweetened beverages in an urban city. The researcher hypothesized that the tax successfully reduces consumption of unhealthy drinks among low-income households by increasing prices, while leaving the purchasing habits of high-income households completely unaffected due to their lower sensitivity to minor price changes.
     
     Prompt:
     Which choice, if true, would most directly support the researcher's hypothesis?
     
     Options:
     A) Following the implementation of the tax, sales of sugar-sweetened beverages dropped by 30% in grocery stores located within low-income neighborhoods, but remained completely unchanged in high-income neighborhoods.
     B) Total tax revenue collected from sugar-sweetened beverages increased steadily across all neighborhoods during the first twelve months of the program.
     C) Low-income residents reported that they noticed the price increase but chose to buy untaxed fruit juices that contained identical amounts of sugar.
     D) High-income residents reported that they reduced their overall grocery spending by purchasing generic brands instead of name-brand sugary beverages.
     
     Correct Answer: A
     
     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice B is incorrect because a uniform increase in revenue indicates continued purchasing across the board, failing to prove a targeted drop in low-income consumption.
     * Choice C is incorrect because switching to equally sugary untaxed juices contradicts the premise that the tax successfully reduced the consumption of *unhealthy* drinks for that demographic.
     * Choice D is incorrect because if high-income residents altered their habits to buy generic brands, it refutes the claim that their purchasing habits remained "completely unaffected."

     QUESTION 70
     Passage:
     Geneticists hypothesized that a specific mutation in the *ARX-2* gene provides robust evolutionary resistance to malaria infections, but incurs a severe biological cost by reducing overall reproductive fitness (successful pregnancy rates) when individuals live in environments free from malaria threats. To test this, they compiled long-term health and reproductive records across multiple geographic regions with varying historical malaria exposure rates.
     
     Prompt:
     Which choice, if true, would most directly support the geneticists' hypothesis?
     
     Options:
     A) In regions with high malaria prevalence, individuals carrying the *ARX-2* mutation had a 90% survival rate during outbreaks, but in malaria-free zones, individuals with the mutation had 25% fewer successful pregnancies than those without it.
     B) Individuals carrying the *ARX-2* mutation exhibited a uniform 15% reduction in successful pregnancy rates regardless of whether they lived in high-malaria or malaria-free environments.
     C) The *ARX-2* mutation was found to be incredibly rare across all geographic regions, appearing only in populations that had migrated away from coastal wetlands.
     D) In malaria-free zones, individuals with the mutation experienced higher overall life expectancies because the mutation protected them from other infectious diseases.
     
     Correct Answer: A
     
     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice B is incorrect because a uniform reduction in pregnancy rates without showing heightened survival advantages during active outbreaks fails to demonstrate the evolutionary trade-off of *resistance* in threat zones.
     * Choice C is incorrect because the rarity or migration history of a population does not provide direct physiological data on disease resistance or reproductive fitness metrics.
     * Choice D is incorrect because if the mutation increases life expectancy in malaria-free zones, it directly contradicts the idea that the mutation incurs a severe biological cost under normal conditions.

     QUESTION 71
     Passage:
     The following text is adapted from a literary critique of absolute realism in 20th-century political novels.
     Critics often argue that multi-perspective narrative structures are employed primarily to mirror the psychological interiority and fragmented subjectivities of modern characters. However, a close analysis of Sophia Sterling’s political novels suggests an alternative objective. Sterling’s shifting perspectives do not merely catalog private emotional states; rather, they function as a deliberate mechanism to destabilize the reader's trust in institutional authority. By juxtaposing the highly polished, self-serving accounts of official bureaucrats with the raw, conflicting recollections of marginalized citizens, Sterling avoids providing an objective, authoritative narrative voice, thereby forcing the reader to recognize that historical truth is an artifact of political power.
     
     Prompt:
     Which choice provides the most direct textual evidence to support the critic's alternative interpretation of Sterling's novels?
     
     Options:
     A) In Sterling’s *The Iron Gavel*, a high-ranking judge delivers a flawless public speech defending a state execution, followed immediately by a chapter composed of contradictory diary entries from three separate witnesses that expose the judge's systemic corruption.
     B) In Sterling’s *Shadows of the Plaza*, a young factory worker spends several chapters reflecting deeply on his childhood memories, concluding that his internal sense of isolation is entirely unrelated to the ongoing political strike.
     C) In Sterling’s *The Ledger*, an omniscient, detached narrator provides a meticulous, chronological record of a city council meeting, ensuring that every politician's statement is reported with absolute clarity and neutrality.
     D) In Sterling’s *Whispers of Revolution*, a political activist delivers a long, uninterrupted monologue that convinces all characters, regardless of their social class, to accept a single, unified view of historical events.
     
     Correct Answer: A
     
     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice B is incorrect because the character's reflections focus on private childhood memories unconnected to political dynamics, which aligns with the *traditional* psychological interpretation that the critic is explicitly rejecting.
     * Choice C is incorrect because an omniscient, neutral narrator providing a clear, chronological record directly contradicts Sterling's use of shifting, unstable multi-perspective structures.
     * Choice D is incorrect because a single monologue that creates a unified, universally accepted view undermines the core premise that the text avoids a singular authoritative voice to challenge institutional narratives.

     QUESTION 72
     Passage:
     In modern cosmology, the prevailing Lambda-CDM model characterizes dark energy as a "cosmological constant"—a static, unaltering vacuum energy density inherent to space that accelerates cosmic expansion at a perfectly uniform rate across time. However, proponents of alternative "quintessence" frameworks argue that dark energy is not a static constant but rather a dynamic, evolving scalar field whose energy density and accelerating influence fluctuate over cosmic epochs. To adjudicate between these paradigms, astrophysicists analyzed precision high-redshift data from Type Ia supernovae to map the rate of cosmic acceleration across the universe's 13.8-billion-year history.
     
     Prompt:
     Which choice, if true, would most directly support the dynamic "quintessence" framework over the traditional cosmological constant model?
     
     Options:
     A) The supernova data revealed that the rate of cosmic acceleration was significantly slower 8 billion years ago than it is today, demonstrating a clear variation in dark energy's influence across different historical epochs.
     B) The data confirmed that the energy density of dark energy remains precisely fixed at 10 to the power of minus 29 grams per cubic centimeter across all measured spatial coordinates and time intervals.
     C) Cosmological observations indicated that the rate of cosmic expansion is perfectly balanced by the gravitational attraction exerted by baryonic matter and static dark matter structures.
     D) Computer models showed that if dark energy were completely dynamic, the structural formation of early galaxies would have been delayed by several billion years.
     
     Correct Answer: A
     
     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice B is incorrect because a precisely fixed, unaltering energy density perfectly validates the static "cosmological constant" model, directly refuting the quintessence framework.
     * Choice C is incorrect because a balance between expansion and matter gravity does not address whether the expansion force itself fluctuates over time or remains constant.
     * Choice D is incorrect because showing a negative consequence of a dynamic model within a simulation does not provide empirical evidence that the physical universe actually exhibits fluctuating dark energy rates.

     QUESTION 73
     Passage:
     The "handicap principle" in evolutionary biology posits that elaborate male secondary sexual ornaments, such as the cumbersome tail of a peacock, are maintained by sexual selection because they function as "honest signals" of superior genetic quality. According to this framework, these ornaments are biologically costly to produce and maintain; therefore, only individuals with robust health and low parasite loads can afford to develop them without dying. Unhealthy or genetically inferior males cannot fake these signals because the physiological stress of producing the ornament would compromise their survival. To test this, researchers evaluated offspring survival across various male phenotypes under high-stress conditions.
     
     Prompt:
     Which choice, if true, would most directly support the honest signaling framework outlined by the handicap principle?
     
     Options:
     A) Offspring sired by males with naturally elaborate ornaments exhibited exceptional immune responses and high survival rates when exposed to parasites, even when raised by infected foster mothers, whereas artificially gluing larger ornaments onto low-quality males resulted in highly vulnerable offspring with high mortality rates.
     B) Male birds with smaller, less colorful ornaments suffered significantly lower predation rates in the wild, allowing them to produce a higher total volume of offspring over their lifespans compared to highly ornate males.
     C) When researchers administered a nutrient-rich diet to low-quality males, those males easily developed massive, vibrant ornaments that were visually indistinguishable from those of high-quality males without experiencing any reduction in lifespan.
     D) Parasite loads across the entire bird population fluctuated in response to seasonal rainfall variations, affecting ornate and non-ornate males to an identical degree.
     
     Correct Answer: A
     
     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice B is incorrect because if simple males produce more offspring over time due to low predation, it outlines a selective advantage *against* elaborate ornaments, failing to explain why expensive traits persist as honest quality indicators.
     * Choice C is incorrect because if low-quality individuals can easily fake the signal via a brief dietary shift without a survival penalty, it directly disproves the premise that the trait is an un-fakable, honest indicator of underlying genetic quality.
     * Choice D is incorrect because a uniform seasonal impact across all males fails to show a correlation between individual ornament size and specific, heritable parasite resistance.

     QUESTION 74
     Passage:
     The neuropeptide oxytocin has historically been celebrated in behavioral neuroscience as a universal catalyst for empathy, pro-social behavior, and altruism. However, a group of researchers has proposed the "in-group/out-group salience" hypothesis. They contend that oxytocin does not promote generalized global benevolence; instead, it sharpens the cognitive boundaries between social groups. According to this alternative model, oxytocin selectively amplifies trust, cooperation, and empathy toward familiar in-group allies while simultaneously increasing defensive aggression, xenophobia, and non-cooperation when interacting with unfamiliar out-group rivals.
     
     Prompt:
     Which choice, if true, would most directly support the researchers' in-group/out-group salience hypothesis?
     
     Options:
     A) Participants administered oxytocin exhibited elevated levels of trust and financial sharing during a game when paired with assigned teammates, but demonstrated a marked increase in unprovoked financial penalization and hostility when interacting with members of a competing rival team compared to a placebo group.
     B) Oxytocin administration caused participants to distribute financial rewards completely equally among all individuals in the experiment, regardless of whether those individuals belonged to their assigned team or a rival team.
     C) Neuroimaging scans revealed that oxytocin uniformly suppressed activity in the amygdala across all participants, resulting in a generalized reduction in social anxiety and fear when meeting strangers from diverse backgrounds.
     D) Participants who naturally produced high baseline levels of oxytocin scored exceptionally high on standardized empathy questionnaires that measured reactions to fictional characters in neutral settings.
     
     Correct Answer: A
     
     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice B is incorrect because equal distribution across teams supports the *traditional* view of universal benevolence, directly contradicting the selective in-group/out-group bias hypothesis.
     * Choice C is incorrect because a uniform reduction in anxiety and fear when meeting strangers outlines a global pro-social easing effect, failing to show the heightened defensive aggression toward out-groups predicted by the model.
     * Choice D is incorrect because empathetic responses to fictional characters in neutral settings do not test or demonstrate polarized behaviors based on explicit social group divisions.

     QUESTION 75
     Passage:
     Traditional archeological narratives frequently attribute the catastrophic collapse of Late Bronze Age civilizations in the Eastern Mediterranean around 1200 BCE to a prolonged, region-wide mega-drought that devastated agricultural systems and induced mass starvation. However, an alternative hypothesis suggests that the collapse was primarily a socio-economic phenomenon triggered by a systemic disruption of maritime trade networks. Proponents of this view argue that the elite political structures of these civilizations were fragilely dependent on the continuous importation of exotic raw materials, such as tin and copper, to maintain their political legitimacy and military apparatus.
     
     Prompt:
     Which choice, if true, would most directly support the alternative socio-economic trade disruption hypothesis over the traditional drought narrative?
     
     Options:
     A) High-resolution pollen and sediment core analyses from the collapse window reveal stable, historically normal rainfall levels and agricultural yields, whereas contemporary shipwreck inventories and palace tablets show an abrupt, absolute cessation in the importation of metal ingots at major urban ports.
     B) Historical records confirm that severe crop failures and famines occurred simultaneously across Egypt, Mycenae, and the Hittite Empire, forcing major cities to abandon trade entirely to focus on local foraging.
     C) Archeologists discovered massive hoards of bronze weapons buried outside city walls, indicating that local militaries possessed an overabundance of copper and tin during the final years of the civilization.
     D) Climate simulations indicated that even if a mega-drought had occurred, Eastern Mediterranean civilizations possessed sophisticated irrigation networks that could completely neutralize agricultural losses for decades.
     
     Correct Answer: A
     
     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice B is incorrect because confirming widespread crop failures and famines directly reinforces the traditional *drought and starvation* narrative, rather than isolating trade disruption as an independent cause.
     * Choice C is incorrect because an overabundance of copper and tin weapons contradicts the claim that a lack of imported raw metals crippled the military and political apparatus.
     * Choice D is incorrect because a simulation showing that irrigation *could* neutralize a drought does not provide physical evidence that a drought did not happen, nor does it prove that a maritime trade stoppage occurred in reality.

     QUESTION 76
     Passage:
     Critics of Universal Basic Income (UBI) programs frequently argue that providing unconditional cash transfers to citizens incentivizes labor market exit, predicting a substantial drop in economic productivity as recipients reduce their working hours. Conversely, behavioral economists hypothesize that UBI functions as an entrepreneurial catalyst by mitigating the existential financial risks associated with starting a new business venture. They contend that when individuals possess a guaranteed financial safety net, they are more likely to allocate labor toward high-risk, high-reward innovations.
     
     Prompt:
     Which choice, if true, would most directly support the behavioral economists' hypothesis?
     
     Options:
     A) Participants in a multi-year UBI pilot program maintained their baseline working hours at their existing primary jobs, but registered new business startups and filed patent applications at a rate three times higher than a demographic control group of non-recipients.
     B) Following the introduction of the cash transfers, over 45% of UBI recipients completely resigned from their employment positions to spend more time on leisure activities and personal travel.
     C) Economic data revealed that UBI recipients spent the majority of their unconditional cash transfers on immediate consumption goods, such as groceries and rent, rather than investing in financial stocks.
     D) Surveys indicated that business owners in regions without UBI programs were significantly more profitable than business owners operating within UBI pilot zones.
     
     Correct Answer: A
     
     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice B is incorrect because a massive resignation for leisure directly validates the critics' warning about labor market exit, refuting the behavioral economists' entrepreneurial hypothesis.
     * Choice C is incorrect because spending funds on immediate consumption goods like groceries and rent fails to show that the program acts as an innovative or entrepreneurial catalyst.
     * Choice D is incorrect because lower profitability for businesses within UBI zones suggests a negative regional economic impact, which undermines rather than supports the economists' positive thesis.

     QUESTION 77
     Passage:
     When attacked by herbivorous insects, many plant species emit volatile organic compounds (VOCs) into the surrounding air. For decades, plant ecologists interpreted this phenomenon as an altruistic warning mechanism evolved to alert neighboring plants of impending danger, allowing them to proactively elevate their chemical defenses. However, an alternative evolutionary model suggests that VOC emissions are fundamentally a selfish trait designed to recruit predatory insects. According to this model, the volatile compounds function as airborne chemical homing signals that attract carnivorous wasps or mites that actively consume and neutralize the attacking herbivores, with any warning provided to neighboring foliage being merely an incidental byproduct.
     
     Prompt:
     Which choice, if true, would most directly support the alternative selfish predator-recruitment model over the altruistic warning model?
     
     Options:
     A) Damaged plants placed in sealed airflow chambers that completely prevented their VOCs from reaching neighboring foliage still experienced a 65% reduction in herbivore damage due to an immediate influx of parasitic wasps attracted by the scent.
     B) Neighboring plants exposed to VOC emissions immediately synthesized high concentrations of bitter tannins that successfully prevented caterpillars from consuming their leaves.
     C) Mutant plants engineered to be incapable of producing VOC emissions grew significantly larger and produced more seeds than wild-type plants when grown in predator-free environments.
     D) Carnivorous mites were found to avoid plants that emitted high levels of VOCs, preferring instead to hunt on undamaged, odorless foliage where prey visibility was higher.
     
     Correct Answer: A
     
     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice B is incorrect because neighboring plants successfully synthesizing defensive tannins in response to VOCs directly validates the altruistic warning model.
     * Choice C is incorrect because growth advantages in a predator-free environment demonstrate the metabolic cost of producing the chemical, but do not adjudicate between whether the function is to warn neighbors or recruit predators.
     * Choice D is incorrect because predators actively *avoiding* VOC emitting plants directly refutes the predator-recruitment model.

     QUESTION 78
     Passage:
     A long-standing debate in cognitive science concerns whether human facial recognition operates via holistic configuration processing (analyzing the spatial relationships of the entire face simultaneously) or via piecemeal feature analysis (deconstructing the face into isolated individual parts like an eye or nose). To isolate the mechanism, researchers designed a study measuring recognition accuracy when faces were presented upright versus when they were inverted (turned upside down). Crucially, inversion preserves all individual piecemeal features perfectly but severely disrupts the brain's ability to perceive holistic spatial configurations.
     
     Prompt:
     Which choice, if true, would most directly support the holistic configuration processing model?
     
     Options:
     A) Participants identified familiar faces with 95% accuracy when presented upright, but their recognition performance dropped to near-chance levels when the faces were inverted, despite all individual features remaining perfectly clear and visible.
     B) Recognition accuracy remained high and completely unchanged regardless of whether the faces were presented upright or inverted, provided the eyes retained their original color.
     C) Participants with localized brain damage were completely unable to recognize isolated noses or mouths, but instantly identified complete faces when shown in an inverted position.
     D) Computerized facial recognition software utilized piecemeal feature analysis to identify individuals with equal efficiency across both upright and inverted image formats.
     
     Correct Answer: A
     
     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice B is incorrect because if performance remains unchanged when inverted, it indicates the brain relies on piecemeal features that survive inversion, directly refuting the holistic model.
     * Choice C is incorrect because failing to recognize isolated features while succeeding on inverted faces contradicts the premise that inversion disrupts holistic processing, describing an anomalous pathological condition instead.
     * Choice D is incorrect because the operational parameters of computer software algorithms do not provide empirical evidence regarding the biological cognitive mechanisms of the human brain.

     QUESTION 79
     Passage:
     In the sociology of science, Max Planck famously posited that revolutionary scientific paradigms do not triumph because individual established researchers change their minds and are gradually convinced by new empirical data. Instead, Planck asserted that paradigms shift because older generations of scientists who hold entrenched views eventually retire and pass away, allowing a new generation of researchers who are accustomed to the alternative framework to ascend to institutional prominence (a concept termed "Planck's Principle").
     
     Prompt:
     Which choice, if true, would most directly support Planck's Principle during a major historical scientific revolution?
     
     Options:
     A) Citation analyses revealed that senior scientists who published papers rejecting the new theory continued to do so throughout their entire careers, while the macro-level adoption rate of the paradigm grew in direct proportion to the hiring of newly graduated PhD faculty members.
     B) Historical letters demonstrate that over 80% of established senior scientists completely abandoned their previous publications and signed a public manifesto endorsing the new paradigm within two years of its discovery.
     C) University records showed that funding for research projects utilizing the old scientific paradigm increased substantially as older faculty members reached the peak of their administrative power.
     D) A comprehensive survey indicated that young researchers abandoned the new paradigm and reverted to traditional theories whenever they were mentored by senior faculty members.
     
     Correct Answer: A
     
     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice B is incorrect because senior scientists rapidly changing their minds and endorsing the new paradigm directly refutes Planck's Principle, validating a data-driven persuasion model instead.
     * Choice C is incorrect because increasing funding for the old paradigm shows institutional entrenchment, but does not track the generational replacement mechanism required to prove a paradigm shift according to Planck.
     * Choice D is incorrect because young researchers reverting to old theories when mentored by seniors outlines a mechanism of conservative continuity, which prevents rather than explains a revolutionary paradigm shift.
