     QUESTION 80
     Passage:
     Microclimatologists investigating the "urban heat island" effect—where cities experience significantly higher temperatures than surrounding rural areas—debated the primary physical driver of this phenomenon. Traditional theories attribute the temperature disparity to the thermal mass of engineering materials, arguing that asphalt and concrete absorb and retain solar radiation far more efficiently than natural soil. Conversely, an alternative hypothesis suggests that the primary driver is the systematic reduction in evapo-transpirative cooling resulting from the removal of vegetation canopies.
     
     Prompt:
     Which choice, if true, would most directly support the alternative vegetation canopy hypothesis over the traditional material thermal mass theory?
     
     Options:
     A) High-density urban neighborhoods featuring extensive concrete infrastructure but dense street-tree canopies exhibited summer surface temperatures identical to rural forest baselines, whereas urban zones with low canopy cover but highly reflective "cool pavement" materials remained significantly hotter.
     B) Thermal imaging data confirmed that dark asphalt parking lots retained heat for up to six hours after sunset, causing localized air temperatures to remain elevated throughout the night.
     C) Rural agricultural zones experience rapid temperature drops during winter months because bare soil lacks the capacity to retain heat in the absence of crop cover.
     D) Microclimatic models indicated that replacing all urban concrete structures with natural soil would reduce a city's average summer surface temperature by 85% within one week.
     
     Correct Answer: A
     
     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice B is incorrect because demonstrating that dark asphalt retains heat for hours directly supports the traditional *material thermal mass* theory, rather than isolating vegetation canopy as the primary driver.
     * Choice C is incorrect because winter temperature drops in rural fields do not provide comparative data isolating the causal mechanics of urban heat islands during peak summer periods.
     * Choice D is incorrect because a model stating that replacing concrete with soil works perfectly reinforces the material mass theory, directly undermining the alternative vegetation canopy hypothesis.

• Command of Evidence (Quantitative)
     -----------------------------------------------------------------
     [DIFFICULTY LEVEL: LOW - QUESTIONS 81-90]
     
     QUESTION 81
     Passage:
     A botanist conducted an experiment to see how different types of organic fertilizer affect the height of sunflower plants over a four-week period. The botanist divided identical seedlings into four groups, giving each group a different fertilizer type (A, B, C, or D) while keeping water and sunlight conditions exactly the same. The botanist claims that Fertilizer C is the most effective at increasing sunflower height.
     
     Table: Average Sunflower Height (cm) After Four Weeks
     | Fertilizer Type | Average Height (cm) |
     |-----------------|---------------------|
     | Type A          | 42.5                |
     | Type B          | 38.1                |
     | Type C          | 54.8                |
     | Type D          | 40.2                |
     
     Prompt:
     Which choice best uses data from the table to support the botanist's claim?
     
     Options:
     A) Sunflowers given Type C fertilizer reached an average height of 54.8 cm, which was higher than the average height of any other group.
     B) Sunflowers given Type B fertilizer were the shortest on average, measuring only 38.1 cm at the end of the four weeks.
     C) The average height of sunflowers given Type A fertilizer was 42.5 cm, which was higher than the height of those given Type D.
     D) Sunflowers given Type D fertilizer grew to an average height of 40.2 cm, outperforming those given Type B fertilizer.
     
     Correct Answer: A
     
     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice B is incorrect because stating that Type B produced the shortest plants does not provide direct evidence supporting the claim that Type C is the *most effective*.
     * Choice C is incorrect because comparing Type A and Type D is irrelevant to validating the effectiveness of Type C.
     * Choice D is incorrect because comparing Type D and Type B fails to provide data regarding Type C's superior performance.

     -----------------------------------------------------------------
     
     QUESTION 82
     Passage:
     A city planner tracked the average number of daily visitors to three different public parks during the summer and winter seasons to determine if seasonal changes affect park utilization uniformly. The planner asserts that while all three parks experience a decline in visitors during the winter, Oakridge Park retains the highest number of daily visitors regardless of the season.
     
     Table: Average Daily Visitors by Season
     | Park Name       | Summer Visitors | Winter Visitors |
     |-----------------|-----------------|-----------------|
     | Oakridge Park   | 1,200           | 450             |
     | Lakeside Park   | 950             | 310             |
     | Riverview Park  | 800             | 250             |
     
     Prompt:
     Which choice best uses data from the table to support the city planner's assertion?
     
     Options:
     A) Lakeside Park had 950 daily visitors in the summer, which dropped to 310 visitors in the winter.
     B) Oakridge Park had 1,200 summer visitors and 450 winter visitors, both of which are higher than the respective totals for Lakeside and Riverview parks.
     C) Riverview Park had the lowest attendance in both seasons, with 800 visitors in the summer and 250 in the winter.
     D) The total number of visitors to all three parks combined was significantly higher in the summer than in the winter.
     
     Correct Answer: B
     
     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice A is incorrect because it provides data exclusively for Lakeside Park, failing to demonstrate Oakridge Park's relative success.
     * Choice C is incorrect because stating that Riverview Park has the lowest attendance does not directly confirm that Oakridge Park has the *highest* baseline across both seasons.
     * Choice D is incorrect because summarizing total aggregate seasonal attendance does not isolate or validate Oakridge Park's individual seasonal performance.

     -----------------------------------------------------------------
     
     QUESTION 83
     Passage:
     An environmental scientist measured the average amount of electricity generated daily by three different models of residential solar panels (Model X, Model Y, and Model Z) under cloudy and sunny weather conditions. The scientist claims that Model Y is uniquely resilient to poor weather, generating more electricity on cloudy days than either of the other two models generate under identical cloudy conditions.
     
     Table: Average Daily Electricity Generation (kWh)
     | Panel Model     | Sunny Days | Cloudy Days |
     |-----------------|------------|-------------|
     | Model X         | 15.2       | 6.4         |
     | Model Y         | 14.8       | 8.9         |
     | Model Z         | 16.1       | 5.1         |
     
     Prompt:
     Which choice best uses data from the table to support the scientist's claim?
     
     Options:
     A) Model Z generated the highest amount of electricity on sunny days, reaching 16.1 kWh.
     B) Model X generated 15.2 kWh on sunny days and dropped to 6.4 kWh on cloudy days.
     C) Model Y generated 8.9 kWh on cloudy days, which is higher than the 6.4 kWh for Model X and 5.1 kWh for Model Z.
     D) All three solar panel models generated less than 10 kWh of electricity on days with heavy cloud cover.
     
     Correct Answer: C
     
     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice A is incorrect because sunny day performance for Model Z does not address Model Y's performance under cloudy conditions.
     * Choice B is incorrect because tracking Model X's performance dropdown does not evaluate Model Y's superior comparative resilience.
     * Choice D is incorrect because a general statement that all models fall below 10 kWh fails to highlight Model Y's relative advantage over its competitors.

     -----------------------------------------------------------------
     
     QUESTION 84
     Passage:
     A student is investigating the water retention capabilities of four common household soil additives: peat moss, perlite, vermiculite, and compost. The student mixes equal amounts of each additive into separate pots of dry soil, pours 500 mL of water into each pot, and measures how much water drains out the bottom after 10 minutes. The student claims that peat moss is the most effective additive at retaining water within the soil matrix.
     
     Table: Water Drained After 10 Minutes (mL)
     | Soil Additive   | Water Drained (mL) |
     |-----------------|--------------------|
     | Peat Moss       | 85                 |
     | Perlite         | 340                |
     | Vermiculite     | 190                |
     | Compost         | 120                |
     
     Prompt:
     Which choice best uses data from the table to support the student's claim?
     
     Options:
     A) Pots containing perlite allowed 340 mL of water to drain out, indicating a very low retention rate.
     B) Pots containing peat moss allowed only 85 mL of water to drain out, which was the lowest volume recorded among the additives.
     C) Vermiculite allowed 190 mL to drain, which was more water than what drained from pots with compost.
     D) The total volume of water poured into each experimental soil pot was exactly 500 mL.
     
     Correct Answer: B
     
     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice A is incorrect because outlining perlite's low retention rate does not prove that peat moss has the highest retention rate.
     * Choice C is incorrect because comparing vermiculite and compost is irrelevant to supporting a claim focused specifically on peat moss.
     * Choice D is incorrect because repeating a fixed baseline methodology parameter provides no analytical evidence regarding the experimental outcome.

     -----------------------------------------------------------------
     
     QUESTION 85
     Passage:
     A nutritionist compared the sugar content per serving across four popular brands of breakfast cereal (Brands W, X, Y, and Z) to evaluate options for a low-sugar diet program. The nutritionist notes that while Brand W has a reputation for being an unhealthy choice, it actually contains less sugar per serving than Brand Z.
     
     Table: Sugar Content per Cereal Serving (grams)
     | Cereal Brand    | Sugar per Serving (g) |
     |-----------------|-----------------------|
     | Brand W         | 9.2                   |
     | Brand X         | 4.5                   |
     | Brand Y         | 2.1                   |
     | Brand Z         | 11.8                  |
     
     Prompt:
     Which choice best uses data from the table to support the nutritionist's note?
     
     Options:
     A) Brand Y contained the absolute lowest amount of sugar per serving, measuring just 2.1 grams.
     B) Brand X contained 4.5 grams of sugar per serving, making it healthier than Brand W.
     C) Brand Z contained 11.8 grams of sugar per serving, while Brand W contained 9.2 grams per serving.
     D) Brand W and Brand Z both contained more than twice the amount of sugar found in Brand X.
     
     Correct Answer: C
     
     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice A is incorrect because highlighting Brand Y's minimal sugar levels does not evaluate the specific comparison between Brand W and Brand Z.
     * Choice B is incorrect because comparing Brand X to Brand W does not confirm that Brand W is lower in sugar than Brand Z.
     * Choice D is incorrect because stating that both exceed Brand X's levels fails to specify their relative relationship to one another.

     -----------------------------------------------------------------
     
     QUESTION 86
     Passage:
     A marine biologist tracked the diving habits of three specific marine mammal species—the harbor seal, the sea otter, and the elephant seal—to compare their average maximum dive depths. The biologist hypothesized that species with larger body masses generally achieve much deeper maximum dives than species with smaller body masses.
     
     Table: Average Mass and Maximum Dive Depth
     | Species Name    | Average Mass (kg) | Max Dive Depth (m) |
     |-----------------|-------------------|--------------------|
     | Sea Otter       | 35                | 55                 |
     | Harbor Seal     | 100               | 450                |
     | Elephant Seal   | 2,000             | 1,500              |
     
     Prompt:
     Which choice best uses data from the table to support the biologist's hypothesis?
     
     Options:
     A) The sea otter has an average mass of 35 kg and reaches a maximum dive depth of 55 meters.
     B) The elephant seal, which has the largest average mass at 2,000 kg, achieved the deepest maximum dive depth at 1,500 meters.
     C) The harbor seal is heavier than the sea otter but lighter than the elephant seal.
     D) Marine mammals can remain underwater for extended periods regardless of their average maximum depth profiles.
     
     Correct Answer: B
     
     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice A is incorrect because listing data solely for the smallest species does not establish a positive correlation between increasing mass and increasing depth.
     * Choice C is incorrect because stating a mass hierarchy without linking it directly to dive depth outcomes fails to support the hypothesis.
     * Choice D is incorrect because an unquantified assertion about underwater duration is irrelevant to the specific variables tracking mass and dive depths.

     -----------------------------------------------------------------
     
     QUESTION 87
     Passage:
     An agricultural extension agent measured the crop yields of three distinct heirloom tomato varieties (Cherokee Purple, Brandywine, and San Marzano) across plots using traditional tillage versus no-tillage farming practices. The agent claims that the San Marzano variety yields more fruit when grown using no-tillage practices than when grown using traditional tillage.
     
     Table: Average Tomato Yield per Plot (lbs)
     | Tomato Variety   | Traditional Tillage | No-Tillage Practices |
     |------------------|---------------------|----------------------|
     | Cherokee Purple  | 145                 | 130                  |
     | Brandywine       | 112                 | 115                  |
     | San Marzano      | 160                 | 185                  |
     
     Prompt:
     Which choice best uses data from the table to support the agent's claim?
     
     Options:
     A) Cherokee Purple yielded 145 lbs under traditional tillage, which dropped to 130 lbs under no-tillage.
     B) Brandywine yields were relatively stable, showing 112 lbs under traditional tillage and 115 lbs under no-tillage.
     C) San Marzano plots produced 185 lbs of fruit under no-tillage practices compared to 160 lbs under traditional tillage.
     D) San Marzano produced the highest overall yield under traditional tillage compared to the other two varieties.
     
     Correct Answer: C
     
     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice A is incorrect because the data for Cherokee Purple contradicts the pattern claimed for San Marzano and addresses the wrong variety.
     * Choice B is incorrect because Brandywine's data does not provide evidence regarding the San Marzano variety's performance.
     * Choice D is incorrect because evaluating traditional tillage performance across varieties fails to validate the claim that San Marzano improves *specifically under no-tillage*.

     -----------------------------------------------------------------
     
     QUESTION 88
     Passage:
     A consumer electronics reviewer tested the operational battery life of four wireless headphone brands under two configurations: Active Noise Cancellation (ANC) turned ON and ANC turned OFF. The reviewer asserts that Brand K experiences the most severe percentage drop in battery life when ANC is activated.
     
     Table: Average Battery Life (Hours)
     | Headphone Brand  | ANC Off | ANC On |
     |------------------|---------|--------|
     | Brand J          | 30      | 25     |
     | Brand K          | 24      | 12     |
     | Brand L          | 40      | 35     |
     | Brand M          | 20      | 18     |
     
     Prompt:
     Which choice best uses data from the table to support the reviewer's assertion?
     
     Options:
     A) Brand L maintained the longest overall battery life, lasting 40 hours with ANC off and 35 hours with ANC on.
     B) Brand K's battery life was cut in half from 24 hours to 12 hours when ANC was activated, a larger relative decrease than any other brand.
     C) Brand M lasted 20 hours with ANC off, which was only 2 hours longer than its runtime with ANC on.
     D) Turning ANC off resulted in a uniform battery runtime of over 20 hours across all four headphone brands tested.
     
     Correct Answer: B
     
     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice A is incorrect because Brand L's top longevity performance does not support the assertion about Brand K's severe drop rate.
     * Choice C is incorrect because citing Brand M's minor 2-hour drop does not isolate or prove Brand K's maximum percentage decrease.
     * Choice D is incorrect because summarizing a general baseline parameter across brands fails to calculate or compare individual activation penalty drops.

     -----------------------------------------------------------------
     
     QUESTION 89
     Passage:
     An amateur astronomer recorded the number of meteors visible per hour during a celestial meteor shower from three distinct observation altitudes: sea level, a foothills balcony (500 m), and a mountain ridge (2,500 m). The astronomer hypothesized that atmospheric interference at lower altitudes limits visibility, meaning that meteor count increases consistently with observation altitude.
     
     Table: Meteors Detected per Hour by Location
     | Observation Site | Altitude (m) | Meteors per Hour |
     |------------------|--------------|------------------|
     | Sea Level Bay    | 0            | 12               |
     | Foothills Station| 500          | 28               |
     | Mountain Ridge   | 2,500        | 65               |
     
     Prompt:
     Which choice best uses data from the table to support the astronomer's hypothesis?
     
     Options:
     A) Only 12 meteors were detected per hour at the Sea Level Bay site.
     B) The meteor count rose from 12 at sea level, to 28 at 500 meters, and reached a peak of 65 at 2,500 meters.
     C) Foothills Station detected more than double the number of meteors recorded at the Sea Level Bay site.
     D) Observations at high altitudes are generally more expensive due to equipment transportation challenges.
     
     Correct Answer: B
     
     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice A is incorrect because isolating the sea level count does not demonstrate a multi-point upward correlation across ascending altitudes.
     * Choice C is incorrect because while it shows a single-step increase from sea level to 500m, it leaves out the critical 2,500m mountain data that confirms the full hypothesis.
     * Choice D is incorrect because economic transportation costs are completely irrelevant to the physical data tracking meteor visibility.

     -----------------------------------------------------------------
     
     QUESTION 90
     Passage:
     A geologist measured the rate of soil erosion on hillsides with varying amounts of plant root density to evaluate land stability measures. The geologist hypothesized that hillsides with thick grass cover would experience significantly less soil runoff during a rainstorm than hillsides with sparse or no vegetation.
     
     Table: Soil Runoff (kg) and Vegetation Density
     | Plot Category    | Vegetation Cover % | Average Soil Runoff (kg) |
     |------------------|--------------------|---------------------------|
     | Bare Earth       | 0%                 | 84.5                      |
     | Sparse Shrubs    | 25%                | 42.1                      |
     | Dense Grass      | 85%                | 5.2                       |
     
     Prompt:
     Which choice best uses data from the table to support the geologist's hypothesis?
     
     Options:
     A) Plots covered with sparse shrubs had 25% vegetation cover and resulted in 42.1 kg of average soil runoff.
     B) Bare Earth plots experienced an average soil runoff of 84.5 kg during the experimental rainstorm.
     C) Dense Grass plots, which had 85% vegetation cover, lost only 5.2 kg of soil, far less than the 84.5 kg lost by Bare Earth plots.
     D) Increasing vegetation cover from 0% to 25% halved the total volume of average soil runoff recorded by the team.
     
     Correct Answer: C
     
     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice A is incorrect because isolating the sparse shrubs middle tier does not compare the high density grass benefit against the low density danger.
     * Choice B is incorrect because stating the bare earth erosion baseline fails to integrate the protective effect of dense grass cover.
     * Choice D is incorrect because tracking the initial step from 0% to 25% ignores the dense grass plot group (85%) which forms the core of the hypothesis.

     [DIFFICULTY LEVEL: MEDIUM-LOW - QUESTIONS 91-100]
     
     QUESTION 91
     Passage:
     An economist investigated the relationship between local minimum wage increases and employment numbers within the fast-food sector across four neighboring counties (Counties 1, 2, 3, and 4) over a two-year period. Critics argued that raising the minimum wage would force restaurants to lay off workers, resulting in a net decrease in fast-food employment. The economist, however, hypothesized that modest wage increases do not automatically lead to job losses and can coexist with stable or expanding employment counts.
     
     Table: Wage and Fast-Food Employment Changes
     | County   | Minimum Wage Change | Fast-Food Employment Change |
     |----------|---------------------|------------------------------|
     | County 1 | +$0.50 / hour        | +4.2% Growth                 |
     | County 2 | +$1.50 / hour        | +1.8% Growth                 |
     | County 3 | No Change            | -0.5% Decline                |
     | County 4 | +$2.50 / hour        | -3.1% Decline                |
     
     Prompt:
     Which choice best uses data from the table to support the economist's hypothesis?
     
     Options:
     A) County 4 instituted the largest minimum wage increase (+$2.50) and experienced a 3.1% decline in fast-food employment.
     B) Counties 1 and 2 both enacted minimum wage increases yet saw positive job growth of 4.2% and 1.8% respectively, proving job losses are not automatic.
     C) County 3 maintained its baseline minimum wage constant and experienced a minor 0.5% decline in its fast-food employment sector.
     D) Fast-food employment grew faster in County 1 than in any other county listed in the economist's two-year dataset.
     
     Correct Answer: B
     
     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice A is incorrect because County 4's data validates the *critics' argument* (wage hike leading to job losses), thereby failing to support the economist's counter-hypothesis.
     * Choice C is incorrect because outlining a decline in a county with no wage change does not prove that wage increases themselves can coexist with job growth.
     * Choice D is incorrect because simply stating that County 1 grew the fastest misses the structural link showing that it grew *despite/alongside* an explicit minimum wage increase.

     -----------------------------------------------------------------
     
     QUESTION 92
     Passage:
     A climatologist studied the carbon sequestration efficiency (how much CO2 is absorbed per square kilometer) of four distinct forest ecosystems: tropical rainforest, temperate deciduous forest, boreal coniferous forest, and coastal mangrove forest. The researcher hypothesized that while tropical rainforests absorb the largest total volume of carbon globally due to their vast geographic size, coastal mangrove forests are significantly more efficient on a per-square-kilometer basis.
     
     Table: Forest Carbon Sequestration Data
     | Forest Ecosystem    | Global Area (million km²) | CO2 Absorbed per km² (tons/year) |
     |---------------------|---------------------------|----------------------------------|
     | Tropical Rainforest | 12.4                      | 2,100                            |
     | Temperate Deciduous | 8.1                       | 1,350                            |
     | Boreal Coniferous   | 15.2                      | 980                              |
     | Coastal Mangrove    | 0.15                      | 4,500                            |
     
     Prompt:
     Which choice best uses data from the table to support the climatologist's hypothesis?
     
     Options:
     A) Boreal coniferous forests blanket the largest global area at 15.2 million km² but absorb only 980 tons of CO2 per km² each year.
     |B) Tropical rainforests cover 12.4 million km² and sequester 2,100 tons per km², which represents the highest total global volume.
     C) Coastal mangrove forests occupy just 0.15 million km² but sequester 4,500 tons of CO2 per km² per year, more than double the per-km² rate of tropical rainforests.
     D) Temperate deciduous forests exhibit an efficiency of 1,350 tons per km², making them more efficient than boreal coniferous forests.
     
     Correct Answer: C
     
     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice A is incorrect because tracking boreal forest metrics does not address the comparative claim between tropical rainforests and coastal mangroves.
     * Choice B is incorrect because focusing only on the tropical rainforest area and baseline rate fails to evaluate or include the coastal mangrove's superior per-unit efficiency.
     * Choice D is incorrect because comparing temperate and boreal systems is entirely tangential to the core hypothesis contrasting rainforests and mangroves.

     -----------------------------------------------------------------
     
     QUESTION 93
     Passage:
     A sociolinguist investigated the rate of vocabulary retention among adult students learning a second language through three distinct instructional methods: digital flashcard repetition, immersion conversation blocks, and traditional textbook grammar translation. The researcher asserted that while immersion conversation leads to superior long-term conversational fluency, digital flashcard repetition yields the highest immediate retention scores for raw vocabulary word lists.
     
     Table: Average Vocabulary Words Retained After 1 Week
     | Student Demographic | Flashcard Repetition | Immersion Blocks | Textbook Translation |
     |---------------------|----------------------|------------------|----------------------|
     | Beginner Adults     | 82                   | 45               | 58                   |
     | Intermediate Adults  | 94                   | 62               | 60                   |
     | Advanced Adults      | 78                   | 70               | 48                   |
     
     Prompt:
     Which choice best uses data from the table to support the sociolinguist's assertion?
     
     Options:
     A) Advanced adults retained 70 words through immersion blocks, which was higher than the 48 words retained via textbook translation.
     B) Across all three proficiency levels, vocabulary retention scores were consistently highest for individuals utilizing digital flashcard repetition.
     C) Intermediate adults achieved a retention score of 94 via flashcard repetition, compared to a score of 60 via textbook translation.
     D) Beginner adults scored lowest in the immersion category, retaining an average of only 45 vocabulary words after one week.
     
     Correct Answer: B
     
     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice A is incorrect because isolating advanced adult immersion scores fails to validate the claim that *flashcards* yield the highest raw word counts across the board.
     * Choice C is incorrect because focusing on only one proficiency level (Intermediate) provides weaker support than an option identifying that this trend holds true uniformly across all demographics.
     * Choice D is incorrect because highlighting a weakness in beginner immersion does not provide positive empirical evidence regarding flashcard superiority.

     -----------------------------------------------------------------
     
     QUESTION 94
     Passage:
     A particle physicist evaluated the shielding efficiency of four distinct materials (lead, concrete, iron, and water) against high-energy radiation. The physicist hypothesized that the thickness of a material required to stop 99% of incoming radiation is inversely proportional to its atomic density, meaning denser materials require much less physical thickness to serve as an effective block.
     
     Table: Material Characteristics and Shielding Thresholds
     | Shielding Material | Density (g/cm³) | Required Thickness for 99% Block (cm) |
     |--------------------|-----------------|----------------------------------------|
     | Lead               | 11.34           | 1.2                                    |
     | Iron               | 7.87            | 3.5                                    |
     | Concrete           | 2.40            | 18.0                                   |
     | Water              | 1.00            | 45.0                                   |
     
     Prompt:
     Which choice best uses data from the table to support the physicist's hypothesis?
     
     Options:
     A) Lead has the highest density at 11.34 g/cm³ and requires the smallest thickness (1.2 cm), while water has the lowest density (1.00 g/cm³) and requires the greatest thickness (45.0 cm).
     B) Iron requires a thickness of 3.5 cm to achieve a 99% block, which is significantly thinner than the 18.0 cm required by concrete blocks.
     C) Concrete is denser than water by 1.40 g/cm³ and successfully blocks radiation using 27 fewer centimeters of physical material.
     D) The physical thickness required to shield against high-energy radiation increases as the atomic density of the material increases.
     
     Correct Answer: A
     
     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice B is incorrect because comparing just iron and concrete provides a narrow snapshot rather than illustrating the complete inverse correlation spanning the entire density spectrum from lead down to water.
     * Choice C is incorrect because although the numbers are accurate, Choice A offers a more robust confirmation of the hypothesis by pairing the absolute extremes (highest vs lowest density and thickness).
     * Choice D is incorrect because it describes a *direct* proportional relationship, which completely reverses the inverse correlation outlined in the hypothesis.

     -----------------------------------------------------------------
     
     QUESTION 95
     Passage:
     An ornithologist investigated the foraging behaviors of three woodwarbler species (Species A, B, and C) across different zones of spruce trees to test the concept of resource partitioning. The ornithologist claimed that each species avoids direct competition by spending the vast majority of its feeding time in a distinct vertical zone of the canopy (lower, middle, or upper branches).
     
     Table: Percentage of Feeding Time Spent by Canopy Zone
     | Warbler Species | Lower Branches | Middle Branches | Upper Branches |
     |-----------------|----------------|-----------------|----------------|
     | Species A       | 75%            | 15%             | 10%            |
     | Species B       | 12%            | 80%             | 8%             |
     | Species C       | 5%             | 10%             | 85%            |
     
     Prompt:
     Which choice best uses data from the table to support the ornithologist's claim?
     
     Options:
     A) Species A spends 15% of its time in the middle branches, whereas Species B spends 80% of its feeding time there.
     B) Each species concentrated at least 75% of its feeding time in a single unique zone: Species A in the lower, Species B in the middle, and Species C in the upper branches.
     C) Species C avoids competition by spending only 5% of its foraging time feeding on bugs located along the lower branches.
     D) All three species spend less than 20% of their total foraging time feeding together in the middle branch canopy zone.
     
     Correct Answer: B
     
     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice A is incorrect because contrasting the middle branch percentages of Species A and B does not confirm that a clear three-way structural partitioning exists across all zones.
     * Choice C is incorrect because emphasizing Species C's avoidance of lower branches fails to state where its primary, non-competing foraging focus is actually directed.
     * Choice D is incorrect because the table shows that Species B spends 80% of its time in the middle branches, meaning they do not all spend less than 20% there.

     -----------------------------------------------------------------
     
     QUESTION 96
     Passage:
     A marine chemist evaluated the dissolved oxygen retention levels across three different synthetic water tank mixtures (Saline, Brackish, and Fresh) at varying temperatures. The chemist hypothesized that the solubility of oxygen in water is compromised by both high thermal inputs and high salt concentrations, meaning cold freshwater environments retain the absolute highest concentrations of dissolved gas.
     
     Table: Dissolved Oxygen Concentrations (mg/L)
     | Water Mixture Type | Cold Configuration (4°C) | Warm Configuration (25°C) |
     |--------------------|---------------------------|---------------------------|
     | Saline Mixture     | 8.2                       | 5.4                       |
     | Brackish Mixture   | 10.1                      | 6.8                       |
     | Fresh Mixture      | 12.5                      | 8.1                       |
     
     Prompt:
     Which choice best uses data from the table to support the chemist's hypothesis?
     
     Options:
     A) The Warm Saline Mixture retained 5.4 mg/L of dissolved oxygen, which was the lowest concentration measured in the entire experiment.
     B) The Fresh Mixture retained 12.5 mg/L of oxygen when cold, which was higher than any other value, and oxygen levels dropped across all mixtures when shifted to warm configurations.
     C) Brackish water mixtures consistently maintained middle-tier oxygen profiles regardless of whether thermal configurations were set to 4°C or 25°C.
     D) Dissolved oxygen concentrations rose by exactly 2.8 mg/L when shifting fresh water from warm temperatures to cold temperatures.
     
     Correct Answer: B
     
     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice A is incorrect because isolating the absolute lowest value confirms the negative impact of heat and salt but does not explicitly confirm that cold freshwater is the *highest* point or validate the overarching trend.
     * Choice C is incorrect because tracking the intermediate performance of brackish water fails to directly evaluate the dual extremes (fresh/saline and cold/warm) driving the hypothesis.
     * Choice D is incorrect because focusing on a single mathematical delta for freshwater leaves out the saline and brackish comparison points needed to prove the salt concentration aspect of the claim.

     -----------------------------------------------------------------
     
     QUESTION 97
     Passage:
     An urban agriculturalist compared the heavy metal accumulation rates in lettuce leaves across crops grown in three urban environments: a standard ground-level backyard plot, a raised bed plot lined with geotextile fabric, and a hydroponic indoor shelf system. The researcher asserted that soil-isolated configurations (hydroponic and lined raised beds) successfully reduce lead contamination below the strict health threshold of 0.5 parts per million (ppm).
     
     Table: Lead Concentrations in Harvested Lettuce Leaves
     | Trial Batch | Ground backyard plot | Lined Raised Bed | Hydroponic Indoor System |
     |-------------|----------------------|------------------|---------------------------|
     | Batch 1     | 1.2 ppm              | 0.2 ppm          | 0.02 ppm                  |
     | Batch 2     | 0.9 ppm              | 0.3 ppm          | 0.01 ppm                  |
     | Batch 3     | 1.5 ppm              | 0.1 ppm          | 0.03 ppm                  |
     
     Prompt:
     Which choice best uses data from the table to support the researcher's assertion?
     
     Options:
     A) Ground backyard plots produced lead concentrations peaking at 1.5 ppm in Batch 3, which significantly exceeded safe standards.
     B) Across all three trial batches, both the lined raised bed and hydroponic system consistently kept lead levels below 0.5 ppm, while ground plots always exceeded it.
     C) Hydroponic indoor systems were more effective than lined raised beds, achieving a ultra-low minimum lead reading of 0.01 ppm in Batch 2.
     D) Lined raised beds allowed lead concentrations to fluctuate between 0.1 ppm and 0.3 ppm across the multi-batch experimental timeline.
     
     Correct Answer: B
     
     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice A is incorrect because outlining the failures of the ground backyard plots does not explicitly verify that the other two systems successfully met the 0.5 ppm threshold.
     * Choice C is incorrect because ranking the performance difference between hydroponics and raised beds misses the broader assertion that *both* successfully remained below the 0.5 ppm maximum limit.
     * Choice D is incorrect because summarizing the raw variance of raised beds fails to compare them against the ground control plots or evaluate them against the fixed health threshold metric.

     QUESTION 98
     Passage:
     A transportation analyst investigated the fuel efficiency drops experienced by commercial freight trucks driving at varying highway speeds while hauling different payload volumes. The analyst hypothesized that high driving speeds create severe aerodynamic drag penalties that degrade fuel economy to a greater extent than adding weight to the cargo payload bed.
     
     Table: Average Fuel Economy (Miles per Gallon - MPG)
     | Cargo Payload | Standard Speed (55 mph) | Elevated Speed (75 mph) |
     |---------------|-------------------------|-------------------------|
     | Light Load    | 8.5 MPG                 | 6.1 MPG                 |
     | Medium Load   | 8.1 MPG                 | 5.8 MPG                 |
     | Heavy Load    | 7.6 MPG                 | 5.4 MPG                 |
     
     Prompt:
     Which choice best uses data from the table to support the analyst's hypothesis?
     
     Options:
     A) Increasing speed from 55 to 75 mph caused a drop of 2.4 MPG for light loads, which is a larger decrease than the 0.9 MPG drop caused by increasing cargo from light to heavy at a fixed speed of 55 mph.
     B) Hauling a heavy load at an elevated speed of 75 mph yielded the worst fuel economy performance at 5.4 MPG.
     C) Trucks carrying a medium load managed 8.1 MPG when keeping speeds down to a standard 55 mph.
     D) Cargo adjustments from light to heavy loads caused fuel efficiency to drop uniformly by less than 1.0 MPG across both speed columns.
     
     Correct Answer: A
     
     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice B is incorrect because identifying the single lowest performance value does not isolate or mathematically contrast the independent impacts of speed vs weight.
     * Choice C is incorrect because citing an isolated baseline value for medium loads does not calculate relative efficiency drops.
     * Choice D is incorrect because noting that payload modifications cause minor drops tells only half the story; it fails to contrast this finding against the much larger speed drop to prove the hypothesis.

     QUESTION 99
     Passage:
     An archeometrist measured the density of obsidian artifacts recovered from three separate excavation layers (Layers Alpha, Beta, and Gamma) at an ancient site in Anatolia to identify shifts in tool-making preferences. The researcher hypothesized that early artisans in the oldest layer favored highly dense obsidian sourced from volcanic regions, while later generations shifted toward lower density glass variants. Note: Layer Gamma is the oldest layer, and Layer Alpha is the newest.
     
     Table: Average Obsidian Artifact Density (g/cm³)
     | Excavation Stratum | Tool Type: Blades | Tool Type: Scrapers |
     |--------------------|-------------------|----------------------|
     | Layer Alpha (New)  | 2.35              | 2.40                 |
     | Layer Beta (Mid)   | 2.52              | 2.55                 |
     | Layer Gamma (Old)  | 2.78              | 2.82                 |
     
     Prompt:
     Which choice best uses data from the table to support the researcher's hypothesis?
     
     Options:
     A) Obsidian blades recovered from the mid-tier Layer Beta exhibited a uniform average density of 2.52 g/cm³.
     B) In the oldest layer (Gamma), both blades and scrapers possessed the highest average densities (2.78 and 2.82 g/cm³), and artifact density decreased sequentially in newer layers.
     C) Scrapers always maintained a slightly higher structural density than blades across all three historical excavation strata.
     D) Artifact density dropped by exactly 0.43 g/cm³ when comparing blades from Layer Gamma with blades from Layer Alpha.
     
     Correct Answer: B
     
     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice A is incorrect because presenting an isolated median data point for blades fails to trace the full historical progression across layers.
     * Choice C is incorrect because comparing the structural differences between blades and scrapers is irrelevant to the chronological hypothesis tracking age layers.
     * Choice D is incorrect because a narrow mathematical extraction for one tool type lacks the comprehensive validation achieved by capturing both tool types across the full timeline.

     QUESTION 100
     Passage:
     A media studies professor evaluated user engagement metrics across three news delivery platforms (Digital Website, Audio Podcast, and Print Newsletter) across different reader age brackets. The professor claimed that while younger readers are heavily drawn to digital formats, the Print Newsletter remains the most effective tool for maintaining long-term engagement among readers over the age of 60.
     
     Table: Average Engagement Score (Scale of 1-100)
     | Reader Age Group | Digital Website | Audio Podcast | Print Newsletter |
     |------------------|-----------------|---------------|------------------|
     | Ages 18–35       | 88              | 74            | 22               |
     | Ages 36–59       | 65              | 68            | 54               |
     | Ages 60+         | 41              | 35            | 82               |
     
     Prompt:
     Which choice best uses data from the table to support the professor's claim?
     
     Options:
     A) For the 18–35 age bracket, the digital website achieved an engagement score of 88, whereas the print newsletter scored only 22.
     B) For readers aged 60 and older, the Print Newsletter earned an engagement score of 82, which significantly surpassed the scores for the Digital Website (41) and Audio Podcast (35).
     C) Audio podcasts maintained relatively stable engagement profiles, tracking between 35 and 74 points across all age demographics.
     D) Print newsletter engagement expanded from a minimum score of 22 up to a maximum score of 82 as the reader demographic aged.
     
     Correct Answer: B
     
     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice A is incorrect because data proving younger readers prefer digital formats fails to support the secondary, core part of the claim focusing on the over-60 demographic's print preference.
     * Choice C is incorrect because tracking podcast stability is completely tangential to evaluating print news efficacy among seniors.
     * Choice D is incorrect because tracing the general upward trajectory of print as people age does not explicitly confirm that print *outperforms its direct competitors* within the senior demographic.

     QUESTION 101
     Passage:
     A plant ecologist investigated how soil salinity affects the germination rate of two coastal grass variants: *Distichlis spicata* (Variant 1) and *Spartina patens* (Variant 2). A previous study claimed that Variant 1 is entirely salt-tolerant, showing no reduction in germination success as salinity increases. The ecologist, however, believes this claim is oversimplified. She hypothesizes that while Variant 1 tolerates moderate salinity better than Variant 2, its germination rate still drops significantly once salinity reaches high levels (above 20 parts per thousand, or ppt).
     
     Table: Average Germination Success Rate (%)
     | Salinity Level | Variant 1 (*D. spicata*) | Variant 2 (*S. patens*) |
     |----------------|--------------------------|--------------------------|
     | Low (0 ppt)    | 95%                      | 92%                      |
     | Medium (15 ppt)| 92%                      | 54%                      |
     | High (30 ppt)  | 42%                      | 12%                      |
     
     Prompt:
     Which choice best uses data from the table to complete the assertion?
     The data in the table support the ecologist's hypothesis rather than the previous study's claim because as salinity levels rose from 0 ppt to 15 ppt, Variant 1's germination rate fell by only 3%, but when salinity reached 30 ppt, Variant 1's germination rate ________
     
     Options:
     A) dropped substantially to 42%, demonstrating that high salinity severely impairs its germination success despite its moderate tolerance.
     B) fell to 12%, indicating that it is less resilient to extreme salt conditions than Variant 2.
     C) remained statistically unchanged at 92%, validating the previous study's assertion of absolute tolerance.
     D) decreased to 42%, which matched the exact percentage drop experienced by Variant 2 across the same interval.
     
     Correct Answer: A
     
     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice B is incorrect because 12% is the value for Variant 2, not Variant 1, representing a data mislookup.
     * Choice C is incorrect because it misstates the data trends, claiming stability at 92% when the table shows a drop to 42%.
     * Choice D is incorrect because Variant 2 dropped from 92% to 12% (an 80% decrease), which does not mathematically match Variant 1's performance profile.

     | Home Goods       | $8.4      | $9.2      | $12.6     | $14.1     |

     Which choice best uses data from the table to support the analyst's contention?

     A) Apparel revenues climbed steadily from $14.2 million in Q1 to a peak of $22.4 million in Q4, confirming the board's optimistic assessment for that specific sector.
     B) Home Goods revenue grew by over $5 million between Q1 and Q4, demonstrating a strong positive response to the new marketing campaign.
     C) While Apparel and Home Goods revenues grew in the second half of the year, Electronics revenues actually declined significantly, dropping from $34.5 million in Q2 to $21.0 million in Q3 and $19.5 million in Q4.

     QUESTION 103

The scientist hypothesized that Catalyst Y operates via an activation threshold mechanism, meaning it remains completely ineffective at low and moderate temperatures but delivers superior strength restoration compared to the other catalysts once the environment hits a high temperature threshold of 60°C.
     
     Table: Tensile Strength Restoration Percentage (%)
     | Applied Chemical Catalyst | Low Temp (20°C) | Mid Temp (40°C) | High Temp (60°C) |
     |---------------------------|-----------------|-----------------|------------------|
     | Catalyst X                | 45%             | 60%             | 70%              |
     | Catalyst Y                | 5%              | 8%              | 95%              |
     | Catalyst Z                | 30%             | 55%             | 80%              |
     
     Prompt:
     Which choice best uses data from the table to support the scientist's hypothesis?
     
     Options:
     A) Catalyst Y achieved a negligible 5% restoration at 20°C and 8% at 40°C, but surged to 95% at 60°C, outperforming Catalyst X's 70% and Catalyst Z's 80% at that same threshold.
     B) Catalyst X demonstrated the most stable and reliable healing progression, advancing from 45% up to 70% as temperatures increased.
     C) Catalyst Z delivered a 55% restoration rate at mid-range temperatures, making it more effective than Catalyst Y across both low and moderate settings.
     D) Curing polymers at 60°C ensured that all three chemical catalysts achieved strength restoration levels of at least 70% or greater.
     
     Correct Answer: A
     
     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice B is incorrect because tracking Catalyst X's stable linear progression does not address or evaluate Catalyst Y's specific activation threshold profile.
     * Choice C is incorrect because outlining Catalyst Z's mid-range superiority fails to confirm the second, critical part of the hypothesis: Catalyst Y's ultimate dominance at 60°C.
     * Choice D is incorrect because a generalized summary statement ignores the specific, dramatic threshold jump that isolates Catalyst Y's unique behavioral mechanism.

     QUESTION 104
     Passage:
     An environmental scientist investigated the nitrogen run-off mitigation rates achieved by installing buffer strips composed of three distinct vegetation types (Turf Grass, Native Wildflowers, and Mixed Wetland Reeds) across varying slope gradients. The scientist claimed that while standard Turf Grass is effective on gentle slopes, its mitigation capacity collapses on steep inclines, making Mixed Wetland Reeds a significantly better choice for slopes exceeding a 10% gradient.
     
     Table: Average Nitrogen Run-off Mitigation Efficiency (%)
     | Buffer Strip Vegetation Type | Gentle Slope (2% Grade) | Moderate Slope (6% Grade) | Steep Slope (12% Grade) |
     |------------------------------|-------------------------|---------------------------|-------------------------|
     | Turf Grass                   | 82%                     | 55%                       | 18%                     |
     | Native Wildflowers           | 64%                     | 58%                       | 40%                     |
     | Mixed Wetland Reeds          | 78%                     | 75%                       | 72%                     |
     
     Prompt:
     Which choice best uses data from the table to support the scientist's claim?
     
     Options:
     A) Mixed Wetland Reeds maintained a highly stable mitigation efficiency, dropping slightly from 78% on gentle slopes to 72% on steep slopes.
     B) Turf Grass achieved the highest baseline efficiency at 82% on gentle slopes, outperforming Native Wildflowers' 64% and Mixed Wetland Reeds' 78%.
     C) On a 12% grade steep slope, Turf Grass efficiency plummeted to 18%, whereas Mixed Wetland Reeds retained an efficiency of 72%, far outperforming the other options.
     D) Native Wildflowers were unique because their mitigation efficiency remained stable at around 58% on moderate gradients.
     
     Correct Answer: C
     
     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice A is incorrect because stating Mixed Wetland Reeds' individual stability across gradients does not explicitly contrast it against the specific efficiency collapse of Turf Grass required by the prompt.
     * Choice B is incorrect because highlighting Turf Grass's success on gentle slopes focuses on the wrong gradient condition, failing to address the steep incline comparison.
     * Choice D is incorrect because isolating wildflower performance on moderate gradients ignores the core comparative focus between grass and wetland reeds on steep hillsides.

     QUESTION 105
     Passage:

The model states that an impending eruption is preceded by a sharp, exponential increase in the ratio of carbon dioxide (CO2) to sulfur dioxide (SO2) gases emitted from the primary active fissure (Site B), while minor flank vents (Sites A and C) remain chemically stable.
     
     Table: CO2 to SO2 Gas Emission Ratios Over Time
     | Observation Site | 30 Days Before Eruption | 15 Days Before Eruption | 1 Day Before Eruption |
     |------------------|-------------------------|-------------------------|------------------------|
     | Site A (Flank)   | 1.5                     | 1.6                     | 1.4                    |
     | Site B (Primary) | 2.1                     | 8.4                     | 45.2                   |
     | Site C (Flank)   | 0.8                     | 0.9                     | 1.1                    |
     
     Prompt:
     Which choice best uses data from the table to support the volcanologist's predictive model?
     
     Options:
     A) Site A and Site C flank vent ratios remained low and stable, tracking around 1.5 and 1.0, while the primary fissure at Site B experienced a massive surge from 2.1 up to 45.2.
     B) Site B's gas ratio increased from 2.1 to 8.4 midway through the observation timeline, indicating a steady linear growth pattern.
     C) Flank vent Site C exhibited a minor, continuous upward trend, moving from 0.8 up to 1.1 over the 30-day tracking window.
     D) The average aggregate gas ratio across all three monitored vent sites combined climbed to its highest point one day before the eruption.
     
     Correct Answer: A

     * Choice D is incorrect because mathematical aggregation blurs the critical distinction between the primary fissure's surge and the flank vents' flat baseline profiles.

     Table: Average Maze Escape Times (Seconds)
     | Dosage Tier | Day 1 Training Baseline | Day 5 Evaluation Trial | Day 10 Final Evaluation |
     |-------------|-------------------------|------------------------|-------------------------|

     QUESTION 111
     Passage:
     The following text is adapted from a research report on avian foraging ecology.
     Biologists investigating the competitive exclusion principle frequently study the hunting strategies of predatory birds in overlapping territories. A long-standing hypothesis posits that when two closely related raptor species—the Northern Harrier and the Red-tailed Hawk—share a habitat, they divide resources via temporal segregation, meaning one species hunts primarily during early dawn hours while the other concentrates its activity during peak afternoon heat, thereby minimizing direct physical encounters. Ecologist Elena Vance designed a study to evaluate this hypothesis by recording active hunts across multiple field sites.
     
     Table: Average Number of Active Hunts Observed per Hour
     | Raptor Species    | Early Dawn (5 AM - 7 AM) | Midday (11 AM - 1 PM) | Late Afternoon (4 PM - 6 PM) |
     |-------------------|---------------------------|------------------------|------------------------------|
     | Northern Harrier  | 14.2                      | 2.1                    | 15.8                         |
     | Red-tailed Hawk   | 3.5                       | 18.4                   | 4.2                          |
     
     Prompt:
     Which choice best uses data from the table to complete the evaluation of the temporal segregation hypothesis?
     The data in the table ________ the temporal segregation hypothesis because the Northern Harrier's active hunting peaked during early dawn (14.2) and late afternoon (15.8) while dropping to a minimum at midday (2.1), which perfectly alternated with the Red-tailed Hawk's hunting profile, which ________
     
     Options:
     A) support; reached its maximum intensity during midday at 18.4 hunts per hour, precisely when the Harrier's activity was lowest.
     B) weaken; remained low during early dawn (3.5) and late afternoon (4.2), indicating that the two species consistently avoided hunting at the same times.
     C) refute; peaked at 18.4 hunts per hour during midday, demonstrating that both raptor species are highly active during the exact same intervals of the day.
     D) support; exhibited a completely uniform distribution of 18.4 hunts per hour across all measured periods of the daytime tracking cycle.
     
     Correct Answer: A
     
     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice B is incorrect because it claims the data *weakens* the hypothesis, but the text description of the data actually confirms a perfect alternating pattern of temporal segregation.
     * Choice C is incorrect because it claims the data *refutes* the model by suggesting they are active at the same time, which directly misinterprets the table (the Harrier is low when the Hawk is high).
     * Choice D is incorrect because it misrepresents the table data, claiming the Hawk's activity was uniform across all periods when it actually peaked strictly at midday.

     QUESTION 112
     Passage:
     In solid-state physics, the efficiency of an thermoelectric material—which converts heat gradients directly into electrical energy—is quantified by its dimensionless figure of merit, ZT. Traditional theoretical models suggest that a material's ZT value is maximized when its lattice structures are doped with heavy crystalline compounds like bismuth telluride, which suppress thermal conductivity while maintaining high electrical transport. Physicist Akira Sato hypothesized that while bismuth-doped alloys deliver high performance under low-temperature configurations, a newly synthesized silicon-germanium nanostructure matrix achieves significantly superior ZT values once temperatures exceed 600 Kelvin (K).
     
     Table: Dimensionless Figure of Merit (ZT) Across Thermal Profiles
     | Tested Material Composition | Low Temp (300 K) | Mid Temp (500 K) | High Temp (700 K) | Ultra High Temp (900 K) |
     |-----------------------------|------------------|------------------|-------------------|-------------------------|
     | Bismuth Telluride Alloy     | 1.20             | 1.35             | 0.85              | 0.40                    |
     | Silicon-Germanium Matrix    | 0.25             | 0.60             | 1.65              | 1.90                    |
     | Lead Selenide Compound      | 0.50             | 0.95             | 1.10              | 1.05                    |
     
     Prompt:
     Which choice best uses data from the table to support Sato's hypothesis?
     
     Options:
     A) Bismuth Telluride achieved its peak performance at 500 K with a ZT of 1.35, outperforming the Silicon-Germanium matrix across both low and mid-temperature intervals.
     B) At 700 K and 900 K, the Silicon-Germanium matrix reached ZT values of 1.65 and 1.90 respectively, significantly outperforming Bismuth Telluride (0.85 and 0.40) and Lead Selenide (1.10 and 1.05).
     C) Lead Selenide demonstrated a highly stable performance envelope, holding a ZT value of around 1.05 across all high-temperature testing environments.
     D) The Silicon-Germanium matrix exhibited a continuous upward trajectory, expanding its ZT value by exactly 0.35 points between 300 K and 500 K.
     
     Correct Answer: B
     
     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice A is incorrect because highlighting Bismuth Telluride's early dominance at lower temperatures fails to address the core hypothesis regarding Silicon-Germanium's superior performance at high temperatures.
     * Choice C is incorrect because tracking the stability of the Lead Selenide control compound is completely irrelevant to evaluating Sato's specific claim about Silicon-Germanium.
     * Choice D is incorrect because isolating the initial minor increase at low temperatures ignores the critical high-temperature data (700K and 900K) where the hypothesis is actually proven.

     -----------------------------------------------------------------
     
     QUESTION 113
     Passage:
     The following text is adapted from an economic history essay on pre-industrial labor dynamics.
     A classic debate among economic historians centers on whether the formalization of urban craft guilds in 17th-century Europe functioned as an extractive monopoly that suppressed real wages for day laborers or as an institutional stabilizer that insulated worker compensation from agricultural shock patterns. Historian Clara Dupont hypothesized that the impact of guild formalization was highly contingent upon regional population density: in low-density agrarian regions (such as Sector North), guilds stabilized wages during crop failures, whereas in high-density urban zones (such as Sector South), they locked out non-members and severely depressed day-laborer compensation during market shocks.
     
     Table: Average Daily Real Wage Index (Adjusted for Inflation)
     | Regional Sector | Baseline Years (Normal Crop) | Year 1 Shock (Crop Failure) | Year 2 Shock (Market Disruption) |
     |-----------------|------------------------------|-----------------------------|-----------------------------------|
     | Sector North    | 105                          | 102                         | 104                               |
     | Sector South    | 98                           | 64                          | 51                                |
     | Sector West     | 85                           | 82                         | 79                                |
     
     Prompt:
     Which choice best uses data from the table to support Dupont's contingency hypothesis?
     
     Options:
     A) Sector North maintained an exceptionally stable real wage index, drifting only slightly from 105 to 102 during the crop failure, while Sector South's index collapsed from 98 down to 64 and 51 across the consecutive shock years.
     B) Sector South possessed a lower baseline wage index (98) than Sector North (105) even during normal crop years, confirming that guilds are universally harmful to day laborers.
     C) Real wages in Sector West declined steadily across the entire observation window, dropping from an initial index of 85 down to a final index of 79 in Year 2.
     D) Crop failures in Year 1 caused a uniform real wage reduction of less than 5% across all three pre-industrial economic sectors tracked by Dupont.
     
     Correct Answer: A
     
     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice B is incorrect because a baseline difference during normal years does not track or evaluate how the regions respond differently to *shocks*, which is the core of the contingency hypothesis.
     * Choice C is incorrect because tracking the steady decline of the Sector West control group does not address the comparative claim between Sectors North and South.
     * Choice D is incorrect because it misstates the data trends, claiming a uniform drop of less than 5% when Sector South experienced a massive 34% drop (from 98 to 64) in Year 1.

     QUESTION 114
     Passage:
     In evolutionary microbiology, the "cost of resistance" model states that bacteria acquiring mutations to survive antibiotic treatments exhibit compromised metabolic efficiency when grown in drug-free environments, making them lose out to wild-type strains. Geneticist Marcus Thorne challenged this dogma, hypothesizing that while a single resistance mutation (*mut-1*) incurs a severe metabolic penalty, the subsequent acquisition of a compensatory secondary mutation (*mut-2*) fully restores reproductive fitness, allowing resistant strains to match or exceed wild-type growth rates even in environments completely free of antibiotics.
     
     Table: Average Bacterial Growth Rate (Generations per Hour)
     | Strain Type            | Baseline Glucose Medium | Enriched L-Lactate Medium | Minimal Salt Medium |
     |------------------------|-------------------------|---------------------------|---------------------|
     | Wild-Type (Control)    | 2.4                     | 1.8                       | 1.1                 |
     | Resistant (*mut-1*)    | 1.1                     | 0.8                       | 0.4                 |
     | Compensated (*mut-2*)  | 2.5                     | 1.9                       | 1.2                 |
     
     Prompt:
     Which choice best uses data from the table to support Thorne's hypothesis?
     
     Options:
     A) The single-mutation resistant strain (*mut-1*) grew at a sluggish rate of 1.1 in glucose and 0.8 in L-lactate, confirming the classic cost of resistance model.
     B) Across all three drug-free media types, the compensated strain (*mut-2*) achieved growth rates of 2.5, 1.9, and 1.2, which matched or slightly exceeded the wild-type control benchmarks (2.4, 1.8, and 1.1) and far surpassed the *mut-1* strain.
     C) Wild-type control bacteria demonstrated their highest reproductive efficiency when grown in the baseline glucose medium, reaching 2.4 generations per hour.
     D) The resistant strain (*mut-1*) experienced its absolute worst metabolic performance in the minimal salt medium, clearing only 0.4 generations per hour.
     
     Correct Answer: B
     
     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice A is incorrect because isolating the performance of the *mut-1* strain validates only the *classic model* that Thorne is actively challenging; it fails to provide the compensatory *mut-2* data needed to validate his new hypothesis.
     * Choice C is incorrect because detailing wild-type baseline parameters does not evaluate the reproductive recovery achieved by the mutated bacterial strains.
     * Choice D is incorrect because highlighting a localized failure for the uncompensated strain does not track the cross-media restoration trend driven by the secondary mutation.

     QUESTION 115
     Passage:
     A deep-sea geobiologist investigated the metabolic processing rates of methane-oxidizing archaea consortia across varying benthic sediment depths in cold seep ecosystems. A previous model asserted that archaeal metabolic activity declines in a perfectly linear pattern with sediment depth due to a uniform decrease in thermal energy. The geobiologist contends that this model fails to account for nutrient transport mechanics. He hypothesizes that metabolic processing rates stay high and stable across upper and mid-depth sediment strata, collapsing abruptly only at extreme depths where local sulfate channels become entirely exhausted.
     
     Table: Archaea Metabolic Processing Rate (micromoles/cm³/day)
     | Seep Location | Shallow Strata (0–5 cm) | Mid-Depth Strata (10–15 cm) | Deep Benthic Strata (50+ cm) |
     |---------------|-------------------------|------------------------------|-------------------------------|
     | Seep Site 1   | 45.2                    | 44.8                         | 2.1                           |
     | Seep Site 2   | 38.9                    | 39.1                         | 1.5                           |
     | Seep Site 3   | 52.4                    | 51.9                         | 3.0                           |
     
     Prompt:
     Which choice best uses data from the table to support the geobiologist's hypothesis over the previous linear decline model?
     
     Options:
     A) Across all three seep locations, metabolic processing rates remained nearly identical and highly stable between the shallow and mid-depth strata, but plummeted sharply by over 90% when moving into the deep benthic strata.
     B) Seep Site 3 consistently exhibited the highest overall archaeal metabolic activity, tracking at 52.4 in shallow strata and 51.9 in mid-depth layers.
     C) Archaeal metabolic processing rates at Seep Site 1 decreased slightly from 45.2 to 44.8 micromoles/cm³/day across the first ten centimeters of sediment depth.
     D) The deep benthic strata across all three sites uniformly demonstrated severely depressed processing rates, dropping to a minimum value of 1.5 at Seep Site 2.
     
     Correct Answer: A

     * Choice B is incorrect because highlighting the individual performance peak of Seep Site 3 fails to contrast the upper/mid-depth stability against the deep collapse that defines the geobiologist's structural hypothesis.
     * Choice C is incorrect because focusing on a minor individual drop at Site 1 does not illustrate the comprehensive non-linear trend that characterizes the entire dataset.
     * Choice D is incorrect because summarizing the low values in deep strata without connecting them to the high, stable baselines of the upper layers fails to challenge the previous model's linear progression claim.

     QUESTION 116
     Passage:
     The following text is adapted from a political science research paper on voter mobilization.
     Political scientists frequently debate the efficacy of "canvassing outreach models" in boosting voter turnout during municipal elections. The traditional rational-choice model predicts that intensive door-to-door canvassing yields a uniform upward trend in voter participation across all neighborhoods by reducing structural information costs. Researcher Marcus Vance argued that this model is flawed because it ignores baseline socioeconomic entrenchment. He hypothesized that while canvassing is highly effective in moderate-income districts, it delivers zero measurable turnout changes in both ultra-low-income districts (due to structural alienation) and ultra-high-income districts (where turnout is already maxed out).
     
     Table: Municipal Election Voter Turnout Percentage (%)
     | District Tier (Socioeconomic Baseline) | No-Canvassing Control Group | Intensive Canvassing Group |
     |----------------------------------------|-----------------------------|----------------------------|
     | Tier A (Ultra-Low Income)              | 22.4%                       | 22.5%                      |
     | Tier B (Moderate Income)               | 41.2%                       | 58.6%                      |
     | Tier C (Ultra-High Income)             | 84.5%                       | 84.7%                      |
     
     Prompt:
     Which choice best uses data from the table to support Vance's hypothesis over the traditional rational-choice model?
     
     Options:
     A) Tier B moderate-income districts experienced a massive 17.4% voter turnout surge under intensive canvassing, whereas Tier A and Tier C districts remained statistically flat, showing changes of only 0.1% and 0.2% respectively.
     B) Canvassing group turnout in Tier C reached an absolute peak of 84.7%, proving that door-to-door outreach models are most successful when applied to affluent populations.
     C) In the no-canvassing control groups, voter turnout scaled strictly in accordance with socioeconomic status, moving from 22.4% in Tier A up to 84.5% in Tier C.
     D) Intensive canvassing succeeded in raising voter turnout rates above the 50% threshold for both moderate-income Tier B and high-income Tier C districts.
     
     Correct Answer: A
     
     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice B is incorrect because claiming canvassing was most successful in Tier C misinterprets the table; the *increase* caused by canvassing in Tier C was practically zero (84.5% to 84.7%), meaning the outreach itself had no meaningful impact there.
     * Choice C is incorrect because outlining the baseline control group trend across classes describes a social reality but fails to evaluate the *intervention efficacy of canvassing* which forms the core of the hypothesis.
     * Choice D is incorrect because referencing a fixed 50% threshold completely glosses over the net growth metrics needed to evaluate Vance's multi-tier conditional argument.

     QUESTION 117
     Passage:
     In materials engineering, the fracture toughness of ceramic matrices can be enhanced by embedding carbon nanotube (CNT) alignments. A common manufacturing assumption is that fracture toughness increases linearly with the volume percentage of embedded nanotubes. Mechanical engineer Sarah Lin hypothesized that this linear model oversimplifies the composite's structural limits. She asserted that while increasing CNT volume up to 2.0% steadily reinforces the ceramic matrix, adding any volume beyond that threshold causes nanotube agglomeration (clumping), which introduces internal structural defects that severely degrade fracture toughness back toward baseline levels.
     
     Table: Average Fracture Toughness (MPa·m¹/²)
     | Ceramic Matrix Base Type | 0.0% CNT (Baseline) | 2.0% CNT (Optimal) | 5.0% CNT (Excessive) |
     |--------------------------|---------------------|--------------------|----------------------|
     | Alumina Ceramic          | 3.4                 | 6.8                | 3.6                  |
     | Zirconia Ceramic         | 5.2                 | 9.5                | 5.5                  |
     | Silicon Carbide          | 4.1                 | 8.2                | 4.3                  |
     
     Prompt:
     Which choice best uses data from the table to support Lin's hypothesis over the linear manufacturing assumption?
     
     Options:
     A) Zirconia Ceramic possessed the highest baseline fracture toughness at 5.2 MPa·m¹/² and reached an optimal toughness of 9.5 MPa·m¹/² when infused with 2.0% CNT alignments.
     B) Across all three ceramic base types, fracture toughness doubled when CNT content rose from 0.0% to 2.0%, but crashed abruptly back down to near-baseline levels (3.6, 5.5, and 4.3) when CNT content reached an excessive 5.0%.
     C) Infusing Silicon Carbide with 5.0% CNT resulted in an average fracture toughness of 4.3 MPa·m¹/² which was slightly higher than its unreinforced 0.0% baseline value of 4.1 MPa·m¹/².
     D) The fracture toughness of Alumina Ceramic grew by exactly 3.4 points during the initial reinforcement phase, demonstrating a highly predictable growth trajectory.
     
     Correct Answer: B
     
     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice A is incorrect because highlighting Zirconia's optimal performance at 2.0% leaves out the excessive 5.0% data point needed to prove the subsequent clumping degradation predicted by the hypothesis.
     * Choice C is incorrect because noting that the 5.0% layer is slightly higher than baseline fails to acknowledge or capture the massive drop that occurred relative to the 2.0% optimal peak, missing the structural curve.
     * Choice D is incorrect because isolating the initial step for Alumina ceramic fails to track the complete non-linear inflection trajectory that disproves the linear manufacturing model.

     QUESTION 118
     Passage:
     An environmental toxicologist evaluated the heavy metal bioaccumulation rates in agricultural crops following the application of synthetic pesticide treatments. A previous regulatory report claimed that chromium ions build up inside plant roots in a direct, linear proportion to the total concentration of pesticide applied to the soil. The toxicologist argues that this linear model is dangerously inaccurate because it ignores cellular saturation limits. She hypothesizes that while root accumulation scales rapidly under low application densities, the plant's internal transport channels become completely saturated at a moderate threshold of 10 mg/kg, causing the accumulation rate to plateau completely even under extreme pesticide exposure.
     
     Table: Chromium Ion Concentration in Root Tissue (mg/kg)
     | Tested Crop Variant | Control Tier (0 mg/kg) | Moderate Tier (10 mg/kg) | Extreme Tier (50 mg/kg) |
     |---------------------|------------------------|--------------------------|-------------------------|
     | Crop Variant X      | 0.02                   | 4.50                     | 4.52                    |
     | Crop Variant Y      | 0.05                   | 5.12                     | 5.15                    |
     | Crop Variant Z      | 0.01                   | 3.88                     | 3.91                    |
     
     Prompt:
     Which choice best uses data from the table to support the toxicologist's hypothesis over the regulatory report's claim?
     
     Options:
     A) Crop Variant Y exhibited the highest overall chromium accumulation in root tissue, tracking at 5.12 mg/kg in the moderate tier and 5.15 mg/kg in the extreme exposure environment.
     B) When pesticide application expanded from 10 mg/kg to 50 mg/kg, root chromium concentrations across all three crop variants remained virtually unchanged, staying locked at around 4.5, 5.1, and 3.9 mg/kg and proving a complete saturation plateau.
     C) Crop Variant Z kept chromium ions down to a minimal 0.01 mg/kg under control conditions, outperforming the other variants in safety baselines.
     D) Increasing pesticide exposure from 0 to 10 mg/kg caused root tissue contamination to skyrocket across all variants, demonstrating that low application densities are highly dangerous.
     
     Correct Answer: B
     
     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice A is incorrect because isolating Crop Variant Y's individual maximum value fails to emphasize the cross-tier flatline comparison between the 10 mg/kg and 50 mg/kg marks that explicitly proves the saturation plateau hypothesis.
     * Choice C is incorrect because control tier safety baselines provide zero insight into how the plants respond to rising chemical saturation curves.
     * Choice D is incorrect because highlighting the initial spike under low application densities only addresses the first half of the data, failing to track the critical subsequent plateau that disproves the regulatory report's linear claim.

Archaeologist Marcus Vance challenged this paradigm, arguing that supply networks were strictly compartmentalized by geographical distance and political alliances.      Table: Olive Oil Amphora Frequencies (% of Total Recovered Oil Shards)
