     A) ,
     B) ;
     C) :
     D) — but

     Correct Answer: C

     Correct Answer Explanation:
     * Choice C is correct because the first clause announces that the account challenges the narrative "in two significant respects," and what follows is the enumeration of those two respects. A colon after a complete independent clause that announces a list is standard and precise.

     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice A is incorrect because a comma alone joining two independent clauses creates a comma splice — the clause following the blank ("first, it revises the timeline...") is independent.
     * Choice B is incorrect because while a semicolon can join two independent clauses, it does not signal the enumerative relationship between "two significant respects" and the list that follows — the colon is more precise here.
     * Choice D is incorrect because "— but" uses an em-dash and a coordinating conjunction suggesting contrast, but the items that follow are not in contrast with the announcement of two respects — they are the specifications of those respects.

     A) —
     B) ;
     C) ,
     D) :

     Correct Answer: C

     Correct Answer Explanation:
     * Choice C is correct because the nonrestrictive relative clause "which had been inserted at the last minute during final negotiations" is set off from the rest of the sentence by a pair of commas. The first comma appears before "which"; the blank requires the closing comma to complete the pair and allow the main predicate ("required signatory nations...") to follow.

     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice A is incorrect because an em-dash would create an asymmetric pair with the comma that opened the relative clause — punctuation setting off a parenthetical must be consistent; a comma opened it and a comma must close it.
     * Choice B is incorrect because a semicolon joins two independent clauses and cannot close a nonrestrictive relative clause or separate a subject from its predicate.

   • Form, Structure, and Sense
     -----------------------------------------------------------------
     [DIFFICULTY LEVEL: LOW - QUESTIONS 1-10]

     QUESTION 1
     Passage:
     The students in the after-school program _______ three hours each week practicing debate techniques and public speaking.

     Prompt:
     Which choice completes the text so that it conforms to the conventions of Standard Written English?

     Options:
     A) spends
     B) spend
     C) is spending
     D) has spent

     Correct Answer: B

     Correct Answer Explanation:
     * Choice B is correct because the subject "students" is plural, and the verb must agree with it. "Spend" is the correct plural present-tense form. The prepositional phrase "in the after-school program" comes between the subject and verb but does not affect agreement.

     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice A is incorrect because "spends" is the third-person singular form, which does not agree with the plural subject "students."
     * Choice C is incorrect because "is spending" is a singular progressive construction that does not agree with the plural subject and introduces unnecessary aspect.
     * Choice D is incorrect because "has spent" is the third-person singular present perfect form; it neither agrees with the plural subject nor reflects the simple present tense the sentence requires.

     -----------------------------------------------------------------

     QUESTION 2
     Passage:
     Each of the researchers _______ responsible for submitting a progress report at the end of the semester.

     Prompt:
     Which choice completes the text so that it conforms to the conventions of Standard Written English?

     Options:
     A) are
     B) were
     C) is
     D) have been

     Correct Answer: C

     Correct Answer Explanation:
     * Choice C is correct because the subject is "each," which is a singular indefinite pronoun. Even though "of the researchers" follows, the verb must agree with "each," not with "researchers." "Is" is the correct singular present-tense form.

     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice A is incorrect because "are" is a plural verb that agrees with "researchers" rather than with the actual subject "each," which is singular.
     * Choice B is incorrect because "were" is plural past tense, which neither agrees with the singular subject "each" nor fits the present-tense context of the sentence.
     * Choice D is incorrect because "have been" is a plural present perfect form that does not agree with the singular subject "each."

     -----------------------------------------------------------------

     QUESTION 3
     Passage:
     The team celebrated their victory last night; _______ had worked for months to prepare for the championship match.

     Prompt:
     Which choice completes the text so that it conforms to the conventions of Standard Written English?

     Options:
     A) it
     B) they
     C) one
     D) he or she

     Correct Answer: B

     Correct Answer Explanation:
     * Choice B is correct because the antecedent "team" is being treated as a collective plural in this sentence — the use of "their" earlier establishes that the team is being referred to with plural pronouns. "They" maintains this consistency.

     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice A is incorrect because "it" treats the team as a singular entity, but the sentence has already used "their" to refer to the team in plural terms — switching to "it" would create an inconsistency in pronoun reference.
     * Choice C is incorrect because "one" is an indefinite pronoun that does not refer back to a specific antecedent and would make the sentence unclear and impersonal.
     * Choice D is incorrect because "he or she" refers to individual people rather than to the team as a group, which is the intended antecedent.

     -----------------------------------------------------------------

     QUESTION 4
     Passage:
     The company announced that it _______ expanding its operations to three new countries by the end of the fiscal year.

     Prompt:
     Which choice completes the text so that it conforms to the conventions of Standard Written English?

     Options:
     A) is
     B) were
     C) will have been
     D) had been

     Correct Answer: A

     Correct Answer Explanation:
     * Choice A is correct because the sentence describes a future plan announced in the present context. "Is expanding" (present progressive) is the standard construction for a planned future action, and "is" agrees with the singular subject "it."

     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice B is incorrect because "were" is past tense (or subjunctive), which conflicts with the forward-looking time reference ("by the end of the fiscal year") and does not agree with the singular "it" in a simple declarative statement.
     * Choice C is incorrect because "will have been expanding" (future perfect progressive) implies a continuous action completed by a future point, which is unnecessarily complex for a simple announcement of planned expansion.
     * Choice D is incorrect because "had been" is past perfect, which places the action before another past event — inconsistent with the announcement of a future plan.

     -----------------------------------------------------------------

     QUESTION 5
     Passage:
     The director, along with several producers and the lead actor, _______ planning to attend the film festival in Cannes.

     Prompt:
     Which choice completes the text so that it conforms to the conventions of Standard Written English?

     Options:
     A) are
     B) is
     C) were
     D) have been

     Correct Answer: B

     Correct Answer Explanation:
     * Choice B is correct because the subject is "the director" — a singular noun. "Along with several producers and the lead actor" is a parenthetical phrase that adds information but does not change the grammatical subject. The verb must agree with "the director," so the singular "is" is correct.

     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice A is incorrect because "are" treats the parenthetical phrase as part of a compound subject, but phrases introduced by "along with" do not create compound subjects — the subject remains singular.
     * Choice C is incorrect because "were" is past tense and plural, agreeing with neither the singular subject nor the present-tense context.
     * Choice D is incorrect because "have been" is plural present perfect, which does not agree with the singular subject "the director."

     -----------------------------------------------------------------

     QUESTION 6
     Passage:
     The architect's original sketches, which had been stored in the museum's archive for decades, _______ finally put on public display last spring.

     Prompt:
     Which choice completes the text so that it conforms to the conventions of Standard Written English?

     Options:
     A) was
     B) were
     C) has been
     D) is

     Correct Answer: B

     Correct Answer Explanation:
     * Choice B is correct because the subject "sketches" is plural, requiring the plural past-tense verb "were." The relative clause "which had been stored in the museum's archive for decades" does not change the subject.

     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice A is incorrect because "was" is the singular past-tense form and does not agree with the plural subject "sketches."
     * Choice C is incorrect because "has been" is singular present perfect, which neither agrees with the plural subject nor fits the past-tense context established by "last spring."
     * Choice D is incorrect because "is" is singular present tense, agreeing with neither the plural subject nor the past-tense context of the sentence.

     QUESTION 7
     Passage:
     By the time the rescue team arrived at the crash site, the survivors _______ shelter in an abandoned cabin nearby.

     Prompt:
     Which choice completes the text so that it conforms to the conventions of Standard Written English?

     Options:
     A) find
     B) found
     C) had found
     D) have found

     Correct Answer: C

     Correct Answer Explanation:
     * Choice C is correct because the sentence describes an action (finding shelter) that was completed before another past action (the rescue team arriving). The past perfect "had found" correctly expresses this earlier-past relationship.

     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice A is incorrect because "find" is present tense, which is inconsistent with the past-tense context established by "arrived."
     * Choice B is incorrect because "found" is simple past, which places finding shelter at the same time as the team's arrival — but the sentence's structure ("by the time... arrived") indicates the shelter was found before the arrival, requiring the past perfect.
     * Choice D is incorrect because "have found" is present perfect, which is inconsistent with the past-tense narrative context of the sentence.

     -----------------------------------------------------------------

     QUESTION 8
     Passage:
     The documentary features interviews with scientists _______ research has transformed our understanding of deep-sea ecosystems.

     Prompt:
     Which choice completes the text so that it conforms to the conventions of Standard Written English?

     Options:
     A) who's
     B) whose
     C) whom
     D) who

     Correct Answer: B

     Correct Answer Explanation:
     * Choice B is correct because "whose" is the possessive relative pronoun, referring to the scientists' research. The sentence requires a possessive form to modify "research" — "whose research has transformed" correctly attributes the research to the scientists.

     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice A is incorrect because "who's" is a contraction of "who is" or "who has," not a possessive pronoun — "who is research" is grammatically nonsensical.
     * Choice C is incorrect because "whom" is the objective case of the relative pronoun, used when the pronoun functions as an object. Here the pronoun needs to show possession, not serve as an object.
     * Choice D is incorrect because "who" is the subjective case and does not indicate possession — "who research has transformed" treats "research" as the subject of the relative clause rather than as something possessed by the scientists.

     -----------------------------------------------------------------

     QUESTION 9
     Passage:
     The new regulations require that every employee _______ a mandatory cybersecurity training course before accessing the company's internal network.

     Prompt:
     Which choice completes the text so that it conforms to the conventions of Standard Written English?

     Options:
     A) completes
     B) completed
     C) complete
     D) will complete

     Correct Answer: C

     Correct Answer Explanation:
     * Choice C is correct because "require that" triggers the subjunctive mood in English. After verbs of requirement, demand, or command followed by "that," the verb in the subordinate clause takes the base form (infinitive without "to"), regardless of the subject. "Complete" is the base form.

     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice A is incorrect because "completes" is the indicative third-person singular form, but the subjunctive mood is required after "require that" — the base form "complete" is needed, not the inflected indicative.
     * Choice B is incorrect because "completed" is past tense, which is inconsistent with the present/future context of the requirement and violates the subjunctive mood rule.
     * Choice D is incorrect because "will complete" is future indicative — after "require that," the subjunctive base form is used rather than any auxiliary construction.

     -----------------------------------------------------------------

     QUESTION 10
     Passage:
     The committee members argued heatedly among _______ before reaching a consensus.

     Prompt:
     Which choice completes the text so that it conforms to the conventions of Standard Written English?

     Options:
     A) them
     B) themselves
     C) itself
     D) one another

     Correct Answer: B

     Correct Answer Explanation:
     * Choice B is correct because "themselves" is the reflexive pronoun that corresponds to the plural subject "committee members." When the subject and object of an action refer to the same people — they argued with each other — the reflexive pronoun is required.

     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice A is incorrect because "them" is an object pronoun that would imply the committee members argued with a separate group of people, not with each other — the reflexive "themselves" is required when subject and object are the same.
     * Choice C is incorrect because "itself" is the singular reflexive pronoun for non-human subjects; "committee members" is plural and human, requiring "themselves."
     * Choice D is incorrect because "one another" is used to express reciprocal action between multiple parties ("they helped one another") but is not the standard choice after "among" — "among themselves" is the conventional phrase.

     [DIFFICULTY LEVEL: MEDIUM-LOW - QUESTIONS 11-20]

     QUESTION 11
     Passage:
     The board of directors, despite months of deliberation over the proposed merger, _______ yet to reach a final decision on whether to proceed.

     Prompt:
     Which choice completes the text so that it conforms to the conventions of Standard Written English?

     Options:
     A) are
     B) have been
     C) is
     D) were

     Correct Answer: C

     Correct Answer Explanation:
     * Choice C is correct because "board" is a collective noun that, in American English, is treated as singular when the group acts as a unit. The intervening phrase "despite months of deliberation over the proposed merger" does not change the subject. "Is" correctly agrees with the singular collective noun.

     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice A is incorrect because "are" treats "board" as plural, which is not standard in American English for collective nouns acting as a unified body.
     * Choice B is incorrect because "have been" is plural present perfect, which does not agree with the singular collective noun "board" in American English usage.
     * Choice D is incorrect because "were" is past tense and plural, inconsistent with both the singular subject and the present-tense context of the sentence.

     QUESTION 12
     Passage:
     The report concluded that neither the new software system nor the legacy platforms _______ capable of handling the projected increase in transaction volume.

     Prompt:
     Which choice completes the text so that it conforms to the conventions of Standard Written English?

     Options:
     A) was
     B) is
     C) were
     D) are

     Correct Answer: C

     Correct Answer Explanation:
     * Choice C is correct because in a "neither... nor..." construction, the verb agrees with the subject closest to it — the subject nearest the verb is "the legacy platforms," which is plural. Therefore, the plural past-tense verb "were" is correct (past tense because the report has already concluded).

     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice A is incorrect because "was" is singular, agreeing with the closer subject as it should — but "legacy platforms" is plural, not singular, so the plural form is required.
     * Choice B is incorrect because "is" is singular present tense, which neither agrees with the plural closer subject nor fits the past-tense context (the report "concluded").
     * Choice D is incorrect because while "are" is plural and would agree with "legacy platforms," it is present tense — inconsistent with the past-tense context established by "concluded."

     -----------------------------------------------------------------

     QUESTION 13
     Passage:
     The journalist spent three years investigating the scandal, _______ dozens of sources, reviewing thousands of documents, and ultimately publishing a series of articles that led to several resignations.

     Prompt:
     Which choice completes the text so that it conforms to the conventions of Standard Written English?

     Options:
     A) she interviewed
     B) to interview
     C) having interviewed
     D) interviewing

     Correct Answer: D

     Correct Answer Explanation:
     * Choice D is correct because the sentence uses a series of parallel participial phrases to describe what the journalist did during the three years: "interviewing dozens of sources, reviewing thousands of documents, and ultimately publishing a series of articles." All three items must be parallel in form — "-ing" participial phrases modifying the subject "journalist."

     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice A is incorrect because "she interviewed" introduces a new independent clause with its own subject, breaking the parallelism of the participial phrase series and creating a run-on sentence.
     * Choice B is incorrect because "to interview" is an infinitive, which does not parallel the "-ing" forms "reviewing" and "publishing" that follow in the series.
     * Choice C is incorrect because "having interviewed" uses the perfect participle, which implies the interviewing was completed before the reviewing and publishing — but the sentence presents all three activities as part of the same ongoing investigative process.

     -----------------------------------------------------------------

     QUESTION 14
     Passage:
     The study found that participants who exercised regularly not only reported lower levels of stress _______ also demonstrated measurably improved cognitive performance on standardized tests.

     Prompt:
     Which choice completes the text so that it conforms to the conventions of Standard Written English?

     Options:
     A) and
     B) yet
     C) but
     D) while

     Correct Answer: C

     Correct Answer Explanation:
     * Choice C is correct because the sentence uses the correlative conjunction pair "not only... but also." This pair requires "but" as the second element to complete the parallel structure. "Not only reported... but also demonstrated" is the grammatically correct and idiomatic construction.

     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice A is incorrect because "and" does not complete the "not only... but also" correlative pair — "not only... and also" is not a standard English construction.
     * Choice B is incorrect because "yet" is an adversative conjunction suggesting contrast, which does not fit the additive meaning of the "not only... but also" construction.
     * Choice D is incorrect because "while" introduces a simultaneous or contrasting clause, breaking the correlative pair structure the sentence has established with "not only."

     -----------------------------------------------------------------

     QUESTION 15
     Passage:
     The exhibition showcases paintings by artists from the early twentieth century, many of _______ were working in relative obscurity before being rediscovered by later generations of curators.

     Prompt:
     Which choice completes the text so that it conforms to the conventions of Standard Written English?

     Options:
     A) which
     B) who
     C) whom
     D) whose

     Correct Answer: C

     Correct Answer Explanation:
     * Choice C is correct because "whom" is the objective case of the relative pronoun referring to the human antecedent "artists." In the relative clause "many of _______ were working in obscurity," the pronoun follows the preposition "of" — prepositions require the objective case, making "whom" correct.

     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice A is incorrect because "which" refers to non-human antecedents; "artists" are people, so "whom" is required.
     * Choice B is incorrect because "who" is the subjective case — it cannot follow a preposition. "Many of who" is grammatically non-standard; the objective "whom" is required after "of."
     * Choice D is incorrect because "whose" is the possessive form — "many of whose" would imply possession, but the sentence is describing people who were working in obscurity, not something they possessed.

     QUESTION 16
     Passage:
     When the treaty was signed in 1648, it _______ a series of religious wars that had devastated much of central Europe for three decades.

     Prompt:
     Which choice completes the text so that it conforms to the conventions of Standard Written English?

     Options:
     A) ends
     B) had ended
     C) ended
     D) has ended

     Correct Answer: C

     Correct Answer Explanation:
     * Choice C is correct because the sentence describes two past events — the signing of the treaty and the ending of the wars — that occurred at the same time. Simple past tense "ended" correctly places the ending of the wars simultaneous with or immediately following the treaty signing.

     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice A is incorrect because "ends" is present tense, inconsistent with the past-tense historical context established by "was signed in 1648."
     * Choice B is incorrect because "had ended" (past perfect) would place the wars ending before the treaty was signed — but the treaty is what ended the wars, not something that followed an already-ended conflict.
     * Choice D is incorrect because "has ended" is present perfect, which implies a connection to the present — inappropriate for a specific completed historical event in 1648.

     QUESTION 17
     Passage:
     The foundation's mission is supporting emerging artists, funding community arts programs, and _______ access to arts education in underserved schools.

     Prompt:
     Which choice completes the text so that it conforms to the conventions of Standard Written English?

     Options:
     A) to expand
     B) the expansion of
     C) expanding
     D) it expands

     Correct Answer: C

     Correct Answer Explanation:
     * Choice C is correct because the sentence lists three parallel elements following "is": "supporting emerging artists," "funding community arts programs," and the third item must match this "-ing" gerund form. "Expanding access" maintains the parallel structure.

     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice A is incorrect because "to expand" is an infinitive, which does not parallel the gerund forms "supporting" and "funding" in the series.
     * Choice B is incorrect because "the expansion of" is a noun phrase, which breaks the parallelism — the other two items in the series are gerund phrases, not noun phrases.
     * Choice D is incorrect because "it expands" introduces a new clause with its own subject and verb, which destroys the parallel series structure and creates a grammatically incorrect construction after the list.

     QUESTION 18
     Passage:
     The historian argued that the document, _______ was widely believed to be authentic, had actually been forged sometime in the early nineteenth century.

     Prompt:
     Which choice completes the text so that it conforms to the conventions of Standard Written English?

     Options:
     A) that
     B) which
     C) who
     D) whom

     Correct Answer: B

     Correct Answer Explanation:
     * Choice B is correct because the relative clause ("was widely believed to be authentic") is nonrestrictive — it provides additional information about the document but is not essential to identifying it. Nonrestrictive relative clauses use "which" (set off by commas), not "that." The comma before the blank confirms the nonrestrictive usage.

     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice A is incorrect because "that" introduces restrictive relative clauses — those that are essential to identifying the noun. The commas surrounding this clause indicate it is nonrestrictive, requiring "which."
     * Choice C is incorrect because "who" refers to people or personified entities; "document" is an inanimate object, requiring "which."
     * Choice D is incorrect because "whom" is the objective case of the human relative pronoun — it refers to people and cannot refer to an inanimate "document."

     -----------------------------------------------------------------

     QUESTION 19
     Passage:
     The professor's lecture covered three interconnected themes: the rise of nationalism in the nineteenth century, the restructuring of colonial economies, and _______ of cultural identity under imperial rule.

     Prompt:
     Which choice completes the text so that it conforms to the conventions of Standard Written English?

     Options:
     A) the suppression
     B) suppressing
     C) how suppression occurred
     D) cultural identity was suppressed

     Correct Answer: A

     Correct Answer Explanation:
     * Choice A is correct because the list following the colon contains three parallel noun phrases: "the rise of nationalism," "the restructuring of colonial economies," and the third item must match this pattern. "The suppression of cultural identity under imperial rule" maintains the parallel noun-phrase structure throughout the series.

     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice B is incorrect because "suppressing" is a gerund phrase, which does not parallel the noun phrases "the rise of nationalism" and "the restructuring of colonial economies" used for the other two items in the series.
     * Choice C is incorrect because "how suppression occurred" is a noun clause, which is wordier and grammatically inconsistent with the concise noun phrases used for the other two list items.
     * Choice D is incorrect because "cultural identity was suppressed" is a full independent clause, which cannot function as a list item parallel to noun phrases in a colon-introduced series.

     QUESTION 20
     Passage:
     Despite her initial reluctance to take on the project, the architect _______ a design that won three national awards and was later featured in several major publications.

     Prompt:
     Which choice completes the text so that it conforms to the conventions of Standard Written English?

     Options:
     A) creates
     B) had created
     C) created
     D) would create

     Correct Answer: C

     Correct Answer Explanation:
     * Choice C is correct because the sentence describes a completed past action — the architect designed something that subsequently won awards and was featured in publications. Simple past "created" correctly places this action in the past as a single completed event.

     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice A is incorrect because "creates" is present tense, which is inconsistent with the past-tense context — the awards and publications are presented as already having occurred.
     * Choice B is incorrect because "had created" (past perfect) implies the design was completed before another past event, but no earlier past event is referenced in the sentence — simple past is sufficient.
     * Choice D is incorrect because "would create" indicates a conditional or habitual past action, neither of which fits the sentence's description of a specific, completed achievement.

     QUESTION 21
     Passage:
     The findings of the decade-long study, which tracked over five thousand participants across twelve countries, _______ that regular social connection significantly reduces the risk of cognitive decline in adults over sixty-five.

     Prompt:
     Which choice completes the text so that it conforms to the conventions of Standard Written English?

     Options:
     A) suggests
     B) suggest
     C) is suggesting
     D) has suggested

     Correct Answer: B

     Correct Answer Explanation:
     * Choice B is correct because the subject is "findings" — a plural noun. The lengthy relative clause "which tracked over five thousand participants across twelve countries" interrupts the subject and verb but does not change the subject. "Suggest" is the correct plural present-tense form.

     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice A is incorrect because "suggests" is the third-person singular form, which agrees with "study" — but "study" is the object of a preposition ("of the decade-long study"), not the subject. The true subject is "findings," which is plural.
     * Choice C is incorrect because "is suggesting" is singular progressive, which does not agree with the plural subject "findings" and adds unnecessary progressive aspect to a statement of established research findings.
     * Choice D is incorrect because "has suggested" is singular present perfect, which agrees with neither the plural subject "findings" nor the simple present tense appropriate for describing research conclusions.

     QUESTION 22
     Passage:
     The senator proposed three amendments to the bill: reducing the corporate tax rate by two percentage points, extending the small business exemption by three years, and _______ a new oversight committee to monitor compliance.

     Prompt:
     Which choice completes the text so that it conforms to the conventions of Standard Written English?

     Options:
     A) the establishment of
     B) to establish
     C) establishing
     D) she would establish

     Correct Answer: C

     Correct Answer Explanation:
     * Choice C is correct because the three amendments are listed as parallel gerund phrases: "reducing the corporate tax rate," "extending the small business exemption," and the third must match this "-ing" gerund form. "Establishing a new oversight committee" maintains the parallel structure.

     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice A is incorrect because "the establishment of" is a noun phrase, which breaks the parallelism — the other two items are gerund phrases, not noun phrases introduced by "the."
     * Choice B is incorrect because "to establish" is an infinitive, which does not parallel the gerund forms "reducing" and "extending" used earlier in the list.
     * Choice D is incorrect because "she would establish" introduces a new clause with its own subject and verb, destroying the parallel series structure and creating a grammatically incorrect list item.

     QUESTION 23
     Passage:
     The administration's decision to reclassify the wetlands as developable land has been criticized by environmental groups, several conservation scientists, and _______ who argues that the move violates federal protections established in 1972.

     Prompt:
     Which choice completes the text so that it conforms to the conventions of Standard Written English?

     Options:
     A) a legal scholar
     B) a legal scholar, one
     C) legal scholars
     D) one legal scholar

     Correct Answer: A

     Correct Answer Explanation:
     * Choice A is correct because the relative clause that follows ("who argues that the move violates federal protections") uses the singular verb "argues," indicating the antecedent must be a singular noun. "A legal scholar" is singular and consistent with the singular "argues" in the relative clause.

     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice B is incorrect because "a legal scholar, one" is redundant and grammatically awkward — the additional "one" is unnecessary and disrupts the list structure.
     * Choice C is incorrect because "legal scholars" is plural, which would require "who argue" rather than "who argues" in the relative clause — the singular verb "argues" signals a singular antecedent.
     * Choice D is incorrect because while "one legal scholar" is technically singular, "one" here functions as an indefinite pronoun that would require "argues" to agree — but the phrasing "one legal scholar who argues" is slightly redundant with "one" when "a legal scholar" is the more natural and conventional choice.

     Which choice completes the text so that it conforms to the conventions of Standard Written English?

     Options:
     A) are
     B) were
     C) is
     D) have been

     Correct Answer: C

     Correct Answer Explanation:
     * Choice C is correct because the subject is "chairperson" — a singular noun. The phrase "together with several senior advisors and the lead counsel" is a parenthetical addition, not part of a compound subject. The verb must agree with the singular "chairperson," so "is" is correct.

     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice A is incorrect because "are" treats the additional people named in the "together with" phrase as part of a compound subject, but "together with" does not create a compound subject in standard English — only "and" does.
     * Choice B is incorrect because "were" is past tense and plural, inconsistent with both the singular subject and the present-tense context of ongoing review.
     * Choice D is incorrect because "have been" is plural present perfect, which does not agree with the singular subject "chairperson."

     QUESTION 25

     Prompt:
     Which choice completes the text so that it conforms to the conventions of Standard Written English?

     Options:
     A) that
     B) whom
     C) which
     D) who

     Correct Answer: C

     Correct Answer Explanation:
     * Choice C is correct because "which" is the correct relative pronoun for a nonrestrictive clause modifying the inanimate noun "funds." The commas surrounding the clause ("which had been diverted through a series of shell companies") confirm it is nonrestrictive, requiring "which" rather than "that."

     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice A is incorrect because "that" introduces restrictive relative clauses, but the presence of commas indicates this clause is nonrestrictive — providing additional information rather than defining which funds are meant.
     * Choice B is incorrect because "whom" is the objective case of the human relative pronoun; "funds" is inanimate and cannot be referred to with a human pronoun.

     QUESTION 26
     Passage:
     The negotiations failed not because the parties disagreed on fundamentals _______ because neither side was willing to make the first concession on the procedural question of who would chair the talks.

     Prompt:
     Which choice completes the text so that it conforms to the conventions of Standard Written English?

     Options:
     A) and
     B) but
     C) or
     D) yet

     Correct Answer: B

     Correct Answer Explanation:
     * Choice B is correct because the sentence uses the correlative conjunction pair "not because X... but because Y." The "not because... but because" construction is the standard English form for contrasting two explanations, and "but" is the required second element of this pair.

     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice A is incorrect because "and" would create "not because X and because Y," implying both reasons apply simultaneously — but the sentence intends to replace the first explanation with the second.
     * Choice C is incorrect because "or" creates "not because X or because Y," which implies neither explanation applies — the opposite of what the sentence means.
     * Choice D is incorrect because "yet" is an adversative conjunction typically joining independent clauses, not completing a correlative "not because... because" construction.

     QUESTION 27
     Passage:
     Historians now believe that the letters attributed to the general _______ actually written by his chief of staff, who had a far more literary style than the general himself was known for.

     Prompt:
     Which choice completes the text so that it conforms to the conventions of Standard Written English?

     Options:
     A) was
     B) is
     C) were
     D) are

     Correct Answer: C

     Correct Answer Explanation:
     * Choice C is correct because the subject is "letters," a plural noun, and the tense is past — historians now believe something about letters that existed in the past. "Were" is the plural past-tense form that correctly agrees with "letters" and reflects the historical context.

     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice A is incorrect because "was" is singular past tense and does not agree with the plural subject "letters."
     * Choice B is incorrect because "is" is singular present tense, agreeing with neither the plural subject nor the past-tense context.
     * Choice D is incorrect because "are" is plural present tense — while it agrees with the plural "letters," the historical context requires the past tense "were," not the present.

     QUESTION 28
     Passage:
     The candidates' tax proposals differ significantly: the incumbent favors reducing rates for middle-income earners, while the challenger advocates _______ the rate for top earners and using the revenue to fund infrastructure.

     Prompt:
     Which choice completes the text so that it conforms to the conventions of Standard Written English?

     Options:
     A) to raise
     B) raised
     C) raising
     D) a raise of

     Correct Answer: C

     Correct Answer Explanation:
     * Choice C is correct because "advocates" takes a gerund (an "-ing" noun form) as its complement in standard English usage — one "advocates doing" something, not "advocates to do" something. "Raising the rate" is the grammatically correct object of "advocates."

     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice A is incorrect because "to raise" is an infinitive, but "advocate" is not followed by an infinitive in standard English — "advocates raising" is the correct construction.
     * Choice B is incorrect because "raised" is a past participle or past tense form that cannot function as the direct object of "advocates" in this construction.
     * Choice D is incorrect because "a raise of" is a noun phrase that awkwardly transforms the action into a nominalization, and "a raise of the rate" is not idiomatic in this context.

     QUESTION 29
     Passage:
     The delegation arrived at the summit having _______ for months — reviewing position papers, consulting stakeholders, and running simulations of the most likely negotiating scenarios.

     Prompt:
     Which choice completes the text so that it conforms to the conventions of Standard Written English?

     Options:
     A) prepared
     B) been preparing
     C) prepare
     D) to prepare

     Correct Answer: B

     Correct Answer Explanation:
     * Choice B is correct because "having been preparing" (perfect progressive participle) indicates an ongoing preparatory process completed just before the arrival at the summit. The "having" construction signals that the preparation occurred before the main action (arriving), and the progressive aspect captures that it was an extended, ongoing process — consistent with the list of activities that follows.

     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice A is incorrect because "having prepared" (perfect participle) treats the preparation as a single completed event rather than an extended process, which is less consistent with the list of ongoing activities (reviewing, consulting, running simulations) that follows.
     * Choice C is incorrect because "prepare" is the base form and cannot follow "having" grammatically — "having prepare" is not a standard construction.
     * Choice D is incorrect because "to prepare" is an infinitive and cannot follow "having" — "having to prepare" would mean being obligated to prepare, which changes the meaning entirely.

     -----------------------------------------------------------------

     QUESTION 30
     Passage:
     The editorial board's statement, drafted over the course of several contentious meetings and revised multiple times before publication, _______ a position that surprised both longtime supporters and critics of the paper alike.

     Prompt:
     Which choice completes the text so that it conforms to the conventions of Standard Written English?

     Options:
     A) stake out
     B) staked out
     C) staking out
     D) stakes out

     Correct Answer: B

     Correct Answer Explanation:
     * Choice B is correct because the subject "statement" is singular, and the verb must be in past tense — the statement was already drafted and published. "Staked out" is the singular past-tense form that correctly agrees with the subject and fits the past-tense context.

     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice A is incorrect because "stake out" is the base/plural present form, which does not agree with the singular subject and is inconsistent with the past-tense context.
     * Choice C is incorrect because "staking out" is a participial form that would leave the sentence without a main finite verb, creating a sentence fragment despite the long modifying phrase preceding it.
     * Choice D is incorrect because "stakes out" is the singular present tense form — while it agrees with the singular subject, the past-tense context (the statement was drafted and revised before publication) requires the past tense "staked out."

     -----------------------------------------------------------------
     [DIFFICULTY LEVEL: HIGH - QUESTIONS 31-40]

     QUESTION 31
     Passage:
     The team of engineers responsible for designing the filtration systems that supply clean water to more than forty rural communities _______ awarded a commendation by the regional environmental authority for their work.

     Prompt:
     Which choice completes the text so that it conforms to the conventions of Standard Written English?

     Options:
     A) were
     B) was
     C) are
     D) have been

     Correct Answer: B

     Correct Answer Explanation:
     * Choice B is correct because the grammatical subject is "team," a singular collective noun. The long modifying phrase that follows — "of engineers responsible for designing the filtration systems that supply clean water to more than forty rural communities" — intervenes between subject and verb but does not change the subject. "Was" correctly agrees with the singular "team" in past tense.

     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice A is incorrect because "were" is plural, agreeing with "engineers" or "communities" — but neither is the grammatical subject. The subject is "team," which is singular.
     * Choice C is incorrect because "are" is plural present tense, agreeing with neither the singular subject nor the past-tense context established by "awarded."
     * Choice D is incorrect because "have been" is plural present perfect, which does not agree with the singular collective noun "team."

     -----------------------------------------------------------------

     QUESTION 32
     Passage:
     The policy's critics — including several economists _______ work the administration had previously cited as supportive — argued that the new projections fundamentally undermined the rationale for the initiative.

     Prompt:
     Which choice completes the text so that it conforms to the conventions of Standard Written English?

     Options:
     A) who's
     B) whose
     C) whom
     D) which

     Correct Answer: B

     Correct Answer Explanation:
     * Choice B is correct because "whose" is the possessive relative pronoun referring to the economists' work. The relative clause "whose work the administration had previously cited as supportive" attributes the work to the economists — a possessive relationship requiring "whose."

     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice A is incorrect because "who's" is a contraction of "who is" or "who has," not a possessive — "who is work" is grammatically nonsensical.
     * Choice C is incorrect because "whom" is the objective case of the relative pronoun — it functions as an object, not as a possessive modifier. "Whom work" is not a standard possessive construction.
     * Choice D is incorrect because "which" refers to inanimate objects or non-human entities; "economists" are people, requiring the human relative pronoun "whose."

     -----------------------------------------------------------------

     QUESTION 33
     Passage:
     The novelist's prose style has evolved considerably since her debut: whereas her early work _______ fragmented sentences and a deliberately sparse vocabulary, her recent novels favor long, sinuous constructions that embed subordinate clauses within subordinate clauses.

     Prompt:
     Which choice completes the text so that it conforms to the conventions of Standard Written English?

     Options:
     A) relied on
     B) relies on
     C) had relied on
     D) was relying on

     Correct Answer: A

     Correct Answer Explanation:
     * Choice A is correct because the sentence contrasts the novelist's early work with her recent novels — the "whereas" clause describes the past style of early work, requiring simple past tense. "Relied on" is the correct simple past form, consistent with the contrast between a completed earlier style and her current approach.

     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice B is incorrect because "relies on" is present tense, which would imply her early work still uses this style — inconsistent with the contrast the sentence is drawing between past and present writing styles.
     * Choice C is incorrect because "had relied on" (past perfect) implies the early style ended before another past event, but no such earlier event is referenced — simple past suffices for comparing past and present styles.
     * Choice D is incorrect because "was relying on" (past progressive) implies an ongoing action in progress at a specific past time, which is unnecessarily complex and does not fit the general characterization of an early writing style.

     -----------------------------------------------------------------

     QUESTION 34
     Passage:
     Researchers studying the migration patterns of Arctic terns — birds that travel farther than any other animal on Earth — have found that each individual bird _______ essentially the same route year after year, deviating only when unusual weather conditions force a detour.

     Prompt:
     Which choice completes the text so that it conforms to the conventions of Standard Written English?

     Options:
     A) follow
     B) follows
     C) have followed
     D) are following

     Correct Answer: B

     Correct Answer Explanation:
     * Choice B is correct because the subject of the embedded clause is "each individual bird" — "each" takes a singular verb. Despite the lengthy parenthetical about Arctic terns intervening, the subject of the "have found that" clause is "each individual bird," which requires the singular present-tense "follows."

     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice A is incorrect because "follow" is the base/plural form, which does not agree with the singular subject "each individual bird."
     * Choice C is incorrect because "have followed" is plural present perfect, agreeing with neither the singular subject "each individual bird" nor the simple present tense used to describe an ongoing habitual behavior.
     * Choice D is incorrect because "are following" is plural progressive, which does not agree with the singular "each individual bird" and implies a specific ongoing action rather than a habitual pattern.

     -----------------------------------------------------------------

     QUESTION 35
     Passage:
     The commission's report on urban housing, which was completed after eighteen months of fieldwork and reviewed by an independent panel of experts before _______ released, identified several systemic failures in zoning enforcement that had allowed unsafe conditions to persist for years.

     Prompt:
     Which choice completes the text so that it conforms to the conventions of Standard Written English?

     Options:
     A) it was
     B) being
     C) it being
     D) having been

     Correct Answer: B

     Correct Answer Explanation:
     * Choice B is correct because the sentence uses a parallel passive construction: "completed after eighteen months... and reviewed by an independent panel... before being released." The word "before" here introduces a gerund phrase, and "being released" is the correct gerund form of the passive to parallel the preceding participial phrases in the relative clause.

     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice A is incorrect because "before it was released" would introduce a full subordinate clause, which is grammatically possible but creates a shift in construction — the relative clause has used participial phrases ("completed," "reviewed"), so maintaining the participial/gerund form with "being released" is more consistent.
     * Choice C is incorrect because "it being" is a gerund with an explicit subject, which is awkward and non-standard in this context — the implicit subject of the gerund is already clear from the main clause.
     * Choice D is incorrect because "having been released" (perfect gerund) implies the report was released before being reviewed — the opposite of the intended sequence; the sentence says it was reviewed before release.

     -----------------------------------------------------------------

     QUESTION 36
     Passage:
     The three criteria the selection committee uses to evaluate candidates are academic achievement, demonstrated leadership in extracurricular activities, and _______ to the institution's mission as expressed in the personal statement.

     Prompt:
     Which choice completes the text so that it conforms to the conventions of Standard Written English?

     Options:
     A) how committed they are
     B) their commitment
     C) a commitment that exists
     D) being committed

     Correct Answer: B

     Correct Answer Explanation:
     * Choice B is correct because the three criteria are listed as parallel noun phrases: "academic achievement," "demonstrated leadership in extracurricular activities," and the third must match this pattern. "Their commitment to the institution's mission" is a noun phrase that parallels the preceding items.

     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice A is incorrect because "how committed they are" is a noun clause, which breaks the parallel structure — the other two items are noun phrases, not subordinate clauses.
     * Choice C is incorrect because "a commitment that exists" adds the unnecessary relative clause "that exists," creating an awkward and verbose construction that does not parallel the concise noun phrases used for the other criteria.
     * Choice D is incorrect because "being committed" is a gerund phrase, which does not parallel the noun phrases "academic achievement" and "demonstrated leadership" used for the first two criteria.

     -----------------------------------------------------------------

     QUESTION 37
     Passage:
     The manuscript, which scholars had long assumed _______ lost during the fire that destroyed the monastery's library in 1742, was discovered last year in a private collection in Vienna.

     Prompt:
     Which choice completes the text so that it conforms to the conventions of Standard Written English?

     Options:
     A) to have been
     B) had been
     C) was
     D) to be

     Correct Answer: A

     Correct Answer Explanation:
     * Choice A is correct because "assume" in this context takes an infinitive complement — scholars "assumed [the manuscript] to have been lost." The perfect infinitive "to have been" correctly places the assumed loss before the time of the assuming, and the passive "to have been lost" correctly describes the manuscript's status. This is the standard construction after verbs of mental assumption with a past-referring infinitive.

     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice B is incorrect because "had been" would make the clause "which scholars had long assumed had been lost" — the double "had" creates an awkward construction and the grammar of "assumed" with a "that" clause (implicit here) is less standard than the infinitive construction.
     * Choice C is incorrect because "was" creates "scholars had long assumed was lost," which omits the necessary complementizer and uses simple past rather than the past-referring perfect infinitive needed to place the loss in the past relative to the assuming.
     * Choice D is incorrect because "to be" is the present infinitive, implying scholars assume the manuscript is currently lost — but the sentence reveals it was discovered, meaning the assumption was about a past state, requiring the perfect infinitive "to have been."

     -----------------------------------------------------------------

     QUESTION 38
     Passage:
     Neither the lead attorney nor the junior associates _______ aware of the precedent that the opposing counsel was likely to invoke, a gap in preparation that would prove costly during oral arguments.

     Prompt:
     Which choice completes the text so that it conforms to the conventions of Standard Written English?

     Options:
     A) was
     B) is
     C) were
     D) are

     Correct Answer: C

     Correct Answer Explanation:
     * Choice C is correct because in a "neither... nor..." construction, the verb agrees with the subject closest to it — the subject nearest the verb is "the junior associates," which is plural. Additionally, the past tense is required because the sentence describes a preparation gap that "would prove costly" — past conditional confirming a past context. "Were" is the correct plural past-tense form.

     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice A is incorrect because "was" is singular and would agree with "the lead attorney," but in "neither... nor..." constructions the verb agrees with the closer subject, "the junior associates," which is plural.
     * Choice B is incorrect because "is" is singular present tense, agreeing with neither the plural closer subject nor the past-tense context.
     * Choice D is incorrect because "are" is plural present tense — while it agrees with the plural closer subject, the past-tense context (established by "would prove costly") requires the past form "were."

     -----------------------------------------------------------------

     QUESTION 39
     Passage:
     The task force recommended that the agency _______ its review process, establish clearer criteria for approval, and publish its decisions with detailed explanations within thirty days of each ruling.

     Prompt:
     Which choice completes the text so that it conforms to the conventions of Standard Written English?

     Options:
     A) streamlines
     B) streamlined
     C) streamline
     D) should streamline

     Correct Answer: C

     Correct Answer Explanation:
     * Choice C is correct because "recommend that" triggers the subjunctive mood in English. After verbs of recommendation, suggestion, or demand followed by "that," the verb in the subordinate clause must take the base form (the infinitive without "to") regardless of the subject. "Streamline" is the base form, and it is parallel with the other verbs in the list ("establish" and "publish"), which are also base forms.

     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice A is incorrect because "streamlines" is the third-person singular indicative form — the subjunctive requires the base form "streamline," not the inflected indicative.
     * Choice B is incorrect because "streamlined" is past tense, inconsistent with the subjunctive construction and the present/future-oriented nature of the recommendation.
     * Choice D is incorrect because "should streamline" introduces a modal auxiliary — while semantically similar, the standard English construction after "recommend that" uses the base subjunctive form without a modal, making "streamline" the correct and more formal choice.

     -----------------------------------------------------------------

     QUESTION 40
     Passage:
     The research team, whose members included specialists in virology, epidemiology, and computational modeling, _______ a framework that could be adapted for tracking the spread of pathogens across international borders.

     Prompt:
     Which choice completes the text so that it conforms to the conventions of Standard Written English?

     Options:
     A) develop
     B) developing
     C) developed
     D) have developed

     Correct Answer: C

     Correct Answer Explanation:
     * Choice C is correct because the subject "team" is a singular collective noun, and the sentence describes a completed past action. "Developed" is the singular past-tense form that correctly agrees with "team" and reflects the completion of the framework's creation.

     False Answer Explanations:
     * Choice A is incorrect because "develop" is the base/plural present form, which does not agree with the singular subject and is inconsistent with the past-tense context.
     * Choice B is incorrect because "developing" is a participial form that would leave the sentence without a main finite verb — the long "whose members included..." clause does not supply a main verb for the sentence's subject.
     * Choice D is incorrect because "have developed" is plural present perfect, which does not agree with the singular collective noun "team" in standard American English usage.
